<snip>

#1 - Generally this is true.  However, there are certain
programming problems where the OF/IN are perfectly acceptable and
preferred.

#2 - I'm not sure I understood all of that.  However, this is
what I think I got from this:  That one has to read the whole
spec in order to understand it.  Therefore, to use an example,
one must understand the function fully in order to understand why
account-master-key is being used in two different records.

#3 - Code indentation makes the code readable or unreadable.  Too
little or too much are both problems.  If I were to move zero to
seven different locations, I tend to write such a move as
follows:

    MOVE ZERO       TO  ABC-WIDGET-COUNT
                        ABC-ORDER-AMOUNT
                        XYZ-BACK-ORDER-AMOUNT
                        .
                        .
                        000-INVOICE-PAGE.

This allows one to easily insert/remove/modify a line without
affecting everything else, and, makes it quite plain what is
getting "zeroed out".  If I understood the rule you have here,
this type of indentation could only be done with a logic control
statement (IF, EVALUATE, etc.).

#4 - This is why I love my 3270 emulator and MOD4 operations
(80x43) for source and MOD5 (132x27) for reports, dumps and the
like.  But more to the point, the old argument that a function
should be contained on a page does not work when everything is
screen oriented.  When we printed everything, you got about 50-80
lines on a page (6/8 LPI).  How do you only display a single
function on a screen?  This almost reminds of a project I did
with NASA where each subroutine had to fit entirely on one
printed page.  All of the data areas and comments/doc for the
routine could take up several pages, but the logic had to fit on
one page.  Worked quite well until you had some character
intensive code to paint a screen, and there was no logical break
to it for 130+ lines!

#5 - The ISPF editor is much more powerful than this.  Example:
X ALL;F 'OF' WORD 20 60 all;X "*" 7 ALL;F ABC-WIDGET-ACC PRE ALL

Translates to:  Hide all lines.  Then Find all occurrences of the
word OF between columns 20 & 60 (inclusive).  Then, any line
containing "*" in column 7 is to be hidden.  Then Find anything
that begins with the character string abc-widget-acc.

Using this type of command string allows one to find all
occurrences of the subordinate definitions.  The programmer can
then selectively show, find, or hide anything else not needed.

#6 - 

#7 -


I want to make an observation or two.  If I am going to allow
someone to change a record from a VSAM file (for instance), and,
the change they are doing will change the key of the record, then
I would want two work areas having the same definitions.  This
would allow me to make all the changes and then do the write to
the VSAM file and still be able to reverse the whole process
should something fail before I can get the DELETE done.

What if I am having to populate two physical files that have the
exact same data layouts, but, the only difference is, one
contains OLD records (say paid invoices) and the other contains
NEW records.  They are the same file layouts, same data, except
that physically, the data is different.

To me, these are the main reasons for being able to have the
"dual definitions" where you need the OF or IN to distinguish
(and make unique).
```

#### ↳ Re: Guidelines, Programming Style

- **From:** "William M. Klein" <wmklein@ix.netcom.com>
- **Date:** 2000-12-11T15:28:38-06:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<913gsq$f39$1@slb0.atl.mindspring.net>`
- **References:** `<912p2s$3q3$1@solti3.sdm.de>`

```
The major (and in my opinion only "common") reason for allowing qualified
data-names is for the case that there is an "application need" to use
multiple records with the same layout in multiple separate programs and/or
places within the same program.

It is (IMHO) important to "maintenance" of an entire application that there
be a "single record layout" for use in all programs and all sections and
places within each program.  Furthermore, the "maintenance" of this record
layout should (again IMHO) be the responsibility of a single "group"
(possibly with a "data-dictionary" or similar "repository").  This record
layout should be available to all programs and applications via a common
copylib member.  ("COPYLIB" is an IBM mainframe term - but from the
reference to "ISPF" in the original note, I *assume* you are in an IBM
mainframe environment.)

If there is a single copy member that describes the "record description"
(including any REDEFINES) then it may be maintained in a "single place" and
all applications will AUTOMATICALLY will get any/all changes to the record's
description.

It is possible that if all applications in all places ONLY reference a
record description once, then you don't need qualification.  However, if
even one of your programs require any of the following this doesn't work:
 - The same record is referenced in multiple sections (e.g. Linkage and
File)
 - There are multiple files with the same layout (e.g. input and output - or
master and transaction)
 - There are application needs to maintain copies of records for
simultaneous processing (e.g. "save" record and "current" record)

Once you accept that there are ANY reasons to have multiple copies of the
same record layout in the same program, there are two possible "solutions"
to this.  (The following assumes an '85 Standard compiler)

 1) A single copymember that uses a "tricky" prefix method - that will be
modified by ALL programs via COPY/REPLACING, e.g
   01 :TAG:-File.
      05  :TAG:-Elem1   Pic X.

2) A single copymember that does NOT include an 01-level and is always
copied in under an 01-level name and is referenced via qualification.

   ***

There are proponents (and opponents) of both of these methods.  Either one
is "easy to maintain" in shops that use it "exclusively" and both are hard
to maintain in cases where some/many programmers are not used to them  The
first method *requires* that every COPY of the record description use
COPY/REPLACING (the copymember is not valid COBOL source code). The second
method leads to (slightly) longer source statements (but also allows for
CORRESPONDING option for some statements - which is again good or bad
depending on how it is used).

Note: The one method that I personally find "bad" is where a shop stores
MULTIPLE copies of the same record layout (one for Linkage Section, one for
file section, one for input files, one for output, etc).  I know of shops
where this is "common" - but I find that it is the most error-prone (people
forget to keep all the copies "in sync").

Note2:  This entire thread relates to a shop where there are multiple
(many?) programmers and possibly programming groups.  As some readers of
comp.lang.cobol are in single (or small) programming environments, this is
really totally a matter of "personal preference".  Whatever technique a
single programmer is used to and expects in his/her own code is the "best"
method as long as they use their own consistent style.

Note3: The current ('85) Standard does not allow VALUE clauses in Linkage
section.  This *could* lead to a problem with using a single copylib member
for all references to a record layout.  HOWEVER, IBM (the environment of
this thread) does allow it already (and, furthermore, the next Standard will
allow this specifically so that programmers MAY have common copymember in
all sections).
```

SNIP

OK so I'm only an amateur, but I have a programme with a certain 
amount of duplication which is done to enable records to be 
recreated in the event of damage.

As a result I have deliberately used the amse variable names 
to enable use of the MOVE CORRESPONDING clause. This makes 
my code infintely more readable.

Personally, I suggest anyone who can't instantly understand 
DATE of THIS-TRANSACTION as opposed to DATE of LAST-TRANSACTION 
should give up reading comics and go back to studying English (or
American) at school I find this much more readable than adding 
short suffixes or prefixes, and this is one of the aims of CoBOL!

The use of suffixes requires one to have an overall understanding 
of the programme first. Its ok for the current programmers, but 
isn't necessarily instantly obvious to the newcomer.

That said, I can see that use of such extensions can be very useful.

What isn't useful is to introduce a new code rule half-way through 
a project. This is called "amending the terms of reference" and your 
reply will be, OK, we can accommodate that, but at an extra cost of
$$$$$ and a delay of x days/weeks.  Who knows, maybe they'll say yes, 
and thus give you the extra work! No doubt your boss will love you 
for it.

We once had a client joiner who always underquoted on Govenment projects, 
knowing he'd make a loss. When they came back with any amendment to the 
specifications (as he knew they would) he'd sting them for the money 
on the variation, so making it up to a healthy profit.

Government never did learn.

stringer@es.co.nz

##### ↳ ↳ Re: Guidelines, Programming Style

- **From:** Calvin Crumrine <Calvin_Crumrine@dced.state.ak.us>

stringer wrote:

>
…[34 more quoted lines elided]…
> stringer@es.co.nz

I think the original poster posited a situation wherein you referenced two
account numbers in the same program, not the same account number twice.
Qualification was required because the account numbers came from different
files originally developed for different purposes in different programs,
neither of which took into account the existence of the other so they both,
logically, called their fields 'ACCOUNT-NBR'.

The only way I can think of to avoid qualification due to these unforeseen
circumstances is to use a prefix/suffix naming convention. Situations wherein
you reference the same data twice in the same program cannot be handled thusly
with any guarantee of maintainability.
```

#### ↳ Re: Guidelines, Programming Style

- **From:** "John C. Smith" <noname@nowhere.net>

I've been coding in COBOL for 16 years, and I've coded both ways outlined
below, and I personally don't prefer one over the other, nor have I seen an
advantage as far as maintenance is concerned either way.  I will say that
one can easily go too far in naming fields within working-storage.   I
detest overly-long variable names.  What DOES make a difference when it
comes to future maintenance is well- thought-out, efficient, structured
code.

You are going in the right direction in developing coding standards.
Standards are a good thing if they are practical and relevant.

Regards,
J. Richard L.

#### ↳ Re: Guidelines, Programming Style

- **From:** "Judson McClendon" <judmc@bellsouth.net>
- **Date:** 2000-12-14T09:41:13-06:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<oS5_5.2734$QY4.91115@news2.atl>`
- **References:** `<912p2s$3q3$1@solti3.sdm.de>`

```
"Achim Schupeta" <schupeta@canach.muc.sdm.de> wrote:
> [snip]

I agree with your client.  Besides, the client is always right.  I
see qualification as a complete waste of typing time and code space
which merely obfuscates the code.  Only in rare situations have I
seen it to be beneficial.  Of course, people can get used to, and
then begin to justify, just about anything. :-)

Each data name in a given system should be spelled identically every
time it is used, except for a prefix (*NOT* suffix!), which is unique
to each 01 record in which it appears.  I find that 3 to 5 character
prefixes are generally best.  Two character prefixes are enough to be
unique, but usually not enough to be mnemonic, which is important for
clarity.  Making an acronym prefix from the 01 record name is often
convenient (e.g. 01 Date-Work-Area -> DWA-xxx).

Every abbreviated word should be abbreviated exactly the same in every
use of the word in data and procedure names, throughout a system.  It
is usually necessary to keep an abbreviations dictionary, with one
person responsible for maintaining it.  For example, having 'NUMBER'
abbreviated 'NO', 'NR', 'NBR', etc. in various places is nothing but
confusion.

One of the primary signs of excellence is consistency, consistency,
consistency.  Most programmers think they produce 'good code'.  You
have to know what their associates and clients think to tell the real
pros from the heard.  If you're really good, other programmers like
to maintain your code, and will often tell you so, especially when
they work on one of your programs after spending weeks modifying
someone else's crummy code. :-)
```

##### ↳ ↳ Re: Guidelines, Programming Style

    It always seemed to me that the best reason to use
qualification
was to allow the use of move corresponding.  And the
best reason to use move corresponding would be 2 (or more)
record defintions that are ALMOST identical, but not quite.

    If the records, or record fragments are exactly identical,
why not
use a group move.  A good example would be 2 records full of
numbers,
one with comp fields, one with useage display.  A move corr would
be very nice in this case.

###### ↳ ↳ ↳ Re: MOVE CORRESPONDING

_(thread depth: 4)_

- **From:** "William M. Klein" <wmklein@ix.netcom.com>
- **Date:** 2000-12-18T06:04:12-06:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<91kud9$pci$1@slb7.atl.mindspring.net>`
- **References:** `<912p2s$3q3$1@solti3.sdm.de> <oS5_5.2734$QY4.91115@news2.atl> <3a3d653e.1722278@news1.attglobal.net> <Gth%5.12504$wX2.220110@typhoon.austin.rr.com>`

```
The "usual" problems (that I know of are)

1) The two records do NOT use the same COPY member because the Picture/Usage
are different - so the names get out of sync, (e.g.  someone changes a field
called ADDR to Address1)

2) The two records do NOT use the same COPY member - and someone adds a new
level in the middle of one of the records, e.g changes

  01 A.
      05 B Pic X.
    to
  01 A.
    03 C.
      05 B Pic X.
```

###### ↳ ↳ ↳ Re: MOVE CORRESPONDING

_(thread depth: 4)_

- **From:** "Judson McClendon" <judmc@bellsouth.net>
- **Date:** 2000-12-19T09:14:02-06:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<VWK%5.2108$xU2.144479@news1.atl>`
- **References:** `<912p2s$3q3$1@solti3.sdm.de> <oS5_5.2734$QY4.91115@news2.atl> <3a3d653e.1722278@news1.attglobal.net> <Gth%5.12504$wX2.220110@typhoon.austin.rr.com>`

```
The major problem is that CORRESPONDING is like a time bomb, waiting
for some careless or inattentive maintenance programmer to modify
one of the structures a bit for some reason, changing the fields
that are corresponding.  Remember that each CORRESPONDING field
much match in every detail, name and qualifiers, up to but not
including the group data name used in the  CORRESPONDING statement
itself.  Also, no field under a REDEFINES below the primary group
identifier will be considered corresponding.  This problem is much
compounded by the fact that the compiler usually doesn't tell you
which fields are being referenced.  In my experience, unless all
the maintenance programmers are extraordinarily careful (doubtful
at best), CORRESPONDING is almost as dangerous as ALTER.  When you
consider how easy it is to construct the explicit statements with
modern text editors using block copy, I see no reason whatsoever to
use CORRESPONDING.  No one could argue that CORRESPONDING adds to
clarity, for only a detailed inspection of both structures reveals
which fields will be affected.  At best it is a shortcut that can
easily return to bite you when least expected.  Clarity us more
important than brevity.  Otherwise, why not always use the shortest
data and paragraph names we can think of? ;-)

The only place I can imagine CORRESPONDING being appropriate is in
a one-time program.  Even there, I would rather use explicit
statements and be *certain*. :-)
```

IMHO, there's not too much risk if you're using COPYBOOKS that are pretty
straightforward - e.g., 

01 INREC.
     copy rec.

01 OUTREC.
     copy rec.

MOVE CORRESPONDING INREC TO OUTREC.

This is pretty useful for file expansions, conversions, merges, etc.

The concept is pretty similar to the SQL construct SELECT table.*, whose
usefulness would not be disputed by anyone, except perhaps by DBAs and Data
Modelers perhaps, but then they don't have to do any REAL work anyway, do they?

If you have to maintain that program and you see the MOVE CORRESPONDING, you
can't see what is moving and what is not. You'll have to lookup both records
and check field for field to know if they are moved or not. The first thing I
do when I have to change a program like this is expand the statement.

###### ↳ ↳ ↳ Re: Guidelines, Programming Style

- **From:** luke <luke_bryan@my-deja.com>
- **Date:** 2000-12-18T15:10:25+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<91l9cr$nrh$1@nnrp1.deja.com>`
- **References:** `<912p2s$3q3$1@solti3.sdm.de> <oS5_5.2734$QY4.91115@news2.atl> <3a3d653e.1722278@news1.attglobal.net>`

```
I agree.  I can also add another use of MOVE CORRESPONDING.
Suppose you have an input file that has up to 500 different record
layouts.  And suppose the customer enters the records they want using a
text editor.  The record type is the first 3 characters of the record.
Each record has from one up to 45 parameters the customer may enter.
Each parameter is separated by a single space.  Parameters vary in size.

With all of that said, now you can easily see that all of the
parameters do not fall outside of their "boxes".  In other words, the
spaces between them are indeed all spaces.

At the beginning of each record's routine you simply put

MOVE CORRESPONDING RECORD-IS-TYPE-ABC TO WS-WHITE-SPACE.

Here is what WS-WHITE-SPACE looks like:

01  WS-WHITE-SPACE.
    02 WS-WHITE-SPACE-1             PIC X(01).
    02 WS-WHITE-SPACE-2             PIC X(01).
       <snip>
    02 WS-WHITE-SPACE-46            PIC X(01).

The RECORD-IS-TYPE-... records all have WS-WHITE-SPACE-1, WS-WHITE-
SPACE-2, etc. defined as the one byte spaces between the
parameters.

Thus you can check for spaces between the parameters with just two
sentences.

MOVE CORRESPONDING RECORD-IS-TYPE-ABC TO WS-WHITE-SPACE.
IF WS-WHITE-SPACE IS NOT EQUAL TO SPACE
    234-REPORT-USER-ERROR THRU 234-EXIT
END-IF.

Life is grand in COBOL.


In article <3a3d653e.1722278@news1.attglobal.net>,
  thaneH@softwaresimple.com (Thane Hubbell) wrote:
> I used to be of the same opinion re: Qualification.  However, having
> made great use of MOVE ... CORRESPONDING... ADD ... CORRESPONDING and
…[24 more quoted lines elided]…
> >Every abbreviated word should be abbreviated exactly the same in
every
> >use of the word in data and procedure names, throughout a system.  It
> >is usually necessary to keep an abbreviations dictionary, with one
…[22 more quoted lines elided]…
>


Sent via Deja.com
http://www.deja.com/
```

#### ↳ Re: Guidelines, Programming Style

- **From:** rjones1005@aol.com (RJones1005)
- **Date:** 2000-12-15T05:15:15+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<20001215001515.26557.00004816@ng-fu1.aol.com>`
- **References:** `<912p2s$3q3$1@solti3.sdm.de>`

```
> There are some general
>rules like inserting useful comments as well as specific
>rules like the obligation to have an 'WHEN OTHERS'-clause
>at the end of each EVALUATE.

WHEN OTHERS has saved me dozens of debug hours, even, and especially, on a few
EVALAUTES where I said "this path will never be taken".  Thank goodness I
didn't listen to myself!

>Names of variables has to be unique such that there is no
>necessity to use COBOLs qualification construct OF (or IN).
…[4 more quoted lines elided]…
>'ACCOUNT-NR-STH' and 'ACCOUNT-NR-ATH'.

You mention impact of code already written using qualifiers.  I can see
*extensive* coding to get rid of them in existing code - not to mention the
*extensive* regression testing needed.  I say if it works, don't fix it.  But
you can start from this point and inforce the rule.  In our shop we use
prefixes.  So if I'm reading a particular FD from disk and storing it to a
table in memory, I use exactly the same file definition, but REPLACE the prefix
- eliminating the need for qualification and it actually makes a nice
association in my mind between the file and table and screen variable; same
'core' name w/ yet a different prefixs ("I'm moving it from the table to the
screen now...).  Makes code *easier* to follow not harder.

This new rule should not be an absolute, but when a programmer uses it, (s)he
better be able to back it up w/ solid reasoning.  That's what code reviews are
for (in part).

[using qualifiers is bad because] 
>4.) Because of several many-line-statements there will be 
>less code per terminal-screen.

Never sacrifice readablity/comprehensibility for brevity.  You gotta maintain
this stuff!  Judge on a case-by-case basis. Besides that, unless you are using
a 24 line x 80 character DOS type editor, this is a non-issue.  Besides, what
modern compiler doesn't allow you to ignore the area A, area B, col 72
nonsense?



Better plan on teaching techniques for avoiding the need for qualification. 
Getting halfway through coding then realizing you need to do something to avoid
qualifing will cause development schedule delays - and I don't mean an hour.


>7.) The debugger used in our environment (INTERTEST) is
>unable to distinguish variables with same basename in
>different structures from the code.

Get another tool.
```

##### ↳ ↳ Re: Guidelines, Programming Style

- **From:** "William M. Klein" <wmklein@ix.netcom.com>
- **Date:** 2000-12-15T15:00:41-06:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<91e0lh$lhr$1@slb6.atl.mindspring.net>`
- **References:** `<912p2s$3q3$1@solti3.sdm.de> <20001215001515.26557.00004816@ng-fu1.aol.com>`

```
"RJones1005" <rjones1005@aol.com>
>
> Never sacrifice readablity/comprehensibility for brevity.  You gotta
maintain
> this stuff!  Judge on a case-by-case basis. Besides that, unless you are
using
> a 24 line x 80 character DOS type editor, this is a non-issue.  Besides,
what
> modern compiler doesn't allow you to ignore the area A, area B, col 72
> nonsense?
>

Boy - is this a "limited" world view!  (and totally ignores that the
original post was pretty clearly talking about an IBM mainframe development
environment.) I'll bet that you don't EVER work with non-PC compilers.
Almost *all* mainframe compilers still have A-/B-margin rules and most still
have an R-margin rule. How do you handle continued alphanumeric literals
(with embedded spaces) is you don't have an R-margin (col 72 or 80 or
something similar) rules.  This is "fixed" in the next COBOL Standard, but
by adding a new continuation format that I don't think many vendors support
yet.

Furthermore, *every* ANSI/ISO conforming compiler *must* still detect
violations of these rules when you turn on "standard conformance" checking -
which is usually "advisable" when you are developing programs that might
(eventually) need to be compiled by multiple compilers.
```

In other words, you know better that the customer does what they want.
That is an excellent way to turn a large prosperous enterprise into a
small, failing one.  Steve Jobs took the same line around late 1979.

anyhow.  At least, not for long.  If a contractor did that to me, they
would face me in court.  Anyway, if your reputation is as good as you
say it is, the customer won't try to tell you how to do your job.

###### ↳ ↳ ↳ Re: Guidelines, Programming Style

_(thread depth: 4)_

- **From:** "Judson McClendon" <judmc@bellsouth.net>
- **Date:** 2000-12-20T16:54:56-06:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<1Na06.2940$xU2.203262@news1.atl>`
- **References:** `<912p2s$3q3$1@solti3.sdm.de> <91d0fo$dq1$1@solti3.sdm.de> <n8L%5.2110$xU2.144318@news1.atl> <91pffh$3gk$1@sshuraab-i-1.production.compuserve.com>`

```
Yes, but the appropriate response is to reply to the client *in
writing* with the cons (and pros, if any) of the request, along
with an estimated cost to make the requested changes.  Then let
the client decide if it's worth it.  If you are strongly against
the client's request, require them to put the request in writing
before proceeding.  If anyone ever complains about the code, you
have the written request and your written objections.  If you
feel the request makes the code so bad you don't want your
company associated with it, explain that you will be happy to
complete the project as originally specified, or you will assist
(at fee) to transfer the project to someone willing to code it
their way.

Don't ever hold the client over a barrel, or stand in the way of
them doing what they want to do, other than something illegal or
unethical.  Just turn it around and think how you would feel if
you were the client and paying for the project out of your own
pocket.  If you treat clients as you would want to be treated,
you will always prosper in the long run.
```

One thing which has changed over the years is how easy it is to type more
words.  In the teletype days, being terse was important.  Now we can go
into working storage, cut a column of data names, go into the procedure
division, copy that column twice, do some manipulating and have the
individual code typed correctly and completely.  Replace that move
corresponding with a perform if desired.

I use ADD ... Corresponding and MOVE ... Corresponding for control
breaks where report writer is unavailable.  The nice thing is that you
can add a field in the data division without modifying the procedure
division.  Using the method described below one must remember to go
change every add/move section in the program -- using corresponding
it's all "automatic".  I still see great utility for this construct.

<a id="t-396a92c37f"></a>
## Thread: And yet another text on quantum comptation ... — 1 msgs

### And yet another text on quantum comptation ...

- **From:** Herwig Huener & Josella Simone Playton <webmaster@Josella-Simone-Playton.de>
- **Date:** 2000-12-11T21:55:12+01:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol,ger.ct
- **Message-ID:** `<3A353F30.96DF737E@Josella-Simone-Playton.de>`

```
2000-12-11 22:00:00 MEZ

And yet another text on quantum comptation which I may
recommend:

http://www.sees.bangor.ac.uk/~schmuel/comp/comp.html

This one shows nicely how reversible computing and quantum
computing fits together. No programmer is required to think
about the management of destroying information - a
compiler can do that easily. Just as I guessed. That
way, we can keep reversible computation / quantum
computation out of any language at the language-specific
level.

(No USAGE QBOOL in the next COBOL-Standard necessary -
although the text gives hints about a dedicated
programming language for a quantum computer.)

What this text does not show is how quantum computation
fits into the many worlds interpretation - no idea
why this facet of the subject is omitted. The
many-dimensional Hilbert-Space is not quite as good
for imagination.

If you feel intimidated by the notation of quantum
mechanics, just read over it and keep to the easy parts.
So did I.

Herwig
```

#### ↳ Re: Socket and cobol

- **From:** "William M. Klein" <wmklein@ix.netcom.com>
- **Date:** 2000-12-12T13:17:43-06:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<915tg6$3fj$1@slb6.atl.mindspring.net>`
- **References:** `<oomZ5.1853$Kw2.72544@twister2.tin.it>`

```
From one of my "usually reliable sources",

"Since he apparently are working in dos and unix only, I really have no
other suggestion than that he either link in the C library functions
directly or creates a wrapper API that he links with. He would then have to
provide the HTTP functionality himself which will be quite a challenge,
unless there are thirdparty libraries available, which I am pretty sure
there are. Definitely for Unix. If he had been developing for Windows, the
answer is surprisingly easy, if he wants to rely on Internet Explorer.
Because Internet Explorer comes with a high end HTTP api, which should serve
his needs well. The API he should look for is WinInet, if he goes to the web
he will find all he needs here:

        http://msdn.microsoft.com/workshop/networking/wininet/wininet.asp

As he will notice, this does not only apply to HTTP, but also FTP and
Gopher.
Problem is of course if he must be on Unix and Dos, in that case I regret to
say that I have no exact answers other than the proposal above."
```

<a id="t-cbcf2d9b00"></a>
## Thread: Internationalization in COBOL — 2 msgs

### Internationalization in COBOL

- **From:** "Rover" <Rover@pobox.com>
- **Date:** 2000-12-12T22:03:18+10:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<915422$e0j$1@bunyip.cc.uq.edu.au>`

```
Hi,

Does someone have a good source of material in showing me how to handle Double Byte Characters Sets or UNICODE in COBOL running on minis and mainframes? What is the best way to convert an existing suite of COBOL program from SBCS to handle foreign languages?

Thanks.

Rover
```

#### ↳ Re: Internationalization in COBOL

- **From:** "William M. Klein" <wmklein@ix.netcom.com>
- **Date:** 2000-12-12T12:25:09-06:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<915qf0$eld$1@slb7.atl.mindspring.net>`
- **References:** `<915422$e0j$1@bunyip.cc.uq.edu.au>`

```
*UNFORTUNATELY* there is no "general" way to do this today - without knowing
which compiler you are using.  If by "mainframe and minis" you mean IBM
mainframe compilers - and the PC compilers that "emulate them" - or if you
mean any "mini" compiler that conforms to the (older) X/Open Standard, then
you *probably* can/should use PIC N (and the implied USAGE NATIONAL).
However, these have limited support for run-time LOCALES (i.e. same source
code but different "run-time results" depending on where - what locale -
your application is actually run).

All of this *is* included in the draft Standard. So once (if) it gets
approved and implemented, there will be "standard" ways to do this.

If this is not a "general" question but a question about how to do a
specific task with a specific compiler (and specific operating system), let
us know the details and we can give you more information/solutions.
```

---

<a id="t-baa4b133ce"></a>
## Thread: debug options in cobol os/390 — 1 msgs

_Topics: [`Mainframe, z/OS, JCL, CICS`](topics.md#mainframe)_

### Re: debug options in cobol os/390

- **From:** scomstock@aol.com (S Comstock)
- **Date:** 2000-12-12T13:16:55+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<20001212081655.26594.00004186@ng-fu1.aol.com>`
- **References:** `<90limt$hhl10@sunsv007>`

```
Noï¿½l Garnier writes ...

>Hello,
>
…[6 more quoted lines elided]…
>

I thought we had this one just last week.

Anyway, TEST(ALL,SYM) costs a lot in terms of performance and should never be
used in production (I don't have a number on the cost, though).

In our class "COBOL Debugging and Maintenance in the LE Environment" we
recommend TEST(NONE,SYM). This embeds your data map in your load module. This
can create signficantly larger load modules but you get no performance hit
(except for module load time). But, if you abend you get a formatted dump of
all data division items. With V2R10 and COBOL for OS/390 & VM V2R2 you can code
TEST(NONE,SYM,SEPARATE) and the data map will be stored in a separate file;
this shrinks your load module and you only need to ensure the file containing
the data map is in your STEPLIB.

Hope this helps.

Regards,


Steve Comstock
Telephone: 303-393-8716
www.trainersfriend.com
email: steve@trainersfriend.com
256-B S. Monaco Parkway
Denver, CO 80224
USA
```

## Thread: Embedded SQL and Fujitsu COBOL — 11 msgs

_Topics: [`Compilers and vendors`](topics.md#compilers) · [`Databases and SQL`](topics.md#databases)_

### Embedded SQL and Fujitsu COBOL

- **From:** Floyd Johnson <floydj@netins.net>
- **Date:** 2000-12-12T10:50:30-05:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<3A364946.F8281687@netins.net>`

```
We have been using embedded SQL for a good portion of the semester, but
only to retrieve portions of a table (e.g. the first five entries).  For
the final exam (ouch), I have asked students to retrieve an entire
table.  Using the samples given in the supplied documentation we have
come up with the following code.  The only error message we receive
(using Fujitsu v3) is "SYNTAX OF WHENEVER STATEMENT IS INVALID."  Yet it
appears to match that given in the documentation.

Are we missing something?  Is there another (or better) technique for
retrieving an entire table?  Is checking SQLSTATE a better way to go? 
Thanks for any comments.

IDENTIFICATION DIVISION.
PROGRAM-ID.                     SQL-Test.

ENVIRONMENT DIVISION.
CONFIGURATION SECTION.
SOURCE-COMPUTER.  IBM-PC.
OBJECT-COMPUTER.  IBM-PC.

DATA DIVISION.
WORKING-STORAGE SECTION.
     exec sql 
         begin declare section 
     end-exec.
01   sqlstate                   pic X(5).
01   counter 			pic S9(9).
01   CharTrip                   pic S9(9)    comp-5.
01   ModName                    pic X(50).
     exec sql 
         end declare section 
     end-exec.		

01   OUT-CharTrip               pic 99999.
01   OUT-ModName	        pic X(50).

PROCEDURE DIVISION.
SQL-Test-paragraph.
	exec sql 
		WHENEVER NOT FOUND GO TO LoopEnd 
	end-exec

	exec sql 
        	CONNECT TO default
	end-exec
		
	exec sql 
	  declare PlaneType cursor STATIC
          for select Charter.Char_Trip, Model.Mod_Name
                     from Charter, Model, Aircraft
                     where Charter.AC_Number = Aircraft.AC_Number
	                   and Aircraft.Mod_Code = Model.Mod_Code
	                   and Model.Mod_Name = 'Navajo
Chieftain'	                
	end-exec
	
	exec sql
	        open PlaneType
	end-exec                        				
	.
	
Looper.    
	exec sql
     		  fetch PlaneType into :CharTrip, :ModName
        end-exec
     
        move CharTrip to OUT-CharTrip
	move ModName to OUT-ModName
        display OUT-CharTrip, "   ", OUT-ModName 
        GO TO Looper
	.

LoopEnd.    
	exec sql
     		  close PlaneType
	end-exec

    	exec sql
     		  rollback work
     	end-exec
     
     	exec sql 
     		  disconnect default
     	end-exec
     
     	stop run
	.		  
```

#### ↳ Re: Embedded SQL and Fujitsu COBOL

- **From:** "Brad Prothero" <brad.prothero@clarica.com>
- **Date:** 2000-12-12T15:15:10-06:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<gAwZ5.8$T4.1822@news.corpcomm.net>`
- **References:** `<3A364946.F8281687@netins.net>`

```

>SQL-Test-paragraph.
> exec sql
> WHENEVER NOT FOUND GO TO LoopEnd
> end-exec

Try "WHENEVER NOT FOUND GO TO :LoopEnd" since you are still in a Exec SQL
statement.

Brad Prothero
Clarica Life Insurance
Fargo, ND
```

Very interesting.  We had a similar problem with quotation marks.  A
student had a SQL statement that worked in an interactive mode, but when
used within a COBOL program it bombed.  At least this was compiling and
sending messages to the ODBC driver and we could look at the trace.  The
offending SQL SELECT statement was being sent to the driver with two
trailing double quotation marks.  When we changed the double quotes to
single quotes, all worked well.  

Thanks for the feedback.

Floyd

the best.  Wierd.

## Thread: Embedded SQL and Fujitsu COBOL — 1 msgs

_Topics: [`Compilers and vendors`](topics.md#compilers) · [`Databases and SQL`](topics.md#databases)_

### Embedded SQL and Fujitsu COBOL

- **From:** Floyd Johnson <floydj@netins.net>
- **Date:** 2000-12-12T10:50:54-05:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<3A36495E.A3256DAE@netins.net>`

```
We have been using embedded SQL for a good portion of the semester, but
only to retrieve portions of a table (e.g. the first five entries).  For
the final exam (ouch), I have asked students to retrieve an entire
table.  Using the samples given in the supplied documentation we have
come up with the following code.  The only error message we receive
(using Fujitsu v3) is "SYNTAX OF WHENEVER STATEMENT IS INVALID."  Yet it
appears to match that given in the documentation.

Are we missing something?  Is there another (or better) technique for
retrieving an entire table?  Is checking SQLSTATE a better way to go? 
Thanks for any comments.

IDENTIFICATION DIVISION.
PROGRAM-ID.                     SQL-Test.

ENVIRONMENT DIVISION.
CONFIGURATION SECTION.
SOURCE-COMPUTER.  IBM-PC.
OBJECT-COMPUTER.  IBM-PC.

DATA DIVISION.
WORKING-STORAGE SECTION.
     exec sql 
         begin declare section 
     end-exec.
01   sqlstate                   pic X(5).
01   counter 			pic S9(9).
01   CharTrip                   pic S9(9)    comp-5.
01   ModName                    pic X(50).
     exec sql 
         end declare section 
     end-exec.		

01   OUT-CharTrip               pic 99999.
01   OUT-ModName	        pic X(50).

PROCEDURE DIVISION.
SQL-Test-paragraph.
	exec sql 
		WHENEVER NOT FOUND GO TO LoopEnd 
	end-exec

	exec sql 
        	CONNECT TO default
	end-exec
		
	exec sql 
	  declare PlaneType cursor STATIC
          for select Charter.Char_Trip, Model.Mod_Name
                     from Charter, Model, Aircraft
                     where Charter.AC_Number = Aircraft.AC_Number
	                   and Aircraft.Mod_Code = Model.Mod_Code
	                   and Model.Mod_Name = 'Navajo
Chieftain'	                
	end-exec
	
	exec sql
	        open PlaneType
	end-exec                        				
	.
	
Looper.    
	exec sql
     		  fetch PlaneType into :CharTrip, :ModName
        end-exec
     
        move CharTrip to OUT-CharTrip
	move ModName to OUT-ModName
        display OUT-CharTrip, "   ", OUT-ModName 
        GO TO Looper
	.

LoopEnd.    
	exec sql
     		  close PlaneType
	end-exec

    	exec sql
     		  rollback work
     	end-exec
     
     	exec sql 
     		  disconnect default
     	end-exec
     
     	stop run
	.		  
```

## Thread: COBOL file structure — 11 msgs

### COBOL file structure

- **From:** FDNY <fdnyd110@datatone.com>
- **Date:** 2000-12-12T12:09:17-05:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<3A365BBB.B1785D3E@datatone.com>`

```
I have a simple question.
I am trying to write a disk to tape COBOL file conversion program on a
Unisys system in Assembler.  What indicates the end of a file?
```

#### ↳ Re: COBOL file structure

- **From:** Susan Allen <susan.a.allen@boeing.com>
- **Date:** 2000-12-13T00:03:44+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<3A36BCE0.81E4E777@boeing.com>`
- **References:** `<3A365BBB.B1785D3E@datatone.com>`

```
FDNY wrote:
> 
> I have a simple question.
> I am trying to write a disk to tape COBOL file conversion program on a
> Unisys system in Assembler.  What indicates the end of a file?

AT END

is a COBOL condition that can be test in the READ statement.
I have always assumed that some sort of binary symbol was written at the
end of file, but perhaps the READ statement is coded in such a way that
a read next record statement failure yields the AT END condition.  (SQL
is like that, reading the next record when a next record does not exit
yields a testable result that means end of file).

	Susan A
```

##### ↳ ↳ Re: COBOL file structure

- **From:** Howard Brazee <howard@brazee.net>
- **Date:** 2000-12-13T07:05:37-07:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<3A378231.F0C784B0@brazee.net>`
- **References:** `<3A365BBB.B1785D3E@datatone.com> <3A36BCE0.81E4E777@boeing.com>`

```
I have always assumed the AT-END condition was something the operating
system knew.  The CoBOL program just asked the OS.  I suppose this
assumption is because I don't need to know what language the file had been
written in to know when it was AT-END, and I could use whatever utility I
want to copy that file.

Does FDNY have some utility which doesn't know when it reaches the EOF?
What is the environment?

#### ↳ Re: COBOL file structure

- **From:** yukonmama@aol.com (YukonMama)
- **Date:** 2000-12-13T03:09:21+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<20001212220921.09174.00004090@ng-ca1.aol.com>`

```
>From: FDNY fdnyd110@datatone.com 
>Date: 12/12/00 12:09 PM Eastern Standard Time
>Message-id: <3A365BBB.B1785D3E@datatone.com>
>
snip
> COBOL file 
snip

::sigh::  This always gets me...

/partial rant mode on

COBOL is a language for computer programming - like English is a language,
French is a language, German is a language etc etc for people to communicate
with (at least we hope they do - this point can be debatable).  

COBOL may have been used to create the file but IT ISN'T THE FILE!  

Files are fixed in length or variable in length, indexed or non-indexed, in
EBCIDIC or ASCII and will be the such whether created via COBOL, or C, or C++,
or Pascal, or the language dejour.

The proper question probably should be 'how do I detect the end of file in
Assembler'  the anwer of which I do not know as I don't know Assembler in any
flavor (I can sorta read it - but that's also iffy). 

/partial rant mode off

Anyway even with this being that this a COBOL language forum there may be
several people here who know the answer to your question anyway.

Eileen
```

##### ↳ ↳ Re: COBOL file structure

- **From:** Christopher Clark <compudata@cadvision.com>
- **Date:** 2000-12-13T10:32:18-07:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<m3zoi0qlb1.fsf@localhost.localdomain>`
- **References:** `<3A365BBB.B1785D3E@datatone.com> <20001212220921.09174.00004090@ng-ca1.aol.com>`

```
yukonmama@aol.com (YukonMama) writes:

> COBOL may have been used to create the file but IT ISN'T THE FILE!
> 
> Files are fixed in length or variable in length, indexed or non-indexed, in
> EBCIDIC or ASCII and will be the such whether created via COBOL, or C, or
> C++, or Pascal, or the language dejour.

  I think the reason this occurs is that in C, C++, Pascal, and for the
most part in the language du jour, the file structure for indexed files
is decided by the programmer.

  An indexed file programmed in COBOL is in a format that the compiler
writer chose, that (based on my experience) they don't document.  If you
need to access the data outside of COBOL, good luck.  As a result, we
see people posting here asking for the format of <compiler's> data
files, because they don't have a copy of <compiler> anymore.
```

###### ↳ ↳ ↳ Re: COBOL file structure

- **From:** "William M. Klein" <wmklein@ix.netcom.com>
- **Date:** 2000-12-13T14:30:05-06:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<918m5g$imd$1@slb7.atl.mindspring.net>`
- **References:** `<3A365BBB.B1785D3E@datatone.com> <20001212220921.09174.00004090@ng-ca1.aol.com> <m3zoi0qlb1.fsf@localhost.localdomain>`

```
"Christopher Clark" <compudata@cadvision.com> wrote in message
news:m3zoi0qlb1.fsf@localhost.localdomain...
> yukonmama@aol.com (YukonMama) writes:
<snip>
>   An indexed file programmed in COBOL is in a format that the compiler
> writer chose, that (based on my experience) they don't document.  If you
…[3 more quoted lines elided]…
>

This is one of those - it depends on the environment in which you work ing
(often Mainframe vs PC).

- In most (all?) mainframe environemnts, "file structures" (even for
"relative" and "indexed" files) are part of the "operating system" - and
have NOTHING to do with the language "accessing them".  This is true
REGARDLESS of whether the mainframe hardware/OS vendor is or is not the same
vendor as the compiler vendor.  (Compare IBM mainframe where SAS/C uses
*IBM* VSAM files as the "indexed file" system.)

- In most (all?) "workstation" environments, only "line sequential" file
systems are part of the operating system.  This means there MAY be vendors
of file systems (compare C-ISAM and BTRIEVE) and these vendors do NOT create
compilers.  OR a compiler vendor may create their OWN file systems (compare
MERANT vs AcuCOBOL vs RM variable length sequential files - much less
indexed file systems).  There may or may NOT be "external interfaces" that
other languages can use to access these files - that depends TOTALLY on the
compiler vendor's decision.
```

#### ↳ Re: COBOL file structure

- **From:** "mangogwr" <mangogrower@telocity.co>
- **Date:** 2000-12-12T22:25:48-05:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<rYBZ5.1027$ja.224957@newsrump.sjc.telocity.net>`
- **References:** `<3A365BBB.B1785D3E@datatone.com>`

```
Look in the Assembler Reference or more likely, the Data System Macros.
Look for the EODADD or something like End Of Data Address.

That will be the address of a routine that is 'jumped' to when the file
system
detects EOD.

But you can probably just  write a few lines of procedure code.
If its a straight 'copy' from one to the other, that's all you need.
If its a keyed file, the check the commands manual, there are likely many
options
compared to IBM MVS/VSE JCL.

I'd feel pretty safe betting that any mini thru mainframe assembler will
have EODADD and ERRADD (Error  Routine Address) that the DCB macro
will require.


FDNY <fdnyd110@datatone.com> wrote in message
news:3A365BBB.B1785D3E@datatone.com...
> I have a simple question.
> I am trying to write a disk to tape COBOL file conversion program on a
> Unisys system in Assembler.  What indicates the end of a file?
>
```

#### ↳ Re: COBOL file structure

- **From:** "DBuck" <dbuck@prairieinet.net>
- **Date:** 2000-12-12T22:11:56-06:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<916spj$3abi4$1@ID-39920.news.dfncis.de>`
- **References:** `<3A365BBB.B1785D3E@datatone.com>`

```

FDNY <fdnyd110@datatone.com> wrote in message
news:3A365BBB.B1785D3E@datatone.com...
> I have a simple question.
> I am trying to write a disk to tape COBOL file conversion program on a
> Unisys system in Assembler.  What indicates the end of a file?
>

Well, first off, COBOL is just a programming language.  It does not have a
native file format.  The end of file marking should be consistent with the
system the file was created on.

Your assembler should support an EODADD (end of file/data) routine that will
branch for you at the end of the file.  You will find information on that
within the description of the DCB.
```

#### ↳ Re: COBOL file structure

- **From:** jacksleight@my-deja.com
- **Date:** 2000-12-13T13:59:52+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<917vck$hno$1@nnrp1.deja.com>`
- **References:** `<3A365BBB.B1785D3E@datatone.com>`

```
In article <3A365BBB.B1785D3E@datatone.com>,
  fdnyd110@datatone.com wrote:
> I have a simple question.
> I am trying to write a disk to tape COBOL file conversion program on a
> Unisys system in Assembler.  What indicates the end of a file?
>
> Generally the language doesn't dictate the physical
format/construction of the file, the operating system does (i.e. the
access method). I'm familliar with IBM mainframes (OS390/MVS, etc.).
In those environments an end of file marker indicates the EOF. This
marker is generated when the file is OPENed for OUTPUT or I-O and
subsequently CLOSEd. Generally, the application pgm does the CLOSE, but
if it abends the OS closes the file. If the OS fails, no EOF marker is
generated.


Sent via Deja.com
http://www.deja.com/
```

- **Message-ID:** `<5oUZ5.27$UN1.6125@newsread2.prod.itd.earthlink.net>`

#### ↳ Re: COBOL file structure

- **From:** jmpii@aol.com (JMPII)

- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<20001221191219.21161.00001467@ng-md1.aol.com>`
- **References:** `<3A365BBB.B1785D3E@datatone.com>`

```
In UNISYS COBOL the end of file (address or record number) is stored in the
Disk File Header and can accessed with COBOL extensions, or better yet in
ALGOL, I have not come across an assembler in the UNISYS A series.
```

## Thread: CEDF/InterTest Invoking in Messaging Environment? — 11 msgs

### CEDF/InterTest Invoking in Messaging Environment?

- **From:** docdwarf@clark.net ( NA)
- **Date:** 2000-12-12T17:27:53+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<tetZ5.4953$Sl.253700@iad-read.news.verio.net>`

```

Please pardon my ignorance about such matters... I've been asked to
modify/enhance/Make Right a CICS/DB2 program which I'm having a bit of
trouble with.  Consider the following:

Program A is invoked when a separate region sends over a message via LU6.2
protocol.  Program A examines this message, part of which is the program
name to which it must link, say... Program B.  Program B receives the
LU6.2-originated messsage via the COMMAREA and then does... stuff.

I've been asked to work with Program B and I am at a loss as to how I
would 'grab' it for examination under CEDF or (even better!) InterTest.  I
know the program's name, a TERMID it is passed and the CONN and NET
associated with this TERMID... but I do *not* know how to invoke any of
the debugging tools on my terminal so that when Program B wakes up I can
step through it.

Might anyone be so kind as to pass along a pointer or three?

Thanks much.

DD
```

#### ↳ Re: CEDF/InterTest Invoking in Messaging Environment?

- **From:** "WOB" <wobconsult@sprynet.com>
- **Date:** 2000-12-12T17:38:03-05:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<9168ui$cpv$1@nntp9.atl.mindspring.net>`
- **References:** `<tetZ5.4953$Sl.253700@iad-read.news.verio.net>`

```
DD,

        You must put the LU6.2 Connection Name under CEDF. When a session
becomes active, you'll be able to step through it. But, make sure no one
else is using the connection or you'll be CEDFing every active session.

Bill

WOB seems to have answered the CEDF part.  (I've never tried that.)  For
Intertest you can go to the "Unconditional Breakpoints" screen (using CNTL) and

terminal to act upon (or something like that) put ".ANY".  (That's "[dot]ANY".)

#### ↳ Re: CEDF/InterTest Invoking in Messaging Environment?

- **From:** Arnold Trembley <arnold.trembley@worldnet.att.net>
- **Date:** 2000-12-13T06:42:03+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<3A3719C2.D6038B56@worldnet.att.net>`
- **References:** `<tetZ5.4953$Sl.253700@iad-read.news.verio.net>`

```
NA wrote:
> 
> Please pardon my ignorance about such matters... I've been asked to
…[19 more quoted lines elided]…
> DD

I'm not sure if this will be any help, since I have been using Xpeditor
for CICS for the last eight years or so.  Prior to that I used InterTest
extensively for debugging CICS programs under conversational tasks.  I
imagine that InterTest has had a few enhancements since CICS 1.6.1!

If you were using Xpeditor I don't think there would be any problem. 
You would just set up a breakpoint at the first executable statement,
make sure monitoring was turned on, and wildcard any terminal.  The
debugging session would be associated with your terminal (but it would
have to be in the same CICS region where program B will execute). 
Xpeditor would trap "program B" as soon as it receives control from the
LINK command.  I have used both Xpeditor and InterTest to trap programs
that receive messages via MRO from another CICS region.

I remember a problem we had with InterTest.  Normally we used a test
program to simulate receipt of messages from our external network.  The
test messages were actually read from a VSAM RRDS file.  The test
program simulated the top of chain for a very long-running
conversational task (lots of XCTL's and LINK's).  The test program was
conversational, but not particularly long running.  The production
program normally sat in a loop on an EXEC CICS RETRIEVE WAIT, then took
the message and XCTL'ed to the next program. 

It came to pass that we had to test the real production program that
received network messages, the one named in the PCT entry as
top-of-chain.  And we could NOT get InterTest to trap it.  This
particular application had 20 tasks (each with a unique TERMID) to
receive network messages from BTAM.  They happened to be written to
restart themselves after an ABEND.  We had to cancel every task and then
send a test message.  The first terminal that received the message would
start the task, and then InterTest could trap it.  Later, when we
switched to Xpeditor (in order to upgrade to CICS release 3.3) we had
the same problem, and had to use the same technique.  

I have fond memories of InterTest.  I think I like the Xpeditor user
interface a little better.  They're both very capable debuggers, but the
InterTest FILE and CORE programs were handy because they could be
secured separately under their own TRAN-IDs.  

I've never learned CEDF.  I've seen it used once or twice, and it's
nowhere near as powerful as InterTest or Xpeditor.  

Good Luck!
```

## Thread: New MERANT press release — 4 msgs

_Topics: [`Compilers and vendors`](topics.md#compilers)_

### New MERANT press release

- **From:** "William M. Klein" <wmklein@ix.netcom.com>
- **Date:** 2000-12-12T13:12:59-06:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<915tag$nda$1@nntp9.atl.mindspring.net>`

```
I thought the following MERANT press release might be of interest to this
group.

"MERANT EnterpriseLink Generates Components From Legacy Assets For Fast
E-Business Enablement
December 12, 2000 08:03:00 AM ET

NEW YORK--(BUSINESS WIRE)--Dec. 12, 2000-- --MERANT Egility Legacy
Transformation and Integration Solution now turns mainframe systems into
powerful new Web-enabled components easily--

MERANT (NNM:MRNT; LSE:MRN), a leading global e-business software solutions
company, today announced major enhancements to its Egility(TM) Legacy
Transformation and Integration Solution with the introduction of
EnterpriseLink(R) featuring Component Generator. EnterpriseLink is designed
to reduce the time to extend mainframe applications to the Web by more than
50 percent. This Egility solution, demonstrated today at the eBusiness
Conference & Expo in New York, integrates and extends mainframe applications
to the Web without having to undertake a major programming effort and
without making changes to existing mainframe production systems.

EnterpriseLink with Component Generator allows the capture of complete
business processes and workflows, then automatically generates reusable,
industry-standard components in the form of JavaBeans, Enterprise JavaBeans
and XML for use throughout organizations seeking to e-enable
business-critical applications. This unique technology allows
business-critical transactions within mainframe applications, written in
COBOL, to be rapidly transformed into "e-business" transactions without
taking existing systems out of production. EnterpriseLink helps customers
quickly extend the reach of these assets by enhancing them to participate in
e-business solutions.

"Application software is a corporate asset and companies should look closely
at these assets and how they can be leveraged for use across the Web, such
as creating a bridge between the legacy applications and the new Web-based
ones," said Tracy Corbo, senior analyst, Hurwitz Group. "EnterpriseLink's
Component Generator function enables developers to expose legacy
applications written in COBOL as services to Java-based applications. This
provides the double benefit of both time-to-market savings coupled with ease
of integration for companies with legacy code that can be re-used for Web
development efforts."

EnterpriseLink with Component Generator captures business workflows from
CICS mainframe applications and automatically generates re-usable e-business
components using the knowledge database contained in MERANT's Revolve(R),
the industry leading COBOL analysis tool, included with EnterpriseLink.
These can be generated as Java Beans, Enterprise Java Beans or XML
components that can be used in an open standards-based environment. In
addition, EnterpriseLink automatically provides the middleware communication
between the components and the legacy application using IBM MQSeries.
EnterpriseLink-generated components can be developed and tested in a full
end-to-end fashion using MERANT's Mainframe Express(TM), a leading
workstation-based COBOL development platform.

"This focus on providing a complete solution for legacy and web-based
systems is profoundly important for our customers seeking to e-enable their
business," said Andrew Weiss, chief technology officer, MERANT. "The
time-to-market demands, coupled with the large investment in COBOL-based
mainframe technology cannot be ignored by companies seeking to maintain
their competitive advantage. Our investment in this technology and with the
enhanced features of Component Generator is clearly in line with our
solution-based strategy that will pay dividends for customers and for
MERANT."
```

#### ↳ Re: New MERANT press release

- **From:** "mangogwr" <mangogrower@telocity.co>

- **Message-ID:** `<B2CZ5.1052$ja.228066@newsrump.sjc.telocity.net>`

Sounds nifty, but I've used some very powerful COBOL 'repackager' tools
like the Merant description sounds, and with any kind of real coding (read
input
file, use some fields to read keyed files, build work record, store into
table,
get details, use keyed file data to populate, store into 2nd table,etc)

They are not as good /quick as an experienced P/A with a good editor (ISPF,
etc).
You have to compile the code (to get COPY / INCLUDES), then Identify
(usually
one variable at a time) EACH variable that you want it to look at, then
select the
SOURCE lines to 'grab', etc.

My goodness, by the time I've done that, I could (and did many times) do it
by hand!

> addition, EnterpriseLink automatically provides the middleware
communication
> between the components and the legacy application using IBM MQSeries.
> EnterpriseLink-generated components can be developed and tested in a full
…[4 more quoted lines elided]…
> systems is profoundly important for our customers seeking to e-enable
their
> business," said Andrew Weiss, chief technology officer, MERANT. "The
> time-to-market demands, coupled with the large investment in COBOL-based
> mainframe technology cannot be ignored by companies seeking to maintain
> their competitive advantage. Our investment in this technology and with
the
> enhanced features of Component Generator is clearly in line with our

…[7 more quoted lines elided]…

#### ↳ Re: New MERANT press release

- **From:** "Peter E. C. Dashwood" <dashwood@enternet.co.nz>
- **Date:** 2000-12-15T09:51:48+13:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<91bdn6$vk1$1@hermes.enternet.co.nz>`
- **References:** `<915tag$nda$1@nntp9.atl.mindspring.net>`

```
Said it before and I say it again:

"The future of computing is in component technology."

The logical extension of this idea is application development by simply
plugging together the appropriate components. Eventually, "clever" software
will do this, by interaction with the end user.
(I believe that will happen around 2015..."Computer programming" as we
understand it today will then be irrelevant. People will still do it, but it
won't be necessary. Unskilled (in computer technology) end users will be
able to construct their own applications by interaction with smart software.
I debated this at length in this forum two years ago and have seen nothing
in the interim to make me change my mind.)

Today they are using Java to  build the components (at least in this
example), but within 3 years the components will be constructible in ANY
language which is appropriate to the task the component is intended to carry
out (including COBOL), and the whole lot will be capable of running together
as one seamless solution. (Watch what happens when .NET becomes
established.)

Some of us are already building components in COBOL and using component
based design for application development.

Even at this early stage I have components developed in VB, COBOL, C++ and
Java, all of which peacefully co-exist and communicate with each other
without problem. (I am currently looking at Delphi as another potential
component contributor. It is a very good development tool.)

Windows Application development  (at least for me) is rapidly becoming a
simple case of selecting the appropriate components and dropping them on to
a form. Similarly, the same components can be easily dropped into HTML to
Web Enable Windows applications.

The concepts of Object Orientation are extremely applicable to component
development and it makes sense to use OO COBOL for this. However, it is not
a REQUIREMENT and good components can be built using structured COBOL. (They
just need to be "packaged" more carefully so that multiple instances can be
invoked...)

I would be interested to hear from anyone in this forum who is currently
using COBOL for component development, or would be interested in doing so.

Please mail me privately: dashwood@enternet.co.nz

Pete.

2000-12-14 10:20:30 MET

Ron schrieb:
> 
> ...

> Okay... and that event would be what?

In the evening of the 14-th of December 1900
Max Planck held a lecture before the
"Deutsche Physikalische Gesellschaft" in
which he explained his mathematical treatment
of black-body-radiation. In order to fit
the physical reality to his formulas, he was
forced to assume that light comes in quantas.

He himself was very reluctant to accept this.
Today we know that this was the first outbreak
of the framework of classical physics, which
was, at that time, believed to be a complete
description of nature.

Without quantum mechanics, it is hard to see
how one would ever develope semiconductor
devices. Computers, if there were any, would be
built with vacuum tubes. So there might be a
slim chance that COBOL would exist in a
society which does not know about QM - but the
internet certainly would not be there. No Java,
no Microsoft, no XML, no what have you.

Also, without QM, there were no nuclear weapons,
so history would have taken an entirely different
course since WWII.

Of course, as Howard Brazee has mentioned in the
other posting correctly, the time was due for this
discovery, and probably within short time,
somebody else would have started it all.

Herwig
```

#### ↳ Re: 14-th of december 1900

- **From:** "Peter E. C. Dashwood" <dashwood@enternet.co.nz>
- **Date:** 2000-12-14T22:32:56+13:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<91a5hp$t9q$1@hermes.enternet.co.nz>`
- **References:** `<3A375662.7AAA58D7@Josella-Simone-Playton.de>`

```
I believe you are referring to Max Planck's discovery of the Quantum,
encapsulated in his formula: E = hv

Where E is the energy being radiated, v is the frequency of the radiation,
and h is Planck's constant (6.6 x 10 -34 joule seconds)

(Basically, what this means is that the higher the frequency, the more
energy is contained in the Radiation. However, it is not infinite because
the "oscillators" in the atom which produce the radiation are limited to
specific intervals. (No one knows why, even today...) This led to the
discovery of the structure of electron shells and the release of packets of
energy ("quanta" ) which became the basis of Quantum Physics.

Planck arrived at his conclusions by a happy accident (he got the maths
"wrong" (more correctly, he did not complete the integration but stopped at
the answer he wanted)), but obtained the right answer. Einstein later went
on to use this work in the paper for which he received his Nobel prize,
concerning the effect of light knocking electrons out of metal. (NOT
Relativity...as many people think).

Planck's work solved the mystery of "Blackbody radiation" and the
"Ultraviolet catastrophe" and completely revolutionised classical physics,
opening the door to Quantum Physics, Quantum chromodynamics, and the
Uncertainty Principle, without which none of the electronic devices
(including computers) which we take for granted today, could function.

Some people (myself included) rate this discovery as one of the most
important scientific breakthroughs in the history of the Human Race,
comparable to the work of Galileo and Newton, and providing the building
blocks for Einstein, Heisenberg and the Nuclear age.

Pete.

>Herwig
I would agree with you that the significance we assign to historical events
is purely a matter of opinion.

It is important to remember however, that alternative histories exist only
in the future. So speculation about them can apply only to future events.
The nature of Quantum Reality is such that once the probability wave is
collapsed, the event becomes real (at least in this Universe...<G>).
Speculation on PAST alternative realities is purely the realm of Science
Fiction (Good fun, but nothing to do with Reality...)

(In other words, History for us is a single Time Line, so we can ascribe
whatever importance to it we like, secure in the knowledge that it cannot be
changed.)

For example, the Uncertainty Principle tells us we cannot know with
certainty the exact location and velocity of a fundamental particle at any
given moment. But we CAN deduce it's exact location and velocity IN THE
PAST.

I took the link you provided and read the article on Quantum Computing. (Not
my first exposure to this project) Very interesting. I believe the practical
difficulties in overcoming the EPR effect will make this technology
unreachable for the foreseeable future, but I hope I'm wrong...<G>

Can you imagine the COBOL required for such a machine?

SET  CURRENT-REALITY TO TIMELINE
COMPUTE ALL POSSIBLE OUTCOMES FOR
      SEARCH  DATABASE
               GET  WINNER OF 4TH RACE AT EPSOM ON SATURDAY
               GET  6 FROM 49 IN LOTTO ON SAME DAY
       END-SEARCH
  RETURNING REALITY-INDEXES
END-COMPUTE
SEARCH REALITY-INDEXES
      AT END
            DISPLAY "The World will end sometime between now and next
Saturday."
      WHEN
            REALITY-INDEXES (Feynman) = CURRENT-REALITY
                  MOVE  WINNER (Feynman) TO RACE-WINNER
                  MOVE  LOTTO    (Feynman)  TO LOTTO-RESULT
END-SEARCH
DISPLAY  RACE-WINNER " will win the 4th race at Epsom on Saturday."
DISPLAY  "The LOTTO balls for Saturday are: " LOTTO-RESULT

Viel Spass, nicht wahr?

Pete.

Not quite. The Multi-Universe-Interpretation of Quantum Mechanics
is consistent. If it is more than an interpretation, the other,
already split realities have the same degree of realism as
our reality has. One of the problems left is the coupling to
gravitation, because we do not observe "ghost"-gravitation which
cannot be attributed to mass distribuion in our own universe.

Also, the Multiverse-Version of QM makes the reality deterministic
again. A deterministic reality does not need to exist, in order
to exist. The Self-Aware-Subsets (we) of such realities would not know
the difference!

> (In other words, History for us is a single Time Line, so we can ascribe

Interpretation.)

- **References:** `<3A375662.7AAA58D7@Josella-Simone-Playton.de> <91a5hp$t9q$1@hermes.enternet.co.nz> <91a5na$qkt$1@news.mch.sbs.de> <91bith$vrv$1@hermes.enternet.co.nz> <3A39CCEB.20971346@Josella-Simone-Playton.de>`

```

Herwig Huener & Josella Simone Playton wrote in message
<3A39CCEB.20971346@Josella-Simone-Playton.de>...
>"Peter E. C. Dashwood" wrote:
>>
…[3 more quoted lines elided]…
>> >"Peter E. C. Dashwood" schrieb:

>Not quite. The Multi-Universe-Interpretation of Quantum Mechanics
>is consistent. If it is more than an interpretation, the other,
…[9 more quoted lines elided]…
>
Yes, the multiverse Interpretation is mathematically consistent, but that
doesn't make it true. Many respected thinkers are moving away from it. You
probably know that the propounders of it  (Everett originally, revived by De
Witt in 1960, then picked up by John Wheeler who is arguably one of the best
brains on the planet in this field) have not always remained convinced of
it.

At a symposium on the centenary of Einstein's birth Wheeler said:
"I confess I have had to reluctantly give up my support of that point of
view in the end - much as I advocated it in the beginning - because I am
afraid it carries too great a load of Metaphysical baggage".

However, it IS one of the very few theories which gives the same result as
the Copenhagen interpretation, and allows a "normal" mind to come to grips
with paradoxes such as Schrodinger's Cat and Young's famous two-slit
experiment.

I believe we are still quite a long way from a detailed understanding of the
Universe. I agree withyou that we choose what we want to believe. Like you,
I am not happy with the Copenhagen interpretation either, but it is probably
the most consistently successful theory in the history of Mankind. It has
NEVER been found to disagree with observable Reality.

Fortunately some of the wilder GUTs are offering glimpses of other
alternatives. I like the idea of SuperString theory, particularly as it
explains the gravitational discrepancy you alluded to.

The second quoted paragraph above is a simple re-statement of the Weak
Anthropic Principle. (The Universe exists because we are here to observe
it...) You may be correct and there may be other past realities but we will
never observe them. Therefore, applying the principle of Occam's Razor, we
can ignore them. They are not REAL for US. The multiverse FUTURE is REAL
(until the wave function is collapsed -referred to as "decoherence" in the
article on Quantum Computing that you referenced),
 and that was the basis of my previous statement.
>> (In other words, History for us is a single Time Line, so we can ascribe
>> whatever importance to it we like, secure in the knowledge that it cannot
be
>> changed.)


>People I very much respect reject the Many-Worlds-Interpretation.
>That can be done safely as long as it is only an interpretation.
>But it sheds a light on the generation of likes and dislikes
>in scientists. So its a matter of psychology, after all?
It certainly is until something definitive comes along.

>(I myself, for instance, prefer Many-Worlds over Copenhagen
>Interpretation.)
You are in good company and the book is not closed on it yet. I also prefer
it to Copenhagen, but there are other interpretations I prefer over both of
them (SuperString Theory looks to me to have the best chance of explaining
it all..)


I'm a bit disappointed that no-one picked up on my Quantum COBOL
example...it is a COBOL forum after all...Guess (apart from Ron...)
everyone's lost their sense of Humour...
>>
>> SET  CURRENT-REALITY TO TIMELINE
…[18 more quoted lines elided]…
>>

>COBOL or any other language will not need a language interface
>to quantum computation. Quantum computing can be called with
>suitable libraries.
>
Er...I think it will be necessary to build a Quantum Computer first...<G>

As I said before, I believe the difficulties posed by the EPR effect will
render this impossible for the foreseeable future.

A computer in a coffee cup is just the sort of thing Journalists love to
seize on. Scientists do the work. Don't believe everything you read...<G>

Pete.

###### ↳ ↳ ↳ Re: 14-th of december 1900

_(thread depth: 6)_

- **From:** "Peter E. C. Dashwood" <dashwood@enternet.co.nz>
- **Date:** 2000-12-16T15:09:28+13:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<91ekfq$4le$4@hermes.enternet.co.nz>`
- **References:** `<3A375662.7AAA58D7@Josella-Simone-Playton.de> <91a5hp$t9q$1@hermes.enternet.co.nz> <91a5na$qkt$1@news.mch.sbs.de> <91bith$vrv$1@hermes.enternet.co.nz> <3A39D033.BDCFBCE9@Josella-Simone-Playton.de> <3a3a59b6$0$229@helios.is.co.za>`

```

Searcher wrote in message <3a3a59b6$0$229@helios.is.co.za>...

>Fact is that if we had to try make as little as possible happen in the
>longest possible time, the answere would slap us in the face faster than
you
>can say nutrino.


Ah, so you've worked in Local Government...? <G>


>Time must be removed from all equations and we will see some different
>results. None of which will be untrue.


Sorry Searcher, if Time were removed from all Equations there would be no
Universe. So there would be no one to see the "different results". Like
Matter and Energy, Time and Space are different aspects of the same thing
(hence the "Space/Time" continuum).

Now, you can change the direction of time without violating the Laws of
Physics (it is called "symmetry") but you cannot remove it altogether.

The idea inherent in what you are saying is not wrong. For example, a
particle which travels at the speed of light (the one which immediately
springs to mind is the photon) has no perception of time. Time is, in effect
"stopped" for it. So, if it was created in the Big Bang 20 billion years
ago, and has been racing round the Universe at the speed of light ever
since, when it finally enters your eye and impinges as a speck of light on
your Consciousness, it would "think" no time at all had elapsed. However,
this is NOT the same as removing time. (The Universe contains many particles
which do NOT travel at the speed of light...my fingers when I'm typing this
are a good example here...)

>
>Its all happening at the same time We are all the same being. All the
…[4 more quoted lines elided]…
>
Cool!
Can I have an ounce or two of whatever you're on <G>?

Pete.
```

2000-12-17 12:50:00 MEZ

"Peter E. C. Dashwood" wrote:
> 
> Herwig Huener & Josella Simone Playton wrote in message
…[18 more quoted lines elided]…
> that has no bearing on their everyday experience.

You may have a point there. The problem with any object orientated
lanuage is that you do not find easy complete examples (four-liners)
of object-programs where objects are really necessary.

> ...

> I thought about picking some of it  up and doing a COBOL conversion but the
> Maths is just out of my reach. (My mind glazes when people start talking
> about imaginary numbers...I can handle the Eigen Vectors in Hilbert space
> but I've ALWAYS had a problem with imaginary numbers...it's a psych
> thing...)

Imaginary numbers is so easy - you have them in a few simle steps:

1. Concede that there exist real numbers.

2. We define the set of all numbers of the form (a, b)
   where a and b are ordinary real numbers.

3. We define addition: (a, b) + (c, d) = (a+c, b+d)

4. We define multiplication: (a, b) * (c, d) = (a*c-b*d), a*d+b*c)

   The act of creation is complete. You can start using these
   numbers. - Now the familiar notoation:

5: We call (0, 1) = i.

Everything else follows. The reason that many people have
difficulties with imaginary and complex numbers is that many
everyday computional activities do not require them. I have
never seen 3 + 5i cows on the meadow, or spent 500 - 200i
currency units such as dollars or euros. If I owe you
500i bucks, the law does not know what kind of legal
relation that is. (Maybe it would be fun to march into
a bank and ask for a loan of 50000 + 100000i Dollars!)

Such things are more common in science and engineering. That's
the reason that FORTRAN has real numbers and COBOL has not.
Of course, given the above rules, you can compute with real
numbers in COBOL quite well.

BTW: Complex numbers might be put into COBOL-objects.
But for computing with such small, oftenly called
objects you need a real fast linkage. But that is
another subject.

> I'm going to get a friend of mine who is a Maths teacher to walk me through
> some of it. If I can find the time (and get the understanding) I'll do an OO
> COBOL version just for fun.
> 
> It certainly is a very interesting project.

Certainly. If you want to do something for mankind - and for
the COBOL community - maybe it's a good idea to place that
example unter the GNU Public License?!

> > ...

> >So much work, so few time ... it has snowed
> >outside (in this country and in this universe)
…[6 more quoted lines elided]…
> and sea are blue and I'm off to a barbeque...

> > ...

> >BTW: Yesterday morning arrived "The Fabric of Reality"
> >by David Deutsch, thank amazon.de. The second
…[6 more quoted lines elided]…
> With a recommendation like that, I'll certainly get a copy.

It may be that he will be one of the next nobel laureates.
I wonder whether I should place a bet on that.

Regards,

Herwig Huener
```

## Thread: NetExpress 3.1 cannot execute nested transactions with MS SQL Server 7 — 2 msgs

_Topics: [`Databases and SQL`](topics.md#databases)_

### NetExpress 3.1 cannot execute nested transactions with MS SQL Server 7

- **From:** "Dragan Matic" <gekko@EUnet.yu>
- **Date:** 2000-12-13T12:53:10+01:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<917om8$fu$1@SOLAIR2.EUnet.yu>`

```
    Following is a short example that should begin an outer transaction,
write some value into table, then start an inner transaction, again write a
row into table, commit inner transaction and  then rollback outer
transaction. As a result none of the two inserts should have written values
into table. What I am getting instead is that both rows are written, as if
rollback didn't exist.
    If I examine value of @@trancount variable that should show number of
levels of nested transactions I see that on the beginning of a program it is
already 1 and none of the subsequent 'exec sql begin transaction end-exec'
lines raises its value. But when first 'commit' is executed @@trancount is
lowered to 0 which means that no rollback can occur.
SampleTable is defined as
    SampleTable(numericValue int not null, stringValue char(50) not null)

      $set sql(dbman=odbc)
       working-storage section.
       exec sql begin declare section end-exec
       01  Numeric-Value           pic s9(05)  comp-5.
       01  String-value            pic x(50).
      *01  trancount   pic s9(09)  comp-5.
       exec sql end declare section end-exec

       procedure division.

           exec sql
               connect to 'SomeDatabase' user 'user'
           end-exec

      *    Check the value of @@trancount here with
      *    exec sql select @@trancount into :trancount end-exec
      *    Notice that it is already 1 althouth no transaction has been
      *    started yet

           exec sql
               begin transaction outer_transaction
           end-exec

      *    @@trancount still = 1

           exec sql
               insert into sampleTable
                   (numericValue, stringValue)
                   values
                   (1, 'First String')
           end-exec

           exec sql
               begin transaction inner_transaction
           end-exec

      *    @@trancount = 1

           exec sql
               insert into sampleTable
                   (NumericValue, StringValue)
                   values
                   (2, 'Second string')
           end-exec
           exec sql
               commit transaction inner_transaction
           end-exec

      *    After this point no rollback can occur since
      *    @@trancount now = 0

           exec sql
               rollback transaction outer_transaction
           end-exec

           @@trancount = 0

           exec sql
               disconnect current
           end-exec

           stop run
           .
```

#### ↳ Re: NetExpress 3.1 cannot execute nested transactions with MS SQL Server 7

- **From:** "Randy Zimmerman" <rzimmerman@wi.rr.com>
- **Date:** 2000-12-14T14:24:54+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<WK4_5.3783$Uq1.524725@typhoon.mn.mediaone.net>`
- **References:** `<917om8$fu$1@SOLAIR2.EUnet.yu>`

```
Following is response from our ODBC/SQL Server support developer:

ODBC does not support nested transactions. OpenESQL accepts Toolkit syntax
but doesn't provide all the functionality that the Toolkit did because
it's using ODBC - it can't. It does provide compatibility with
non-nested transactions using Toolkit syntax, but that's as far as it goes.


Randy Zimmerman
MERANT
