## Thread: MicroFocus 4.1.10 & AIX 4.3.3 — 2 msgs

_Topics: [`Compilers and vendors`](topics.md#compilers)_

### MicroFocus 4.1.10 & AIX 4.3.3

- **From:** "Jacques Vidal" <jvidal@mail.dotcom.fr>
- **Date:** 2000-12-13T13:48:34+01:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<917qkv$50g$1@wanadoo.fr>`

```
Does it work?

The COBOL suite was originally installed on an AIX 4.1 system that was
upgraded to 4.3.3 a few weeks ago. Apparently the compiler was still OK,
as we used it only to generate .int or .gnt modules, or in a few cases
object
modules that were statically linked into an RTS.

But...

We have decided to rewrite our app using Java. The server part is mainly
written in Java, and uses JNI to call legacy code (C and COBOL). The
native libraries are now linked as shared libraries. All JNI functions are
written in C, ofc, and may call C or COBOL code that's located in other
shared libraries.

I've read the /usr/lib/cobol/docs/dynlink.1 document, but it seems I can't
succesfully link C shared libraries with the Microfocus RT libraries. Every
time I try, I get these unresolved symbols:

ld: 0711-317 ERROR: Undefined symbol: hashtb
ld: 0711-317 ERROR: Undefined symbol: mFt_rt_application_config_name

(You can't produce shared libraries directly from the cob command, can you?)

I tried reinstalling the whole COBOL package, but it didn't solve anything.
Is it a compatibility problem? Or maybe are there issues I'm not aware of
with dynamic linking - the dynlink document seemed somewhat outdated?


Jacques Vidal
```

#### ↳ Re: MicroFocus 4.1.10 & AIX 4.3.3

- **From:** Stephen Gennard <stephen.gennard@merant.com>
- **Date:** 2000-12-15T14:33:36+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<3A3A2BC0.1040507@merant.com>`
- **References:** `<917qkv$50g$1@wanadoo.fr>`

```
Hi Jacques,

I would not advise you use OCDS and Java together because Java requires that
the language being called be thread-safe.   OCDS is *not* thread-safe and
does not support shared object either.

However if uses ServerExpress v2.0.10, you will find this includes Java
support for you, it is also thread-safe and includes shared object support.

We provide a Java package that allows you to call COBOL or Object COBOL
from Java, which means you do not have to use JNI....
```

Cromwell,

It it comes from an EBCDIC machine, you'll have to convert to ASCII, and if
it doesn't only contain character data but also numeric values, you'll need
the complete record definition. Without that, you don't know what parts of
the record you have to convert to ASCII
Willem Clements
Brainbench MVP for COBOL II
http://www.brainbench.com
```

#### ↳ Re: what kind of COBOL is this?

- **From:** Howard Brazee <howard@brazee.net>
- **Date:** 2000-12-13T08:00:05-07:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<3A378EF5.30C131EC@brazee.net>`
- **References:** `<zALZ5.27550$Q54.834172@e420r-atl1.usenetserver.com>`

```
I'm betting that it is EBCDIC, and you're reading it on an ASCII machine.  You
might need to find someone on a mainframe and have him look at it (FTP it in
binary mode?).   He can look at it to see if it contains binary or packed
data.  If it doesn't, he can FTP it back to you in character mode.  This FTP
will translate it to ASCII.

cromwell wrote:

> I have a data file from a cobol system that I can't unpack. I have dug
> around on the internet and downloaded some viewers and converters and
…[11 more quoted lines elided]…
>
```

#### ↳ Re: what kind of COBOL is this?

- **From:** Peter Lacey <lacey@mb.sympatico.ca>
- **Date:** 2000-12-14T00:33:03-06:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<3A38699F.E6E6AC02@mb.sympatico.ca>`
- **References:** `<zALZ5.27550$Q54.834172@e420r-atl1.usenetserver.com>`

```
cromwell wrote:

> I have a data file from a cobol system that I can't unpack. I have dug
> around on the internet and downloaded some viewers and converters and
…[11 more quoted lines elided]…
>

"FB" might  mean "Fixed-blocked" - i.e., fixed-length records, several of them
per physical tape record.  "041" might mean that's the record identifier.  See
if it appears in the block.  If it does, several times, then at least you'll
be able to determine the record length.
```

On 15 Dec 2000 14:56:32 GMT, thomas.gonschor@vph-bensberg.de (Thomas
Gonschor) enlightened us:

>Hi!
>
…[5 more quoted lines elided]…
>Thomas

COBOL sp2 is a tool used by COBOL programmers to develop and maintain
contemporary user interfaces for their programs.  It allows the
complexities of such an interface to be somewhat isolated from a COBOL
program, yet still enables a COBOL programmer to have close control
over the interface directly from a program using standard COBOL code.

It will interface with Fujitsu Cobol and there is a verion on the CD
that came with Thane's book.

Bob Wolfe where are you?

Regards,

          ////
         (o o)
-oOO--(_)--OOo-

An optimist thinks that this is the best possible world.
A pessimist fears that this is true.

Help Save The Rainforest
For more info, please see:  
http://www.ran.org/ran/

Remove nospam to email me.

Steve

#### ↳ Re: line feed

- **From:** Terry Winchester <terrywin.nospam@pronetisp.net>
- **Date:** 2000-12-13T16:24:45-05:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<jfpf3tcucg2knqp1mkb8bl7qpvhofv55ic@4ax.com>`
- **References:** `<918aef$rp3$1@nnrp1.deja.com>`

```
On Wed, 13 Dec 2000 17:08:38 GMT, sdeblanc@my-deja.com wrote:

>Ok, please don't laugh at this novice. I am
>looking for the character combination that will
…[12 more quoted lines elided]…
>

You will probably need to use embedded tab characters
(X'09') to get near your column. Most tabs expand to 8
spaces - you need 6, plus 5 spaces (X'20').  Not all 
printers support this method though.

HTH
Good Luck
Terry
```

most printers won't support that. He may need to keep track of  how many
characters have been printed, then do a CR/LF, then space out that many
characters before printing.

I have this in my notes.

I have never tried this though

Vertical and Horizontal cursor motion
Operation  === Type of motion === Ascii sequence === Decimal === Hexa
Vertical Position === # of Rows === Ec&a#R (r) === 027 038 097 #...#
082 (114) === 1B 26 61 #...# 52 (72)
 === # of Dots === Ec*p#Y(y) === 027 042 112 #...# 089(121) === 1B 2A
70 #...# 59 (79) === # of Decipoints === Ec&a#V (v) === 027 038 097
#...# 086(118) === 1B 26 61 #...# 56 (76)
Horizontal Position === # of Columns === Ec&a#C (c) === 027 038 097
#...# 067(99) === 1B 26 61 #...# 43 (63) === # of Dots === Ec*p#X (x)
=== 027 042 112 #...# 088  (120) === 1B 2A 70 #...# 58 (78)
 === # of Decipoints === Ec&a#H (h) === 027 038 097 #...# 072 (104)
=== 1B 26 61 #...# 48 (68)
Half Line Feed ===  === Ec= === 027 061	1B 3D

Put the text in a Excel spreadsheet bearing in mind that the column 
separator is " === ".

FF

 01 HEAD-2.
	  05 H2-TIME.
		10 H2-DOW		PIC X(3).
		10 FILLER		PIC X VALUE SPACE.
		10 H2-TIME-HOURS-LIT        PIC X(2).
	 	10 FILLER		PIC X VALUE ":".
		10 H2-TIME-MINUTES	PIC 99.
		10 FILLER		PIC X VALUE ":".
		10 H2-TIME-SECONDS      PIC 99.
	  05 FILLER			PIC X(13) VALUE SPACES.
	  05 FILLER			PIC X(61)
		VALUE "List of Inventory Items to Reorder".
 01 TITLE-LINE-1.
    05 FILLER     		PIC X(40)  VALUE SPACES.
	  05 FILLER			PIC X(8)   VALUE 'Quantity'.
	  05 FILLER		   	PIC X(4)   VALUE SPACES.
	  05 FILLER  			PIC X(4)   VALUE SPACES.
    05 FILLER			PIC X(6)   VALUE SPACES.
	  05 FILLER			PIC X(8)   VALUE SPACES.
 01 TITLE-LINE-2.
    05 FILLER                     PIC X(8)  VALUE 'Item Nbr'.
	  05 FILLER			PIC X(2)   VALUE SPACES.
	  05 FILLER			PIC X(16)  VALUE 
						 'Item Description'.
	  05 FILLER    			PIC X(14) VALUE SPACES.
	  05 FILLER			PIC X(7)  VALUE 'On Hand'.
	  05 FILLER  			PIC X(7)  VALUE SPACES.
	  05 FILLER			PIC X(9)  VALUE 'Unit Cost'.
    05 FILLER			PIC X(5)  VALUE SPACES.
	  05 FILLER			PIC X(12) VALUE 'Dollar Value'.
 01 DETAIL-LINE.
    05 DL-ITEM-NUM	        PIC  X(08)   VALUE SPACES.
    05 FILLER   		        PIC  X(01)   VALUE SPACES.
    05 DL-ITEM-DESC		PIC  X(30)   VALUE SPACES.
	  05 FILLER			PIC  X(1)    VALUE SPACES. 
	  05 DL-QTY-ON-HAND    	  	PIC  Z(6)9-  VALUE ZEROS.
    05 FILLER			PIC  X(4)    VALUE SPACES.
    05 DL-UNIT-COST		PIC  ZZ,ZZ9.9999-  .
    05 FILLER			PIC  X(1)    VALUE SPACES.
    05 DL-DOLLAR-VALUE		PIC  ZZZ,ZZZ,ZZ9.99-  .
 01 WS-ACCUMULATORS.

     05 WS-QTY-ON-HAND-TOT		PIC  S9(7)   VALUE ZEROS.

	  05 WS-UNIT-COST-TOT		PIC  ZZZ,ZZZ,ZZ9.99 VALUE ZEROS.
	  05 WS-DOLLAR-VALUE-TOT	PIC  999,999,999.99 VALUE ZEROS.
 01 TOTAL-LINE.
    05 FILLER 			PIC  X(10)   VALUE SPACES.
    05 FILLER			PIC  X(5)    VALUE 'Total'.
	  05 FILLER			PIC  X(1)    VALUE SPACES.
	  05 FILLER			PIC  X(10)   VALUE 'Quantities'.
    05 FILLER			PIC  X(15)   VALUE SPACES.
    05 TL-QTY-ON-HAND-TOT	        PIC  Z(6)9-.
    05 FILLER                     PIC  X(4)    VALUE SPACES.
    05 TL-UNIT-COST-TOT           PIC  ZZZ,ZZZ,ZZ9.99.
    05 FILLER                     PIC  X(7)    VALUE SPACES.
    05 TL-DOLLAR-VALUE-TOT        PIC  999,999,999.99.

* 01 WS-QTY-TO-REORDER               PIC  S9(7).
 01 WS-DOW 			PIC 9 	     VALUE ZERO.
 01 WS-REORDER-PT			PIC  9(6).
 01 WS-QTY-ON-HAND		PIC  9(6).
 01 EOF-FLAG		        PIC  X(01)   VALUE SPACE.  
 
 
 01 WS-DOLLAR-VALUE	        PIC S9(14)V99  
					SIGN TRAILING SEPARATE.
 01 WS-PAGE-CNT 			PIC  9(3) VALUE 0.
 01 WS-LINE-CNT			PIC  9(3) VALUE 0.
 01 PAGE-SIZE			PIC  9(3) VALUE 54.
 PROCEDURE DIVISION.
 MAINLINE.
     PERFORM 100-INITIALIZATION
     PERFORM 110-WRITE-HEADINGS
     PERFORM 200-PROCESSING
     PERFORM 300-TERMINATION

	   STOP RUN.
 100-INITIALIZATION.
     OPEN INPUT INVENTORY-FILE
		OUTPUT PRINT-FILE.
*     PERFORM 110-WRITE-HEADINGS
 110-WRITE-HEADINGS.
	   ADD 1 TO WS-PAGE-CNT
	   MOVE WS-PAGE-CNT TO H1-PAGE-NUM.
     MOVE FUNCTION CURRENT-DATE TO SYSTEM-DATE-AND-TIME

	   EVALUATE SYS-DATE-MM
		WHEN 01 MOVE "JAN" TO H1-MONTH-LIT
		WHEN 02 MOVE "FEB" TO H1-MONTH-LIT
		WHEN 03 MOVE "MAR" TO H1-MONTH-LIT
		WHEN 04 MOVE "APR" TO H1-MONTH-LIT
		WHEN 05 MOVE "MAY" TO H1-MONTH-LIT
		WHEN 06 MOVE "JUN" TO H1-MONTH-LIT
		WHEN 07 MOVE "JUL" TO H1-MONTH-LIT
		WHEN 08 MOVE "AUG" TO H1-MONTH-LIT
		WHEN 09 MOVE "SEP" TO H1-MONTH-LIT
		WHEN 10 MOVE "OCT" TO H1-MONTH-LIT
		WHEN 11 MOVE "NOV" TO H1-MONTH-LIT
		WHEN 12 MOVE "DEC" TO H1-MONTH-LIT
	   END-EVALUATE.
	   
	   EVALUATE SYS-TIME-HOURS
		WHEN 00 MOVE "12" TO  H2-TIME-HOURS-LIT
		WHEN 13 MOVE "01" TO  H2-TIME-HOURS-LIT
		WHEN 14 MOVE "02" TO  H2-TIME-HOURS-LIT
		WHEN 15 MOVE "03" TO  H2-TIME-HOURS-LIT
		WHEN 16 MOVE "04" TO  H2-TIME-HOURS-LIT
		WHEN 17 MOVE "05" TO  H2-TIME-HOURS-LIT
		WHEN 18 MOVE "06" TO  H2-TIME-HOURS-LIT
		WHEN 19 MOVE "07" TO  H2-TIME-HOURS-LIT
		WHEN 20 MOVE "08" TO  H2-TIME-HOURS-LIT
 		WHEN 21 MOVE "09" TO  H2-TIME-HOURS-LIT
		WHEN 22 MOVE "10" TO  H2-TIME-HOURS-LIT
		WHEN 23 MOVE "11" TO  H2-TIME-HOURS-LIT
		WHEN 24 MOVE "12" TO  H2-TIME-HOURS-LIT
	   END-EVALUATE.
	   ACCEPT WS-DOW FROM DAY-OF-WEEK 
	       EVALUATE WS-DOW 
		    WHEN 1 MOVE "MON" TO H2-DOW
		    WHEN 2 MOVE "TUE" TO H2-DOW
		    WHEN 3 MOVE "WED" TO H2-DOW
		    WHEN 4 MOVE "THU" TO H2-DOW
		    WHEN 5 MOVE "FRI" TO H2-DOW
		    WHEN 6 MOVE "SAT" TO H2-DOW
		    WHEN 7 MOVE "SUN" TO H2-DOW
	       END-EVALUATE.
*		MOVE SYS-TIME-HOURS   TO H2-TIME-HOURS.
		MOVE SYS-TIME-MINUTES TO H2-TIME-MINUTES.
          MOVE SYS-TIME-SECONDS TO H2-TIME-SECONDS.
		WRITE PRINT-RECORD    FROM HEAD-2 AFTER 1
		MOVE SYS-DATE-CCYY    TO H1-DATE-CCYY.
 		
*   	MOVE SYS-DATE-MM   TO H1-DATE-MM.
 		MOVE SYS-DATE-DD   TO H1-DATE-DD.
          WRITE PRINT-RECORD FROM HEAD-1 AFTER 1
	   MOVE SPACES             TO PRINT-RECORD
		WRITE PRINT-RECORD AFTER 1.
	   MOVE TITLE-LINE-1       TO PRINT-RECORD
		WRITE PRINT-RECORD AFTER ADVANCING 1.
	   MOVE TITLE-LINE-2       TO PRINT-RECORD
		WRITE PRINT-RECORD AFTER ADVANCING 1.	 	
     MOVE SPACES             TO PRINT-RECORD
		WRITE PRINT-RECORD AFTER 1.
	   MOVE 6 TO WS-LINE-CNT.
 200-PROCESSING.
     PERFORM UNTIL EOF-FLAG = 'Y'
         READ INVENTORY-FILE
	       AT END
		   MOVE 'Y' TO EOF-FLAG
         NOT AT END  
*             IF IR-QTY-ON-HAND < IR-REORDER-PT  
             PERFORM 205-PROCESS-A-RECORD    	       
*	         END-IF
	       END-READ 
	   END-PERFORM.
 205-PROCESS-A-RECORD.
	   IF WS-LINE-CNT > PAGE-SIZE
		 PERFORM 110-WRITE-HEADINGS
	   END-IF
     PERFORM 210-DISPLAY-A-LINE
*	   WRITE PRINT-RECORD FROM DETAIL-LINE AFTER 1.
	   ADD 1 TO WS-LINE-CNT.
 210-DISPLAY-A-LINE.
     	   COMPUTE WS-DOLLAR-VALUE 
			ROUNDED = IR-QTY-ON-HAND  *  IR-UNIT-COST  
	           END-COMPUTE
		           
 		 MOVE IR-ITEM-NBR 
		     TO DL-ITEM-NUM
	         MOVE IR-ITEM-DESCRIPTION
 		     TO DL-ITEM-DESC
	         MOVE IR-QTY-ON-HAND
		     TO DL-QTY-ON-HAND
	         MOVE IR-UNIT-COST
		     TO DL-UNIT-COST
		 MOVE WS-DOLLAR-VALUE 
		     TO DL-DOLLAR-VALUE
           MOVE DETAIL-LINE    TO PRINT-RECORD
		 WRITE PRINT-RECORD AFTER 1.
*	   ADD IR-QTY-ON-HAND    TO WS-QTY-ON-HAND-TOT.
*     ADD IR-REORDER-PT     TO WS-REORDER-PT-TOT.
     COMPUTE WS-UNIT-COST-TOT ROUNDED = WS-DOLLAR-VALUE-TOT / 
				  WS-QTY-ON-HAND-TOT
     END-COMPUTE.
     ADD 1 TO WS-LINE-CNT.
 300-TERMINATION.
     MOVE SPACES TO PRINT-RECORD
		WRITE PRINT-RECORD AFTER 1.
	   MOVE WS-QTY-ON-HAND-TOT    TO TL-QTY-ON-HAND-TOT.
	   MOVE WS-UNIT-COST-TOT     TO TL-UNIT-COST-TOT.
*	   MOVE WS-QTY-TO-REORDER-TOT TO TL-DOLLAR-VALUE-TOT.
     MOVE TOTAL-LINE TO PRINT-RECORD.
       WRITE PRINT-RECORD AFTER ADVANCING 1.
     CLOSE INVENTORY-FILE
           PRINT-FILE
```

#### ↳ Re: TOTAL-LINE QUESTION

- **From:** Howard Brazee <howard@brazee.net>
- **Date:** 2000-12-14T07:22:10-07:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<3A38D792.F777797A@brazee.net>`
- **References:** `<20001213200806.12046.00004824@ng-cj1.aol.com>`

```


Deek40 wrote:

> I KEEP GETTING A SYNTAX ERROR WS-DOLLAR-VALUE-TOT IN A ARITHMATIC EXPRESSION
> MUST BE A NUMERIC ITEM.  i CANNOT FIND MY ERROR IN MY CODE I WOULD APPRECIATE
> IT IF SOMEONE COULD PLEASE TAKE A LOOK.

I bet all of the programmers looked at the above question and knew what we would
find in the code.  This is an error we never get though, it is a beginner's only
error.

When a field has a picture such as 999,999,999.99  it no longer is a number.
Numbers can be moved to such a field.  That move puts commas and decimals in the
right place to make a display.  But commas, periods, spaces, dollar signs, plus,
minus, etc. are not numeric.

Only use such pictures in your output.  If you have to have them in your input,
you need to convert these alphanumeric strings to real numbers before you can do
arithmetic with them.  Real numbers do not have commas nor periods in them (the
computer uses the "V" to tell where the decimal is, and "S" to tell if it is
signed)
```

#### ↳ Re: TOTAL-LINE QUESTION

- **From:** lcccpiasabird@my-deja.com
- **Date:** 2000-12-14T16:25:49+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<91asa1$vd5$1@nnrp1.deja.com>`
- **References:** `<20001213200806.12046.00004824@ng-cj1.aol.com>`

```


NOTE:
Any numeric value with a pic clause with a comma, a dolloa sign, a
decimal point blanks (ZZZ), etc is an edited field and can not be used
in a calculation because it has non-numeric data in it for printing
purposes.

You need an accumulator or counter to put the data into in other words
the calculation field must be strictly like (PIC 9(10).)  Your compiler
may be able to unedit the number somehow if you look it up!

In article <20001213200806.12046.00004824@ng-cj1.aol.com>,
  deek40@aol.com (Deek40) wrote:
> I KEEP GETTING A SYNTAX ERROR WS-DOLLAR-VALUE-TOT IN A ARITHMATIC
EXPRESSION

> IT IF SOMEONE COULD PLEASE TAKE A LOOK.
>

> * Class:    CIS160B - Structured Business Programming I.
…[5 more quoted lines elided]…
>
************************************************************************

>
>  ENVIRONMENT DIVISION.
…[256 more quoted lines elided]…
>

http://www.deja.com/

##### ↳ ↳ Re: TOTAL-LINE QUESTION

- **From:** "William M. Klein" <wmklein@ix.netcom.com>
- **Date:** 2000-12-14T12:35:47-06:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<91b3sr$li5$1@slb0.atl.mindspring.net>`
- **References:** `<20001213200806.12046.00004824@ng-cj1.aol.com> <91asa1$vd5$1@nnrp1.deja.com>`

```
Probably not the answer that Derrick should use in his first semester of
COBOL - but there is another alternative which CAN accomplish this without
keeping both a numeric and a numeric-edited version of the field. Consider
the statement:

      COMPUTE WS-UNIT-COST-TOT ROUNDED =
            (Function NumVal (WS-DOLLAR-VALUE-TOT)) / WS-QTY-ON-HAND-TOT
                On Size Error
                       Display "Consider the possibility that QTY-ON-HAND is
zero"
      END-COMPUTE

P.S. notice my removal of the period after the END-COMPUTE statement and the
addition of the ON SIZE ERROR phrase.

   ***

I think that in *most* "real-world" applications, it is BETTER to have both
a numeric and numeric-edited version of such fields - but it isn't required
the the language (since the Intrinsic Function amendment)
```

          10 FILLER		PIC X .

	  05 FILLER 			PIC X(13) VALUE SPACES.
    05 FILLER			PIC X(40)
		VALUE "CIS160 Structured Business Programming".
	  05 FILLER 			PIC X(10) VALUE SPACES.
	  05 FILLER			PIC X(5)  VALUE "Page ".
	  05 H1-PAGE-NUM		PIC 9.
 01 HEAD-2.
	  05 H2-TIME.
		10 H2-DOW		PIC X(3).

	  05 FILLER			PIC X(61)
		VALUE "List of Inventory Items to Reorder".
 01 TITLE-LINE-1.
    05 FILLER     		PIC X(40)  VALUE SPACES.
	  05 FILLER			PIC X(8)   VALUE 'Quantity'.
	  05 FILLER		   	PIC X(4)   VALUE SPACES.
	  05 FILLER  			PIC X(4)   VALUE SPACES.
    05 FILLER			PIC X(6)   VALUE SPACES.
	  05 FILLER			PIC X(8)   VALUE SPACES.
 01 TITLE-LINE-2.

	  05 FILLER			PIC X(2)   VALUE SPACES.

						 'Item Description'.

	  05 FILLER			PIC X(7)  VALUE 'On Hand'.
	  05 FILLER  			PIC X(7)  VALUE SPACES.
	  05 FILLER			PIC X(9)  VALUE 'Unit Cost'.
    05 FILLER			PIC X(5)  VALUE SPACES.
	  05 FILLER			PIC X(12) VALUE 'Dollar Value'.
 01 DETAIL-LINE.
    05 DL-ITEM-NUM	        PIC  X(08)   VALUE SPACES.
    05 FILLER   		        PIC  X(01)   VALUE SPACES.
    05 DL-ITEM-DESC		PIC  X(30)   VALUE SPACES.
	  05 FILLER			PIC  X(1)    VALUE SPACES. 
	  05 DL-QTY-ON-HAND    	  	PIC  Z(6)9-  VALUE ZEROS.
    05 FILLER			PIC  X(4)    VALUE SPACES.
    05 DL-UNIT-COST		PIC  S9(11)V999 VALUE ZEROS  .
    05 FILLER			PIC  X(1)    VALUE SPACES.
    05 DL-DOLLAR-VALUE		PIC  S9(11)V999 VALUE ZEROS  .
 01 WS-ACCUMULATORS.

     05 WS-QTY-ON-HAND-TOT	PIC  S9(7)   VALUE ZEROS.

	  05 WS-UNIT-COST-TOT		PIC  S9(11)V999 VALUE ZEROS.
	  05 WS-DOLLAR-VALUE-TOT	PIC  S9(11)V999 VALUE ZEROS.
 01 TOTAL-LINE.
    05 FILLER 			PIC  X(10)   VALUE SPACES.
    05 FILLER			PIC  X(5)    VALUE 'Total'.
	  05 FILLER			PIC  X(1)    VALUE SPACES.
	  05 FILLER			PIC  X(10)   VALUE 'Quantities'.
    05 FILLER			PIC  X(15)   VALUE SPACES.
    05 TL-QTY-ON-HAND-TOT	        PIC  S9(7).
    05 FILLER                     PIC  X(4)    VALUE SPACES.
    05 TL-UNIT-COST-TOT           PIC  S9(11)V999.
    05 FILLER                     PIC  X(7)    VALUE SPACES.
    05 TL-DOLLAR-VALUE-TOT        PIC  S9(11)V999.

 01 WS-DOW 			PIC 9 	     VALUE ZERO.
 01 WS-REORDER-PT			PIC  9(6).
 01 WS-QTY-ON-HAND		PIC  9(6).
 01 EOF-FLAG		        PIC  X(01)   VALUE SPACE.  
 
 
 01 WS-DOLLAR-VALUE	        PIC S9(14)V99  
					SIGN TRAILING SEPARATE.
 01 WS-PAGE-CNT 			PIC  9(3) VALUE 0.
 01 WS-LINE-CNT			PIC  9(3) VALUE 0.
 01 PAGE-SIZE			PIC  9(3) VALUE 54.
 PROCEDURE DIVISION.
 MAINLINE.
     PERFORM 100-INITIALIZATION
     PERFORM 110-WRITE-HEADINGS
     PERFORM 200-PROCESSING
     PERFORM 300-TERMINATION

	   STOP RUN.
 100-INITIALIZATION.
     OPEN INPUT INVENTORY-FILE
		OUTPUT PRINT-FILE.
 110-WRITE-HEADINGS.
	   ADD 1 TO WS-PAGE-CNT
	   MOVE WS-PAGE-CNT TO H1-PAGE-NUM.
     MOVE FUNCTION CURRENT-DATE TO SYSTEM-DATE-AND-TIME

	   EVALUATE SYS-DATE-MM
		WHEN 01 MOVE "JAN" TO H1-MONTH-LIT
		WHEN 02 MOVE "FEB" TO H1-MONTH-LIT
		WHEN 03 MOVE "MAR" TO H1-MONTH-LIT
		WHEN 04 MOVE "APR" TO H1-MONTH-LIT
		WHEN 05 MOVE "MAY" TO H1-MONTH-LIT
		WHEN 06 MOVE "JUN" TO H1-MONTH-LIT
		WHEN 07 MOVE "JUL" TO H1-MONTH-LIT
		WHEN 08 MOVE "AUG" TO H1-MONTH-LIT
		WHEN 09 MOVE "SEP" TO H1-MONTH-LIT
		WHEN 10 MOVE "OCT" TO H1-MONTH-LIT
		WHEN 11 MOVE "NOV" TO H1-MONTH-LIT
		WHEN 12 MOVE "DEC" TO H1-MONTH-LIT
	   END-EVALUATE.
	   
	   EVALUATE SYS-TIME-HOURS
		WHEN 00 MOVE "12" TO  H2-TIME-HOURS-LIT
		WHEN 13 MOVE "01" TO  H2-TIME-HOURS-LIT
		WHEN 14 MOVE "02" TO  H2-TIME-HOURS-LIT
		WHEN 15 MOVE "03" TO  H2-TIME-HOURS-LIT
		WHEN 16 MOVE "04" TO  H2-TIME-HOURS-LIT
		WHEN 17 MOVE "05" TO  H2-TIME-HOURS-LIT
		WHEN 18 MOVE "06" TO  H2-TIME-HOURS-LIT
		WHEN 19 MOVE "07" TO  H2-TIME-HOURS-LIT
		WHEN 20 MOVE "08" TO  H2-TIME-HOURS-LIT
 		WHEN 21 MOVE "09" TO  H2-TIME-HOURS-LIT
		WHEN 22 MOVE "10" TO  H2-TIME-HOURS-LIT
		WHEN 23 MOVE "11" TO  H2-TIME-HOURS-LIT
		WHEN 24 MOVE "12" TO  H2-TIME-HOURS-LIT
	   END-EVALUATE.
	   ACCEPT WS-DOW FROM DAY-OF-WEEK 
	       EVALUATE WS-DOW 
		    WHEN 1 MOVE "MON" TO H2-DOW
		    WHEN 2 MOVE "TUE" TO H2-DOW
		    WHEN 3 MOVE "WED" TO H2-DOW
		    WHEN 4 MOVE "THU" TO H2-DOW
		    WHEN 5 MOVE "FRI" TO H2-DOW
		    WHEN 6 MOVE "SAT" TO H2-DOW
		    WHEN 7 MOVE "SUN" TO H2-DOW
	       END-EVALUATE.
*		MOVE SYS-TIME-HOURS   TO H2-TIME-HOURS.
		MOVE SYS-TIME-MINUTES TO H2-TIME-MINUTES.
          MOVE SYS-TIME-SECONDS TO H2-TIME-SECONDS.
		WRITE PRINT-RECORD    FROM HEAD-2 AFTER 1
		MOVE SYS-DATE-CCYY    TO H1-DATE-CCYY.
 		
*   	MOVE SYS-DATE-MM   TO H1-DATE-MM.
 		MOVE SYS-DATE-DD   TO H1-DATE-DD.
          WRITE PRINT-RECORD FROM HEAD-1 AFTER 1
	   MOVE SPACES             TO PRINT-RECORD
		WRITE PRINT-RECORD AFTER 1.
	   MOVE TITLE-LINE-1       TO PRINT-RECORD
		WRITE PRINT-RECORD AFTER ADVANCING 1.
	   MOVE TITLE-LINE-2       TO PRINT-RECORD
		WRITE PRINT-RECORD AFTER ADVANCING 1.	 	
     MOVE SPACES             TO PRINT-RECORD
		WRITE PRINT-RECORD AFTER 1.
	   MOVE 6 TO WS-LINE-CNT.
 200-PROCESSING.
     PERFORM UNTIL EOF-FLAG = 'Y'
         READ INVENTORY-FILE
	       AT END
		   MOVE 'Y' TO EOF-FLAG
         NOT AT END  

             PERFORM 205-PROCESS-A-RECORD    	       
	       END-READ 
	   END-PERFORM.
 205-PROCESS-A-RECORD.
	   IF WS-LINE-CNT > PAGE-SIZE
		 PERFORM 110-WRITE-HEADINGS
	   END-IF
     PERFORM 210-DISPLAY-A-LINE
*	   WRITE PRINT-RECORD FROM DETAIL-LINE AFTER 1.
	   ADD 1 TO WS-LINE-CNT.
 210-DISPLAY-A-LINE.
     	   COMPUTE WS-DOLLAR-VALUE 
			ROUNDED = IR-QTY-ON-HAND  *  IR-UNIT-COST  
	           END-COMPUTE
		           
 		 MOVE IR-ITEM-NBR 
		     TO DL-ITEM-NUM
	         MOVE IR-ITEM-DESCRIPTION
 		     TO DL-ITEM-DESC
	         MOVE IR-QTY-ON-HAND
		     TO DL-QTY-ON-HAND
	         MOVE IR-UNIT-COST
		     TO DL-UNIT-COST
		 MOVE WS-DOLLAR-VALUE 
		     TO DL-DOLLAR-VALUE
           MOVE DETAIL-LINE    TO PRINT-RECORD
		 WRITE PRINT-RECORD AFTER 1.
*	   ADD IR-QTY-ON-HAND    TO WS-QTY-ON-HAND-TOT.
*     ADD IR-REORDER-PT     TO WS-REORDER-PT-TOT.
     COMPUTE WS-UNIT-COST-TOT ROUNDED = WS-DOLLAR-VALUE-TOT / 
				  WS-QTY-ON-HAND-TOT
     END-COMPUTE.
     ADD 1 TO WS-LINE-CNT.
 300-TERMINATION.
     MOVE SPACES TO PRINT-RECORD
		WRITE PRINT-RECORD AFTER 1.
	   MOVE WS-QTY-ON-HAND-TOT   TO TL-QTY-ON-HAND-TOT.
	   MOVE WS-UNIT-COST-TOT     TO TL-UNIT-COST-TOT.
     MOVE WS-DOLLAR-VALUE-TOT TO TL-DOLLAR-VALUE-TOT.
     MOVE TOTAL-LINE TO PRINT-RECORD.
       WRITE PRINT-RECORD AFTER ADVANCING 1.
     CLOSE INVENTORY-FILE
           PRINT-FILE
```

>				  WS-QTY-ON-HAND-TOT

In the above statement you are performing a divide using
WS-QTY-ON-HAND-TOT as your divisor.  However, it contains zero
(initial value) because the statement that would add something to it
is commented out!  Dividing by zero causes black holes to appear in
the universe and computer programs to crash!!



>     ADD 1 TO WS-LINE-CNT.
> 300-TERMINATION.
…[8 more quoted lines elided]…

Steve

##### ↳ ↳ Re: TOTAL-LINE QUESTION

- **From:** "William M. Klein" <wmklein@ix.netcom.com>
- **Date:** 2000-12-15T20:45:44-06:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<91ekvp$ng0$1@nntp9.atl.mindspring.net>`
- **References:** `<20001213200806.12046.00004824@ng-cj1.aol.com> <Oez_5.70734$15.15304406@news1.rdc1.az.home.com>`

```
I may be "overly cautious" - but *in general* - when I code a DIVIDE
statement (either via COMPUTE or DIVIDE) - I either

1) Code an ON SIZE ERROR phrase

2) Code it within an "IF" statement checking for zero

  ***

Some threads in CLC talk about giving the customer what they want, but I
(almost) never believe someone when they tell me a field can't EVER be zero.
(I also am EXTREMELY dubious when a "designer/analyst" tell me that I
specific field can NEVER be greater than some specific value.)  Unless you
are in a "really tight loop," the performance disadvantages of an explicit
ON SIZE ERROR phrase are rarely more significant that "protective coding".
```

Ralph Leiherr

#### ↳ Re: Call a Windows exe Programm

- **From:** "Gael Wilson" <gael.wilson@merant.com>
- **Date:** 2000-12-14T12:46:52
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<91aj1g$1re$1@hyperion.mfltd.co.uk>`

```
Ralph,


"Ralph Leiherr" <leiherr@vwda.de> wrote in message
news:91a5m8$vid$03$1@news.t-online.com...
> Hallo,
>
> first: my compiler is a Micro-Focus Workbench Compiler 4.0.32, my
operating
> system is Windows NT 4.0.
>
> So, I need a call from my program to a exe file. First I use call X"91"
> using Z-Pgm-Result, Z-Pgm-Function, Z-Pgm-Len. And it work�s but the call
> open a DOS-Box in background and I don�t need this.

The reason that the DOS box appears is that the call starts a command
processor to allow DOS commands to be executed as well as executables.

>
> Now my question, how can I call an "window".exe file without a DOS-Box ?


You can do this by using the CBL_EXEC_RUN_UNIT call.

## Thread: Comp2 Data Format — 6 msgs

_Topics: [`Language features and syntax`](topics.md#syntax)_

### Comp2 Data Format

- **From:** "Nick" <Nick@malefica.force9.co.uk>
- **Date:** 2000-12-15T10:13:17
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<t3jroh222sf6fd@corp.supernews.co.uk>`

```
Can anyone tell me how data is actually stored in Comp2 fields?

We are working in a Sco Unix environment and need to retrieve data from
Cobol data files (without using Cobol).  The problem is unpacking data from
some Comp2 fields in these files.

We have written routines (in VB and C) to unpack Comp3 field data as there
seems to be plenty of documentation about how the data is stored for these,
but can't find anything specific about Comp2 fields.

Thanks in anticipation,

Nick Burton
```

#### ↳ Re: Comp2 Data Format

- **From:** "Rick Smith" <ricksmith@aiservices.com>
- **Date:** 2000-12-15T06:18:47-05:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<91cuko$v26$1@news.hitter.net>`
- **References:** `<t3jroh222sf6fd@corp.supernews.co.uk>`

```
The storage format of COMP-2 depends upon the compiler
and the machine on which the data was created.

It is probably floating-point -- equivalent to double in C; but
may be IEEE, IBM, or other and, if IEEE floating-point, may
be either big-endian or little-endian.

More information is required.
------------------
Rick Smith

>Can anyone tell me how data is actually stored in Comp2 fields?

double.

       fourbytesfromdatafile  char[4]
       double value  double

###### ↳ ↳ ↳ Re: Comp2 Data Format

- **From:** "Rick Smith" <ricksmith@aiservices.com>
- **Date:** 2000-12-16T00:04:31-05:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<91et2v$5pq$1@news.hitter.net>`
- **References:** `<t3jroh222sf6fd@corp.supernews.co.uk> <91cuko$v26$1@news.hitter.net> <t3labtaf4f326a@corp.supernews.co.uk>`

```
I think you probably have the answers you need; but I need to
add a standard comment about C structures and COBOL
records.

If you use double within a structure that is intended to be
equivalent to the COBOL record, you will need to be
concerned with structure packing and whether the compiler
can accommodate an improperly aligned field.
------------------
Rick Smith

#### ↳ Re: Comp2 Data Format

- **From:** "Michael Mattias" <michael.mattias@gte.net>
- **Date:** 2000-12-15T11:46:19+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<ewn_5.510$ju6.38514@dfiatx1-snr1.gtei.net>`
- **References:** `<t3jroh222sf6fd@corp.supernews.co.uk>`

```
Nick <Nick@malefica.force9.co.uk> wrote in message
news:t3jroh222sf6fd@corp.supernews.co.uk...
> Can anyone tell me how data is actually stored in Comp2 fields?
>
> We are working in a Sco Unix environment and need to retrieve data from
> Cobol data files (without using Cobol).  The problem is unpacking data
from
> some Comp2 fields in these files.
>
> We have written routines (in VB and C) to unpack Comp3 field data as there
> seems to be plenty of documentation about how the data is stored for
these,
> but can't find anything specific about Comp2 fields.
>

COMP-1 and COMP-2 data are *often* stored as IEEE single and
double-precision floats respectively, but there is no standard method and
the storage is "implementor defined."

As a good example of this, in IBM COBOL for MVS/VM (mainframe) , there is a
system-wide option (I think set through Language Environment) which allows
you to select either FLOAT(IEEE) or FLOAT(NATIVE) as the method of storage
on the system. (You can override this setting on a program by program basis,
but that might upset one or more of your colleagues).

MCM
```

---

#### ↳ Re: does any know how to display bitmap in cobol program?

- **From:** Nigel Eaton <nigele@rcav8r.demon.co.uk>
- **Date:** 2000-12-18T12:04:36+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** alt.cobol,comp.lang.cobol,fj.lang.cobol,umbc.ifsm.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<HXIxB4AU1fP6Iwhz@rcav8r.demon.co.uk>`
- **References:** `<3a39f521.0@news.tm.net.my>`

```
Low,

The bitmap can be created either in the screen section, or in the 
procedure division:

01 MY-SCREEN.
         03 MY-BMP BITMAP LINE 3.45 COL 3.25
                 BITMAP-HANDLE MY-BMP-HANDLE
                 LINES 67 SIZE 120.

or

         DISPLAY BITMAP LINE 12.4 COL 3.25
                 BITMAP-HANDLE MY-BMP-HANDLE
                 LINES 67 SIZE 120.

(for example!)

Before you create the bitmap, you'll need to load the image:

MOVE "..\MYPIC.BMP" TO WS-BITMAP-NAME

CALL "W$BITMAP" USING WBITMAP-LOAD, WS-BITMAP-NAME
                 GIVING MY-BMP-HANDLE.

and you're done.

This is a very quick and dirty explanation, so it's probably not that 
clear. You can get more information from section 5.14 of the user 
interface programming book in the manual set.

I hope this helps!

Best regards

Nigel

>to
…[13 more quoted lines elided]…
>
```

Low:

COBOL sp2 is a 3rd party software product which supports the ability
to embed a 32 bit Active X (OCX) control in your user interface screen
with our SP2OCX32.DLL add-on dynamic link library.

You can obtain charting and graphing OCX controls and embed them into

still controlled by COBOL CALL USING statements.

controls, so it can also be accomplished for older COBOL compilers as

since the late 1980's when Acucobol was first released.  We also

- **From:** "John P Fife" <jfife1@home.com>

```
Bill, Just a question wouldn't it cause less confusion is you just stated
that it is a physical address that is being passed from the calling program
to the called program. This is the reasons the names do not have to match,
you just have to have the same sequence and you should have the same size
otherwise you could wipe out pieces of core storage between the 2 programs.
I know you stated all this it just took a while to digest.

John
"William M. Klein" <wmklein@ix.netcom.com> wrote in message
news:90kkc2$21p$1@slb0.atl.mindspring.net...
> You don't understand the linkage section completely (yet).
>
> The linkage section in a CALLED program (subprogram) matches the storage
> (usually Working-Storage - but also possibly File or other sections) in
the
> CALLING program.  The "matching" is NOT done by name or anything like that
> it.  It is done by "matching" the parameters in the order they appear in
the
> CALL USING statement (in the CALLING program) to those in the Procedure
> Division USING statement (of the called program).  For example, the
…[48 more quoted lines elided]…
> 4) The field descriptions do NOT need to be the same (although the
"length"
> should be).  What happens when this rule is "violated" depends on the
> operating system and the compiler - but it is NOT a good thing to do.
…[41 more quoted lines elided]…
>
```

##### ↳ ↳ Re: Passing Parameters - Error 104

- **From:** "William M. Klein" <wmklein@ix.netcom.com>
- **Date:** 2000-12-16T12:45:09-06:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<91gd6i$7uo$1@slb0.atl.mindspring.net>`
- **References:** `<90k19p$32b$1@nnrp1.deja.com> <90ken5$lov$1@slb1.atl.mindspring.net> <90khou$foh$1@nnrp1.deja.com> <90kkc2$21p$1@slb0.atl.mindspring.net> <Yys_5.70615$15.15180388@news1.rdc1.az.home.com> <91fj7r$157u$1@ulysses.noc.ntua.gr>`

I understand that this would work AS WELL - but so would the original. The
entire point was that you did NOT need to have the Linkage Section items in
the same order as the Procedure Division USING statement. (This doesn't mean
that you shouldn't or can't - but that you don't have to)

### BMS Macro Problem

- **From:** ghobbs@sympatico.ca (G.Hobbs)

```
BMS GURUS:
AM FEELING SOMEWHAT IGNORANT - THOUGHT I KNEW CICS!
BELOW IS A TYPICAL CICS BMS SCREEN.
IT HAS A HEADING LINE, 13 LINES IN THE SAME FORMAT, AND TYPICAL
ESCAPE AND MESSAGE LINES. 3 FIELDS IN THE RECURRING LINES ARE
UPDATABLE.

===================================================
MAP1                         SOME COMPANY                   2000-12-13

FLD1   FIELD2             FIELD3       FIELD4       FIELD5
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

A146   HARRISON     JOHN           N9A 1W9   WINDSOR
A146   JONES            ALLEN          P2S 3E7    HALIFAX
B166   LONSBURY    BETH           13331         DETROIT
   + 10 MORE LINES (same layout)

PF3=>EXIT   PF10=>UPDATE
THESE ARE THE REQUESTED ROWS
===================================================

I NEED TO CODE A BMS MACRO SO THAT THE 13 LINES, WHEN ASSEMBLED,
PRODUCE A COPYBOOK THAT CONTAINS 'OCCURS 13 TIMES' - THEREFORE I
ACCESS 5 FIELDS VIA SUBSCRIPTS AND NOT 65 (5*13) FIELDS BY INDIVIDUAL
FIELD NAMES.

HAVE TRIED:
LOOKING AT THE MANUALS.
THE 'OCCURS' OPTION ON EACH OF THE 5 DFHMDF'S (gruesome).
DO NOT WANT TO USE 'ACCUM PAGING' OPTIONS.
DO NOT WANT TO DEFINE LINES OF LENGTH 79 (BUT OCCURS WORKS).

SO FAR I HAVE CONCLUDED THAT I MUST CODE A DFHMDF FOR EACH FIELD
WHICH I WOULD REALLY LIKE TO AVOID. I THOUGHT A COMBINATION OF
'OCCURS' AND 'GRPNAME' WOULD DO THE TRICK BUT SEEMINGLY THEY ARE
MUTUALLY EXCLUSIVE.
When i worked on a mainframe with SDF i dont remember having any
problem with this but now coding raw BMS, guess i am missing
something.

CAN ANYBODY POINT ME TO A LUMP OF BMS CODE TO ILLUSTRATE A SOLUTION.
MY THANKS IN ADVANCE.

Graham Hobbs
ghobbs@sympatico.ca
```

#### ↳ Re: BMS Macro Problem

- **From:** Liam Devlin <liamddd@optonline.net>
- **Date:** 2000-12-16T04:51:33+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<3A3AF47F.2E6E87B2@optonline.net>`
- **References:** `<3a3a9808.18790389@news1.sympatico.ca>`

```
"G.Hobbs" wrote:
> 
> BMS GURUS:
…[44 more quoted lines elided]…
> ghobbs@sympatico.ca

We REDEFINE the BMS map with our own OCCURS clause in this situation.
Hint, be sure to get the offset to the first redefined field is the same
in your redefinition as in the BMS version, e.g.:

1  MY-MAP  REDEFINES  BMS-MAP.
	5 FILLER			PIC X(177).
	5 MAP-LINE  OCCURS 13 TIMES.
		10 MAP-NAME		PIC X(20).
		10 FILLER		PIC XX.
		10 MAP-FIELD2		PIC ZZ,ZZ9.
etc.

The secret to success here is the FILLER. Give it a shot & come back if
you have any further questions (post what you tried, including the
offsets).

HTH,
LiamD
```

Eileen

## Thread: File compare algorythem/heuristic question — 1 msgs

### Re: File compare algorythem/heuristic question

- **From:** weberm@polaris.net (Ubiquitous)
- **Date:** 2000-12-16T02:22:21+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** alt.cobol,comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<91ejkt$7q2$1@news.utelfla.com>`
- **References:** `<909948$51v$1@news.utelfla.com> <90h5fe$o05$1@nnrp1.deja.com>`

```
In article <90h5fe$o05$1@nnrp1.deja.com>, lcccpiasabird@my-deja.com says:

>What you need is a programming logic book that shows how to process two
>files at once.  Of course they should both be sorted.

That's the first place I looked, but unfortunately, all the books I
browsed described trees, sorting alogorythms, etc.

>Look for a book on Structured Programming Logic.  I still have mine
>from when I went to school.  Occassionally I have looked at it.

Any in particular you could recomend? :-)

For what it's worth, I wound up using a sort with a compound key which
consisted of the "invoice number" and a "record type" field, then
returned the records and used a dummy record to test for when the
invoice number changed...

RETURN SORTREC
       AT END blah blah...

IF SortInvoice NOT = HoldInvoice
   MOVE SortRec TO HoldRec
   IF SortType = A AND HoldType = B
      SortInvoice is not in file B
      END-IF
   IF SortType = B AND HoldType = B
      SortInvoice is not in file B
      END-IF
ELSE
   IF SortType = B AND HoldType = A 
      matching pair found
   ELSE
      error encountered
END-IF.


        "We are about to vote in the last election of the 20th
         century..."    
                                ---Bill Clinton
                                   Las Cruces, New Mexico
                                   November 1, 1996
```

#### ↳ Re: .exe with RM/COBOL-85?

- **From:** "William M. Klein" <wmklein@ix.netcom.com>

```
I will leave others to reply to the question of creating .exe's with RM, but
I did want to "suggest" one thing for your consideration.

Have you tried developing under RM using their "ANSI flagging" facility? My
guess is that if you coded according to the ANSI Standard (not using any
extensions), that you would find it easy (or at least easier) to "port" your
source code to other compilers.

If you have tried this already and it doesn't help, can you give us some
examples of code that compiles and runs correctly under RM but *not* under
CA-Realia?  Also, I would like to mention that CA-Realia doesn't document
(as far as I know) "RM-compatibility".  On the other hand, MERANT (Micro
Focus) *does* provide some RM-emulation/compatibility facilities - and it
MOST certainly provides .exe support (but does include some run-time
charges - depending on how you plan to use them).
```

## Thread: COBOL disk to tape conversion — 6 msgs

### COBOL disk to tape conversion

- **From:** carolcfdny@aol.com (CarolCFDNY)
- **Date:** 2000-12-16T23:56:25+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<20001216185625.04524.00000972@ng-cn1.aol.com>`

```
I work on a non-IBM system.  Currently we get tapes from an IBM site which are
processed by our COBOL compiler.  Now there's a proprosal that we would receive
these files on disk through FTP instead of on tape... but our COBOL compiler
doesn't recognize IBM files on disk, only on tape.  So I'm working on a program
to re-copy those disk files back to tape!  My question is, what marks the end
of a COBOL file?  I know that records consist of a control word which has the
number of bytes in the record then the record ... what control word indicates
the end of a file?

Can anybody help me? ? ? ? ?
```

#### ↳ Re: COBOL disk to tape conversion

- **From:** "William M. Klein" <wmklein@ix.netcom.com>

#### ↳ Re: COBOL disk to tape conversion

- **From:** yukonmama@aol.com (YukonMama)

- **Message-ID:** `<20001216194351.08937.00004490@ng-ca1.aol.com>`

>From: carolcfdny@aol.com  (CarolCFDNY)

or whatever to indicate 'that's all folks'.

#### ↳ Re: COBOL disk to tape conversion

- **From:** "Jerry P" <jerryp@bisusa.com>
- **Date:** 2000-12-17T12:54:09+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<RH2%5.12188$UN1.1323829@newsread2.prod.itd.earthlink.net>`
- **References:** `<20001216185625.04524.00000972@ng-cn1.aol.com>`

```
COBOL does not create a physical end-of-file marker.

End-of-files are the solely a function of the hardware. You cannot
obtain a byte or combination of bytes which can be decoded as an
end-of-file.

Here's the code you want:

OPEN INPUT DISK-FILE.
OPEN OUTPUT TAPE-FILE.
PERFORM WITH NO LIMIT
   READ DISK-FILE
      NOT AT END
         WRITE TAPE-REC FROM DISK-REC
      AT END
         CLOSE DISK-FILE CLOSE TAPE-FILE
         EXIT PERFORM
      END-READ
   END-PERFORM.

We once had a bottle-neck in the keypunch department. Bought an
expensive key-to-tape system. Took the tapes and ran a program to
punch cards from the tapes.

Go figure.


"CarolCFDNY" <carolcfdny@aol.com> wrote in message
news:20001216185625.04524.00000972@ng-cn1.aol.com...
> I work on a non-IBM system.  Currently we get tapes from an IBM site
which are

would receive

compiler

> of a COBOL file?  I know that records consist of a control word
which has the
> number of bytes in the record then the record ... what control word
indicates
> the end of a file?
>
> Can anybody help me? ? ? ? ?

#### ↳ Re: COBOL disk to tape conversion

- **From:** jamesc7460@aol.com (JamesC7460)
- **Date:** 2000-12-19T04:58:33+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<20001218235833.02005.00011191@ng-ch1.aol.com>`
- **References:** `<20001216185625.04524.00000972@ng-cn1.aol.com>`

```
Hi,

One thing to keep in mind is that by default  FTP  translates its output into
line sequential ASCII files which can be a problem if you're used to receiving
your files in fixed record fixed block EBCDIC format.  If EBCDIC is to be sent
untranslated I believe that the send  mode has to be set to BINARY prior to
transmission.  Either that or you need to change your program to read ASCII
line sequential which may or may not be an option depending on the compiler you
use.

Regards,
Jim Castro
```

   are the tapes you are currently getting ascii or ebcdic?
   is the ftp being done in binary or ascii mode?

I think you will find that one set of data is coming one way, the

<a id="t-714a68eb33"></a>
## Thread: Microfocus COBOL/C socket programming? — 2 msgs

_Topics: [`Compilers and vendors`](topics.md#compilers)_

### Microfocus COBOL/C socket programming?

- **From:** markd@bellsouth.net (md2100)
- **Date:** 2000-12-17T13:30:30+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<3a3cbe44.651463995@news1.lig.bellsouth.net>`

```
Anyone attempted using Microfocus COBOL (v3.2) and sockets under Unix?
I need to develop a server program using MF COBOL to get at MF data
files via socket from other environment/language connections (eg,
Java, C, etc).  We have a huge legacy system with gigabytes of MF
COBOL data, and no plans of upgrading to NetExpress.

I realize you can mix C & COBOL under MF, but coming up short on how
to communicate the results of a MF COBOL file operation back to a
driving C socket wrapper (ie, C calling COBOL program).  For example,
if I have a C program that calls COBOL to read a record, how do I pass
the record data _back_ to the C program so it can pass it back across
the socket connection?  Looks like all I can return is a status value.
Would using env variables be an option?

Any help/insight would be greatly appreciated.
```

#### ↳ Re: Microfocus COBOL/C socket programming?

- **From:** lsunley@mb.sympatico.ca
- **Date:** 2000-12-17T17:09:44+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<ZpzG4UNLyRNq-pn2-jqr2Uxepddhl@tcpserver>`
- **References:** `<3a3cbe44.651463995@news1.lig.bellsouth.net>`

```
On Sun, 17 Dec 2000 13:30:30, markd@bellsouth.net (md2100) wrote:

> Anyone attempted using Microfocus COBOL (v3.2) and sockets under Unix?
> I need to develop a server program using MF COBOL to get at MF data
…[12 more quoted lines elided]…
> Any help/insight would be greatly appreciated.


In the C program declare a buff for the data
and pass the address of that buffer to the cobol 
program as a call parameter.

rc  int;
c_buffer char[200];

rc = cobolprogramname(&c_buffer[0])
if (rc) do the stuff with the file data
else you are finished

The COBOL program has to have a linkage section declaring
the parameter and it places the record read in the buffer

working-storage.

01  file-is-open pic 9 value 0.
  88  file-open value 1.

linkage section

01  data-buffer  pic x(200).

procedure division using data-buffer.

    if not file-open
        open file
        move 1 to file-is-open
    end-if.

001-loop.

    read file
       at end go to 002-finish
   end-read.

   move record-area to data-buffer
  exit program returning 1.

002-finished.

    move 0 to file-isopen
    close file
    exit program returning 0.

The program returns a 1 for the return code as long
as file data is returned and a 0 if the file is at end.

Check the documentation to make sure the RETURN-CODE
register is the same as the C int data type.

If you working with ISAM files and you want to obtain
specific records with a key value you will have to
pass the key through another parameter and use 
that for the read, and come up with some return
code convention to indicate a "not found" on the
read.
```

## Thread: Starting.... — 5 msgs

### Starting....

- **From:** Michel <malakoff@sympatico.ca>
- **Date:** 2000-12-17T14:46:31+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<3A3CD1DB.D7D4ADFD@sympatico.ca>`

```
Good morning! Could anyone telle me where I could get some vey basic
informations (like "How to get started?" "Where is the editor?" etc),
like a FAQ of beginners questions before I start harassing you guys with
very basic questions that have already been asked 200000 times....

I am trying to work with Cobol 32, Micro Focus. Thank you in advance.
```

#### ↳ Re: Starting....

- **From:** rjones1005@aol.com (RJones1005)
- **Date:** 2000-12-18T01:01:40+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<20001217200140.07562.00000064@ng-fw1.aol.com>`
- **References:** `<3A3CD1DB.D7D4ADFD@sympatico.ca>`

```
You gotta read some of the getting started stuff in the compiler product
documentation.  At least get down the basic steps to compile then run a
program.

As for editor, the compiler product probably has a built in editor.  Good
compilers have what they call IDE (Integrated Development Environment) when
editing, syntax checking, compiling, running is all done in one place.  I'm
sure MF Cobol has such an IDE.

As for editor you can basically use anything you want.   We use BRIEF, a
good-ol' DOS type editor for programmers, and I like PFE (Programmer File
Editor).  I've even used BBEdit on my Macintosh when working at home.

As for a book, I recommend "Structured COBOL Programming" by Stern & Stern. 
It's a good textbook that explains things clearly.  It sticks to ANSI standard
COBOL.
```

## Thread: CEDF/InterTest Debugging... Thanks Much! — 1 msgs

### CEDF/InterTest Debugging... Thanks Much!

- **From:** docdwarf@clark.net ( NA)
- **Date:** 2000-12-17T14:50:20+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<Mo4%5.5577$Sl.285330@iad-read.news.verio.net>`

```

Greatly appreciated all input on the CEDF/InterTest problem I had for
invoking the debugger for a process, not a transaction (or something like
that).  I was fortunate in that the system always assigned the same
'virtual' terminal to the process I was concerned with so I wound up
setting Intertest to break on that terminal and direct the debug display
to mine, keeping overhead to a minimum.

Thanks much!

DD
```

I kind of expected that response, but we have to emember the point of an
instructor setting an assignment. It is so that the instructor can get
feedback as to how well the students have learned the subject. If
everyone turns in great work the instructor then thinks "Wow! I'm a
great teacher" and then moves on to the next topic. On the other hand if
nobody gets it, then the instructor gets the feedback that they need to
go over the topic again.

So even if you are never going to use COBOL in your future, turning in
someone else's work does the instructor and that instructor's future
students a great disservice.

Sure Usenet is a great place to get assistance if you can demonstrate
that you have done a lot of work yourself, but to ask others to do your
homework for you is not really what Usenet if for.

Pete


BTW How successful were you in getting others to do your C/C++ homework
through eScribe?

Your posts are still online at
http://www.escribe.com/software/generalc/index.html?by=Author&a=Craig%20
S.%20Goldberg
some of the followups make for very interesting reading :-)

I particularly like this response you got back then
++++++++++++
From: John Meyer
Date: Fri, 21 Apr 2000 15:30:34
------------------------------------------------------------------------
--------

My first use for the FAQ:

I want somebody to help with my homework, but I only get smart-ass
remarks?  What gives?

Okay, let's define help here.
Certainly, C++ and C programmers know what its like to be banging your
head against the wall at 2 a.m. in the morning, trying to figure out why
that subroutine or class won't compile properly.  If you've tried and
you tried and you tried and you tried, and then come to help and post
your code, certainly you have a right to get miffed.

 However, most of the time, what it looks like is this:

Dear group:
I have a problem due tomorrow by my dumb teacher who doesn't know
anything and hasn't taught us anything.  Here are the requirements.
Thanks.

See what this looks like?  It looks like plagarism, and programmers
don't like it for several reasons.

First off, it's dishonest on a personal scale.  The teacher may have
been some bum hired off the street giving out last year's assignments,
but you still have an assignment and it's up to you to have the
integrity to do the work.  In the end, you may be the most talented
programmer around, but you sell yourself on your integrity first.  Do
the assignment as best you can, then go to the school and get the
teacher fired if he's such a know-nothing.

More than likely, however, he does know what he's doing, since he was
hired by a university to teach it and universities don't specialize in
hiring people off the street to teach random courses.  It's more than
likely that you didn't understand something he or she said, or you
didn't go to class and take the proper notes.

Secondly, these programmers went to school and did all of the work (many
times, more than what the school did; I'm always assigning myself little
projects) to earn money in this field.  Why would they write a program
for you for free, and let you take the credit, when they earn $200 or
more an hour?

Finally, there's a chance that you will end up with a degree (not
likely, but possible) and out there trying to sell skills that you don't
even have.  And then there's the chance that they'll have to work with
you and will end up doing all of your work then as well.  Or there's the
chance you'll have to design some program that could endanger their
lives, property, or whatever.

With that in mind, here are some guidelines for posting homework
assignments and problems:

* Try the assignment first hand.  Write some pseudocode down, at the
very least, if you don't know what all to do, then write as much code as
you possibly can, filling in the pseudocode

* Post your assignment in reasonable time.  Most people don't check
their e-mail at 3 in the morning looking for some student to help out.
If you don't have it in by 9 your time, don't expect to have the answer
for at least 12 hours, if not more.

* If you have problems for a long time, walk away from the computer and
do something else for an hour or two.  Pounding your head against the
wall after a couple of minutes does nothing but give you a headache and
the wall a dent.

In short, do some code first.
++++++++++++++++

Maybe John's response is longer and kinder than Boris's but the jist is
the same.
```

>screw you....I am never going to use COBOL in my job when I graduate
>anyway..

Never say never...

Anyway, what I've found from learning many different languages is that I learn
to think about problems in different terms.  One tends to think in the
constructs available in a particular language. I know I am a better programmer
because I've taken assembler, FORTRAN, COBOL, Ada, C, C++, Basic, SQL, Dbase. I
never wrote a line of Ada code outside the classroom, but what I learned about
writing code well I learned because of the features and constructs in Ada not
available in COBOL - *yet I am able to apply the ideas and techniques in my
COBOL programming today.
```

#### ↳ Re: Cobol Lab work

There are some questions you could ask in class. Like: "Why do I have
to take this course, I'm a computer information systems major?'

Your professor might answer:

"Somewhere around 70-80% of the code running today is written in
COBOL. Wherever you end up in your career, chances are upwards of 90%
of the production work will have been written in COBOL. At your future
job, probably most of programmers will be creating or maintaining
applications written in COBOL....

'To an information specialist being unfamiliar with COBOL is like
joining the Priesthood without knowing Latin, or trying to be a
carpenter without being able to use a hammer....

He may also answer thus:

'Our purpose is not to make you an expert in COBOL; our purpose is to
teach the techniques of programming, logic, files, record layouts,
human-machine interaction, algorithms, error prediction and analysis,
debugging, and all the hundreds of other facets necessary for a broad
understanding of information technology. COBOL is just a tool to
accomplish this. In this course, COBOL is but a vehicle for the
discovery process, not an end in itself."


Consult the FAQs for this newsgroup and you'll find the conditions
under which many of the regulars will offer assistance in your
project.

```
Though not all schools do, many do require COBOL as part of their
curriculum.  We require a single 3 hour course in File Processing which
uses COBOL as the instructional vehicle.  Some schools require two or
three semesters.  

We spent many hours this past year revising our curriculum.  Part of that
was asking the question of our advisory committee about the role of
COBOL. It was decided to continue to include COBOL as part of the program
for now - while, at the same time, understanding that it will need to be
periodically revisited [:(].

Floyd Johnson

: > > to take this course, I'm a computer information systems major?'
: > >
: > > Your professor might answer:
: > >
: > > "Somewhere around 70-80% of the code running today is written in
: > > COBOL. Wherever you end up in your career, chances are upwards of 90%
: > > of the production work will have been written in COBOL. At your future
: > > job, probably most of programmers will be creating or maintaining
: > > applications written in COBOL....
: > >
: > > 'To an information specialist being unfamiliar with COBOL is like
: > > joining the Priesthood without knowing Latin, or trying to be a
: > > carpenter without being able to use a hammer....
: > >
: > > He may also answer thus:
: > >
: > > 'Our purpose is not to make you an expert in COBOL; our purpose is to
: > > teach the techniques of programming, logic, files, record layouts,
: > > human-machine interaction, algorithms, error prediction and analysis,
: > > debugging, and all the hundreds of other facets necessary for a broad
: > > understanding of information technology. COBOL is just a tool to
: > > accomplish this. In this course, COBOL is but a vehicle for the
: > > discovery process, not an end in itself."
: > >
: > >
: > > Consult the FAQs for this newsgroup and you'll find the conditions
: > > under which many of the regulars will offer assistance in your
: > > project.

### help: adding to an indexed file problem

- **From:** goble@gtech (David. E. Goble)
- **Date:** 2000-12-18T09:21:21+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** alt.cobol,comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<3a3b226f.3154586@news.adelaide.on.net>`

```
Hi all;

I have created a program to create an indexed file from a sequential
file. It has one record.

       FILE-CONTROL.
           SELECT f200-members-file
               ASSIGN TO DISK "data/starters/members.dat"
               ORGANIZATION IS LINE SEQUENTIAL
               ACCESS IS SEQUENTIAL
               FILE STATUS IS w120-file-status.
           SELECT f100-members-file
               ASSIGN TO DISK "data/members.dat"
               ORGANIZATION IS INDEXED
               ACCESS IS RANDOM
               RECORD KEY IS f110-memb-licNo
               ALTERNATE RECORD KEY IS f120-memb-name
               FILE STATUS IS w120-file-status.
       DATA DIVISION.
      ***************
       FILE SECTION.
      *-------------
       FD  f100-members-file
           LABEL RECORDS ARE STANDARD
           RECORD CONTAINS 196 CHARACTERS
           DATA RECORD IS f100-members-rec.

key pic x(07)
name 
	first pic x(14)
	surname pic x(14)

So the indexed file has

temparyChristopher              Surname

I wrote another program to add to the index file. It asks the user for
a first name and surname, then...

           READ f100-members-file
               KEY IS f120-memb-name
               INVALID KEY
                   PERFORM 2100-GET-MORE-DETAILTS
                   PERFORM 2200-WRITE-MEMBER
                   PERFORM 2300-ANYMORE-MEMBERS
               NOT INVALID KEY
                   STRING err1 f110-memb-licNo w120-file-status
                           DELIMITED BY SIZE
                       INTO w990-display-message
                   END-STRING
                   PERFORM 2900-ERROR
           END-READ.

But when I enter the name "Christopher Surname" it does not go thru
the invalid key... code. But acts as if it is comparing the two  index
keys of "   " and "tempary".

As you can see in my selects the alternate key does not have with
duplicates. What am I doing wrong or what do I need to do to get this
to work.


--Regards       David. E. Goble
             goble [AT] kin.net.au
          http://www.kin.net.au/goble
Po Box 648 Kingscote, Kangaroo Island, SA 5223
```

Where is the open statement? did you OPEN I-O or OPEN OUTPUT or what?
Try putting an error control on the open statement to insure it is open
before you do any further processing and make the program display upon
console that it is open or not open.  If it doesnt open do a stop run
and display open error and the status key if it is not open.  Then look
up the status key to see what the status is.  If it is a VSAM indexed
file you need the exact status key value. You have to insure you opened
the file before you can write to it.

###### ↳ ↳ ↳ Re: help: adding to an indexed file problem

- **From:** lcccpiasabird@my-deja.com
- **Date:** 2000-12-22T21:10:46+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** alt.cobol,comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<920g0j$s9j$1@nnrp1.deja.com>`
- **References:** `<3a3b226f.3154586@news.adelaide.on.net> <91oebb$dk6$1@nnrp1.deja.com> <3a421c44.1279696@news.adelaide.on.net>`

```
In article <3a421c44.1279696@news.adelaide.on.net>,
  goble@gtech wrote:

What happens when you get two people named John Smith or something like
that?

Won't you have a duplicate Key???

If the name and a member number were together that would make it unique.
We have one file that has a codex key.  A kind of 5 letter phonetic key
to search the last names that sound the same.  Even that is tied
together with an identification number we just switch the order around
for the alternate key.  The US Census uses this.

I would use one specific key.  Dont describe an alternate key unless
you are using it.  Otherwise, most compilers think you want to use the
alternate key.

I was looking at a write statement from one of our programs it reads
like this:

(first we move new data to a group name in the working storage.)
write record from data-storage-record
    invalid key        perform err-routine(your err routine)

normally if we use the first key we dont mention the alt key.  If you
do the compiler expects you to use the alternate key.  I wrote a
program a while back and I described the alternate key and it wouldn'
allow me to use the primary key.  Your working storage area hould
contain the field with the key.

How  PC record index works I dont have a clue.  I tried a program once
on a pc that used a key and it makes the record index seperate from the
record.  Maybe you have to have a statement saying what the key is when
you write or something.  I just make the key/keys part of the record
(described in working storage) and write the record from that.

Example

---------------------------------
 SELECT CLASS-FILE
   ACCESS IS INDEXED
   RECORD KEY IS CLASS-RK
   ALTERNATE RECORD KEY IS CLASS-AK
   FILE STATUS IS FILE-STATUS.
-------------------------------------
WORKING-STORAGE SECTION.
 01  CL-CLASS-FILE.
     05  CL-KEY        PIC 9(09).
*   ALT KEY
     05  CL-ALT-KEY    PIC X(18).
*   remainder of non-key record
     05  CL-NON-KEY-PART.
         10  CL-FLD-1      PIC 9(05).
         10  CL-FLD-2      PIC X(30).
---------------------------------------
     MOVE WS-SURNAME TO CL-ALT-KEY.
     WRITE CLASS-FILE FROM CL-CLASS-FILE
        INVALID KEY        (your code).
----------------------------------------

A compiler may want something in "both" the alternate and primary key
to write a record.

I don't do many programs with an add to the file, usually the online
programmers do that.  Usually just a rewrite statement to reset
switches.  The IBM book says it just writes the record on the end of
the file.  The key holds the location of the file.



> On Tue, 19 Dec 2000 19:53:19 GMT, lcccpiasabird@my-deja.com wrote:

###### ↳ ↳ ↳ Re: help: adding to an indexed file problem

_(thread depth: 5)_

- **From:** "Peter E. C. Dashwood" <dashwood@enternet.co.nz>
- **Date:** 2000-12-25T15:18:38+13:00
- **Newsgroups:** alt.cobol,comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<926c71$apf$1@hermes.enternet.co.nz>`
- **References:** `<3a3b226f.3154586@news.adelaide.on.net> <91oebb$dk6$1@nnrp1.deja.com> <3a421c44.1279696@news.adelaide.on.net> <920g0j$s9j$1@nnrp1.deja.com> <3a4435ec.8939272@news.adelaide.on.net>`

```

David. E. Goble wrote in message <3a4435ec.8939272@news.adelaide.on.net>...
>On Fri, 22 Dec 2000 21:10:46 GMT, lcccpiasabird@my-deja.com wrote:
>
…[6 more quoted lines elided]…
>My question is simple, WHY!


The answer is also simple, David.

There has to be a logic error. (Or maybe a definition changed between the
version you are running and the version which created the file...)

The fact that the primary key has spaces in it has no bearing on it. You
have correctly defined the Alternate key to be the "Key of Reference".

This apparently exists on the file, but the system is sure that it
doesn't...

Check that the single record on the test file has the correct information in
the Alternate key field. It is not one byte out, or something similar. You
will get an INVALID KEY on READ if the record is not found. It won't be
found if the key on the file doesn't match the key in the program.

This is one reason why it is often better to use a status code where you can
actually see EXACTLY what happened rather than an INVALID KEY "catch-all"

In the snippet you posted you also define "key" and "first" fields. These
are reserved words and will cause unpredictable effects if they get past the
compiler.

If you check the above and it still doesn't work, please mail me the full
source and your test file.

dashwood@enternet.co.nz

Pete.
```

## Thread: Programmer Aptitude Test — 2 msgs

### Re: Programmer Aptitude Test

- **From:** dmazeau@my-deja.com
- **Date:** 2000-12-18T12:26:53+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<91kvqc$glo$1@nnrp1.deja.com>`
- **References:** `<8v3bbc$dgr$1@nnrp1.deja.com> <8v3g83$80b$1@ins21.netins.net> <3A165D18.1CFBE35D@Josella-Simone-Playton.de> <8v5uup$3bt$1@ins21.netins.net> <3a16a749.269742457@207.126.101.100>`

```
In article <3a16a749.269742457@207.126.101.100>,
  thaneH@softwaresimple.com (Thane Hubbell) wrote:
> Tests and the like are often a tool to weed the candidate pool to a
> managable level.  It used to be this was with the Airlines - one HAD
…[9 more quoted lines elided]…
> thing.

In December of 1988, shortly after the elder George Bush beat Michael
Dukakis, I took one of these tests.  Over the years I would say
that test was one "lucky break" for me, and I would also say the
test was not so fair.  It had nothing at all to do with COBOL, but
rather had a lot of strange questions, having to do with logic.
That is, if there where 5 balls of black and red color, with odd
and even numbers on them, and 2 balls of red color where selected
from the set, and they had even numbers on them... et cetera.

I remember halfway through the tests thinking the test was stupid,
and giving up, then five minutes later I decided to look at one
of the questions again, just for fun, because I had nothing else
to do... and I managed to figure that question out. Then I later
went on to answer another question.  Maybe even a third after
that.

In the end I'd imagine that I didn't do well on the test, but I
did better than some others, I am sure, because later they brought
about 7 of us into a small conference room and told us we were
the ones that passed the test.

It was the The Travelers Insurance Companies, in Hartford,
Connecticut.  Later, in January 1989, they put me through a
10 week training course... and that was the start of my COBOL
career.

12 months later I left the company, because I was tired of
Connecticut, and was offered a COBOL job in New York City, doing
securities processing on Wall Street. Actually, Broad Street,
a half block from Wall Street.


Sent via Deja.com
http://www.deja.com/
```

#### ↳ Re: Programmer Aptitude Test

- **From:** Ed Stevens <ed.stevens@home.com>
- **Date:** 2000-12-18T20:47:56+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<91lt5o$abc$1@nnrp1.deja.com>`
- **References:** `<8v3bbc$dgr$1@nnrp1.deja.com> <8v3g83$80b$1@ins21.netins.net> <3A165D18.1CFBE35D@Josella-Simone-Playton.de> <8v5uup$3bt$1@ins21.netins.net> <3a16a749.269742457@207.126.101.100> <91kvqc$glo$1@nnrp1.deja.com>`

```
In article <91kvqc$glo$1@nnrp1.deja.com>,
  dmazeau@my-deja.com wrote:
<snippage>

> In December of 1988, shortly after the elder George Bush beat Michael
> Dukakis, I took one of these tests.  Over the years I would say
…[6 more quoted lines elided]…
>
<snippage>

That's very similar to how I got into the business in '80.  A state
civil service comission (operating much like the federal civil service)
had a posting for a "Computer Programmer/Analyst Trainee" with
qualifications being any 4-year degree and a qualifying score on a
battery of aptitude tests.  All but one of the tests had nothing to do
with computers or programming.  They dealt with logic (like your
example), abstract thinking, pattern recognition, and reading
comprehension.  These are fundamental aptitudes that all programmers
must have and probably can't be effectively taught.  If a person has
these qualities, he can be taught the techniques and technology.  If he
doesn't have these qualities, he probably should seek a career in
another field.  I still think the use of these kinds of tests is valid.
```

<a id="t-fd9df64597"></a>
## Thread: Variable names in text strings — 4 msgs

### Variable names in text strings

- **From:** "Hillel" <hss@larich.com>
- **Date:** 2000-12-18T10:09:00-05:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<t3sa9bk7jbqb24@corp.supernews.com>`

```
Hello Everyone,

I am using Micro Focus COBOL in SCO OpenServer.
If I have the name of a variable in a text string (the value
of another variable), is there any way to then get or use its value?
I have a paragraph that needs to be used the same way
on several different variables, and there is not an opportunity
to move anything to a work variable for that function before
performing it.  I do have a way while in the paragraph to
get the names of those variables as text strings.

Thanks.
```

#### ↳ Re: Variable names in text strings

- **From:** "William M. Klein" <wmklein@ix.netcom.com>
- **Date:** 2000-12-18T11:58:41-06:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<91lj60$p2q$1@slb7.atl.mindspring.net>`
- **References:** `<t3sa9bk7jbqb24@corp.supernews.com>`

```
This is DEFINITELY not a direct answer to the coding issue that you ask
about, but it *might* provide a way to do what you want.

Have you looked at "nested programs"?  If you pass the "relevant" variables
from each location to the nested program, it could do the "common" action.
If there is a "medium small" number of fields that might need this action,
you could code something like:

  Evaluate Variable-name
   When "field1"
      Call Nested-Pgm Using Field1
    When "field2"
       Call Nested-Pgm Using Field2
         ...
     When Other
        Display "unknown field"
   End-Evaluate
```

##### ↳ ↳ Re: Variable names in text strings

- **From:** "Hillel" <hss@larich.com>
- **Date:** 2000-12-18T14:06:43-05:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<t3so70tl2sf4c7@corp.supernews.com>`
- **References:** `<t3sa9bk7jbqb24@corp.supernews.com> <91lj60$p2q$1@slb7.atl.mindspring.net>`

```
Thanks, but calling a subprogram will not work in this case.
This might seem a little strange, but in this case I need to
use a "PERFORM" for this routine and not a "CALL".

---Hillel
```

###### ↳ ↳ ↳ Re: Variable names in text strings

- **From:** "William M. Klein" <wmklein@ix.netcom.com>
- **Date:** 2000-12-18T13:24:13-06:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<91lo6d$8ik$1@slb7.atl.mindspring.net>`
- **References:** `<t3sa9bk7jbqb24@corp.supernews.com> <91lj60$p2q$1@slb7.atl.mindspring.net> <t3so70tl2sf4c7@corp.supernews.com>`

```
My next suggestion is even MORE of a stretch.  Partially, I don't fully
understand why you don't move the "relevant" fields to a working-copy,
Perform the "logic" and then move the working copy back to the original.
However, if there is a reason for avoiding this, let me try another (fairly
obscure) method - that relies on an extension that your compiler PROBABLY
has.

1) Define a field in Linkage Section (but don't put it in your Procedure
Division USING statement) that can "hold" the actual data to be processed.

2) Where (in your logic) you want to perform the "common logic" - place a
    Set Address of Linkage-Section-Item to Address of Real-Item (using an
EVALUATE as in my first example to figure out which data-item to use)
    Perform logic-routine (working on the Linkage Section "copy" of the
data)

     ***

After this is performed the "original" item will already be "modified" to
the new value.
```

## Thread: NetExpress and Win32 spooler — 2 msgs

### NetExpress and Win32 spooler

- **From:** "Giancarlo" <gcan@libero.it>
- **Date:** 2000-12-18T20:38:01+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<JAu%5.133720$hk4.4832816@news.infostrada.it>`

```
I'm using NetExpress 3.0 (Demo version) and Windows 98 second edition. I
wrote a program that generate a report using the report writer, and send the
output directly to the printer port. The length of the report lines is 200
characters, the printer is a Lexmark 2381 plus (a dot matrix printer) and
the program works fine, but if I use the run-time tunable
"printer_redirection", to redirect the output through the Win32 print
spooler using the "generic text only" driver, the program works fine only if
the length of the report line is less than 149 characters. Characters from
column 149 are LOST. I do not think it is a problem of the printer driver,
because I tryed to print a line made of 200 characters from the NOTEPAD of
Windows and it is all OK.

Any help would be greatly appreciated.

Giancarlo Angelini (Italy)
e-mail: gcan@libero.it
```

					SIGN TRAILING SEPARATE.
 01 WS-PAGE-CNT			PIC 9(3) VALUE ZERO.
 01 WS-LINE-CNT			PIC 9(3) VALUE 56.
 01 WS-PAGE-SIZE			PIC 9(3) VALUE 54.
 PROCEDURE DIVISION.
 MAINLINE.
     PERFORM 100-INITIALIZATION
     
     PERFORM 200-PROCESSING

     PERFORM 300-TERMINATION

	   STOP RUN.
 100-INITIALIZATION.
     OPEN INPUT INVENTORY-FILE
		OUTPUT PRINT-FILE.
 110-WRITE-HEADINGS.
     ADD 1 TO WS-PAGE-CNT
	   MOVE WS-PAGE-CNT TO H1-PAGE-NUM
     MOVE FUNCTION CURRENT-DATE TO SYSTEM-DATE-AND-TIME

	   EVALUATE SYS-DATE-MM
		WHEN 01 MOVE "JAN" TO H1-MONTH-LIT
		WHEN 02 MOVE "FEB" TO H1-MONTH-LIT
		WHEN 03 MOVE "MAR" TO H1-MONTH-LIT
		WHEN 04 MOVE "APR" TO H1-MONTH-LIT
		WHEN 05 MOVE "MAY" TO H1-MONTH-LIT
		WHEN 06 MOVE "JUN" TO H1-MONTH-LIT
		WHEN 07 MOVE "JUL" TO H1-MONTH-LIT
		WHEN 08 MOVE "AUG" TO H1-MONTH-LIT
		WHEN 09 MOVE "SEP" TO H1-MONTH-LIT
		WHEN 10 MOVE "OCT" TO H1-MONTH-LIT
		WHEN 11 MOVE "NOV" TO H1-MONTH-LIT
		WHEN 12 MOVE "DEC" TO H1-MONTH-LIT
	   END-EVALUATE.
	   
	   EVALUATE SYS-TIME-HOURS
		WHEN 00 MOVE "12" TO  H2-TIME-HOURS-LIT
		WHEN 01 MOVE "01" TO  H2-TIME-HOURS-LIT
		WHEN 02 MOVE "02" TO  H2-TIME-HOURS-LIT
		WHEN 03 MOVE "03" TO  H2-TIME-HOURS-LIT
		WHEN 04 MOVE "04" TO  H2-TIME-HOURS-LIT
 		WHEN 05 MOVE "05" TO  H2-TIME-HOURS-LIT
		WHEN 06 MOVE "06" TO  H2-TIME-HOURS-LIT
		WHEN 07 MOVE "07" TO  H2-TIME-HOURS-LIT
          WHEN 08 MOVE "08" TO  H2-TIME-HOURS-LIT
		WHEN 09 MOVE "09" TO  H2-TIME-HOURS-LIT
          WHEN 10 MOVE "10" TO  H2-TIME-HOURS-LIT
 		WHEN 11 MOVE "11" TO  H2-TIME-HOURS-LIT
		WHEN 12 MOVE "12" TO  H2-TIME-HOURS-LIT
		WHEN 13 MOVE "01" TO  H2-TIME-HOURS-LIT
		WHEN 14 MOVE "02" TO  H2-TIME-HOURS-LIT
		WHEN 15 MOVE "03" TO  H2-TIME-HOURS-LIT
		WHEN 16 MOVE "04" TO  H2-TIME-HOURS-LIT
		WHEN 17 MOVE "05" TO  H2-TIME-HOURS-LIT
		WHEN 18 MOVE "06" TO  H2-TIME-HOURS-LIT
		WHEN 19 MOVE "07" TO  H2-TIME-HOURS-LIT
		WHEN 20 MOVE "08" TO  H2-TIME-HOURS-LIT
 		WHEN 21 MOVE "09" TO  H2-TIME-HOURS-LIT
		WHEN 22 MOVE "10" TO  H2-TIME-HOURS-LIT
		WHEN 23 MOVE "11" TO  H2-TIME-HOURS-LIT
		WHEN 24 MOVE "12" TO  H2-TIME-HOURS-LIT
	   END-EVALUATE.
	   ACCEPT WS-DOW FROM DAY-OF-WEEK 
	       EVALUATE WS-DOW 
		    WHEN 1 MOVE "MON" TO H2-DOW
		    WHEN 2 MOVE "TUE" TO H2-DOW
		    WHEN 3 MOVE "WED" TO H2-DOW
		    WHEN 4 MOVE "THU" TO H2-DOW
		    WHEN 5 MOVE "FRI" TO H2-DOW
		    WHEN 6 MOVE "SAT" TO H2-DOW
		    WHEN 7 MOVE "SUN" TO H2-DOW
	       END-EVALUATE.
		MOVE SYS-TIME-MINUTES TO H2-TIME-MINUTES.
          MOVE SYS-TIME-SECONDS TO H2-TIME-SECONDS.
		WRITE PRINT-RECORD    FROM HEAD-2 AFTER PAGE.
		MOVE SYS-DATE-CCYY    TO H1-DATE-CCYY.
 		MOVE SYS-DATE-DD      TO H1-DATE-DD.
          WRITE PRINT-RECORD    FROM HEAD-1 AFTER 1.
	   MOVE SPACES                TO PRINT-RECORD
		WRITE PRINT-RECORD    AFTER 1.
	   MOVE TITLE-LINE-1          TO PRINT-RECORD
		WRITE PRINT-RECORD    AFTER ADVANCING 1.
	   MOVE TITLE-LINE-2          TO PRINT-RECORD
		WRITE PRINT-RECORD    AFTER ADVANCING 1.	 	
     MOVE SPACES                TO PRINT-RECORD
		WRITE PRINT-RECORD    AFTER 1.
     MOVE 6 TO WS-LINE-CNT.
 200-PROCESSING.
     PERFORM UNTIL EOF-FLAG = 'Y'
         READ INVENTORY-FILE
	       AT END
		   MOVE 'Y' TO EOF-FLAG
         NOT AT END   
                PERFORM 205-PROCESS-A-RECORD 	       
	       END-READ 
	   END-PERFORM.
 205-PROCESS-A-RECORD.
     IF WS-LINE-CNT > WS-PAGE-SIZE
		PERFORM 110-WRITE-HEADINGS
	   END-IF.
	   COMPUTE IR-DOLLAR-VALUE ROUNDED = IR-QTY-ON-HAND * IR-UNIT-COST
	   END-COMPUTE.
     PERFORM 210-DISPLAY-A-LINE.
     ADD 1 TO WS-LINE-CNT.
  
 210-DISPLAY-A-LINE.     
 		 MOVE IR-ITEM-NBR 
		     TO DL-ITEM-NUM
	         MOVE IR-ITEM-DESCRIPTION
 		     TO DL-ITEM-DESC
	         MOVE IR-QTY-ON-HAND
		     TO DL-QTY-ON-HAND
*	         MOVE IR-REORDER-PT
*		     TO DL-REORDER-PT
*	         MOVE WS-QTY-TO-REORDER
*		     TO DL-QTY-TO-REORDER
		 MOVE IR-UNIT-COST TO
			DL-UNIT-COST.
*		 MOVE IR-DOLLAR-VALUE TO
*			DL-DOLLAR-VALUE
       MOVE DETAIL-LINE    TO PRINT-RECORD
		 WRITE PRINT-RECORD AFTER 1.
	   ADD IR-QTY-ON-HAND    TO WS-QTY-ON-HAND-TOT.
*     ADD IR-REORDER-PT     TO WS-REORDER-PT-TOT.
*     COMPUTE WS-QTY-TO-REORDER-TOT = WS-REORDER-PT-TOT - WS-QTY-ON-HAND-TOT
*     END-COMPUTE.
	   ADD 1 TO WS-LINE-CNT. 
 300-TERMINATION.
     MOVE SPACES TO PRINT-RECORD
		WRITE PRINT-RECORD AFTER 1.
	   MOVE WS-QTY-ON-HAND-TOT    TO TL-QTY-ON-HAND-TOT.
	   MOVE WS-DOLLAR-VALUE-TOT   TO TL-DOLLAR-VALUE-TOT.
*	   MOVE WS-REORDER-PT-TOT     TO TL-REORDER-PT-TOT.
*	   MOVE WS-QTY-TO-REORDER-TOT TO TL-QTY-TO-REORDER-TOT.
     MOVE TOTAL-LINE TO PRINT-RECORD.
       WRITE PRINT-RECORD AFTER ADVANCING 1.
     CLOSE INVENTORY-FILE
           PRINT-FILE
	   .
```

#### ↳ Re: ANOTHER TOTAL-LINE QUESTION

- **From:** mike__c@my-deja.com
- **Date:** 2000-12-19T09:33:03+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<91na0f$egd$1@nnrp1.deja.com>`
- **References:** `<20001218185846.12040.00005458@ng-cj1.aol.com>`

```
In article <20001218185846.12040.00005458@ng-cj1.aol.com>,
  deek40@aol.com (Deek40) wrote:

> Deek

You haven't said which fields you are having trouble with, but as
someone suggested in a reply to your original post, put lots of DISPLAYs
in your program to see what values your problem fields have.

Put the DISPLAYs in whenever a field you are having trouble with is
being moved or changing to verify that it's happening correctly - you
what to trace the journey of a field from the input file through working
storage to the output file.

>
> 	   ACCEPT WS-DOW FROM DAY-OF-WEEK
…[8 more quoted lines elided]…
> 	       END-EVALUATE.

Don't know if you are having trouble with any of your EVALUATE
statements, but it's always advisable to code the WHEN OTHER bit even if
you think it'll never happen, e.g. WHEN OTHER DISPLAY "WS-DOW not
between 1 and 7 " WS-DOW


Sent via Deja.com
http://www.deja.com/
```

#### ↳ Re: ANOTHER TOTAL-LINE QUESTION

- **From:** lcccpiasabird@my-deja.com
- **Date:** 2000-12-19T16:43:30+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<91o37g$2qr$1@nnrp1.deja.com>`
- **References:** `<20001218185846.12040.00005458@ng-cj1.aol.com>`

```



  In article <20001218185846.12040.00005458@ng-cj1.aol.com>,
  deek40@aol.com (Deek40) wrote:

When you round numbers you can get bad results.
I noticed you were rounding.
There are much easier ways to handle the time.  like subtracting 12
based on an if condition!!!!

You can also put the months in one field and then redefining the field
to occur 12 times and then subscripting them out.  I hope your teacher
is teaching you how to use subscripting, if not don't mess with that
part.

I suggest you read your book.  Totals are easy.  You compute the
result, move it to the total and then move it to the total counter.

Important!
If you are computing a rounded amount you need to compute it unrounded,
move it to the total field and then compute it rounded and move it to
the printline, so you don't lose anything in the rounding process. Then
you can round it at the bottom if you want.  The rounded values may not
add up so you can not check it that way.  I suggest making the report
without rounding and then you can check it and then add in the rounding
as an extra step.  When facing a complex problem slve it one step at a
time use an extra field that you can comment out in the printline to
test your results.

explanation.

HAND-TOT
> *     END-COMPUTE.
> 	   ADD 1 TO WS-LINE-CNT.
