#### ↳ Re: ANOTHER TOTAL-LINE QUESTION

- **From:** rjones1005@aol.com (RJones1005)
- **Date:** 2000-12-23T04:50:18+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<20001222235018.03963.00006061@ng-ct1.aol.com>`
- **References:** `<20001218185846.12040.00005458@ng-cj1.aol.com>`

```
>205-PROCESS-A-RECORD.
>     IF WS-LINE-CNT > WS-PAGE-SIZE
…[11 more quoted lines elided]…
> 		     TO D


Deek, don't mix scope terminatores (END-IF, END-<whatever>) and periods.  You
will eventually run into trouble.  I'm not saying this is the problem with your
program however.  Either use periods or use scope terminators, but not both.
```

```
Yes, but no.

things and be consequent. Also make things easy for the people who have to
modify your program (it might be you).
```

```
Deek40 wrote:

> ok, the strangest thing i have learned with programming so far is that everyone
> has a different opinion or tells me a different thing to do or not to do.

There is no single right method - otherwise we could automate the process.  But
figure out where we are all coming from, and remember even contradictory
suggestions for when you are working with real world problems.  If you know why we
make certain suggestions, you can use them, or variations of them to help you (and
use your employers standards as well)
```

#### ↳ Re: Differences between Cobol and Cobol II (Mainframe)

- **From:** scomstock@aol.com (S Comstock)
- **Date:** 2000-12-19T14:17:49+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<20001219091749.10509.00001899@ng-fn1.aol.com>`
- **References:** `<ps9t3tc1gu0tp1gta1i3of94enatj6mivj@4ax.com>`

```
 nigel@gofree.to writes ...

>Can anyone point me to an IBM Publication or can tell me the
>difference between Cobol and Cobol II.
>


Here is a summary of our course "Beyond COBOL II" which covers what's new after
OS/VS COBOL. This two day course covers:

* COBOL II changes
  - mixed-case code, unnamed filler
  - packed-decimal, binary data types
  - changes to tables (sizes, dimensions, intialization)
  - reference modification and hex literals
  - pointers and addresses
  - nested programs
  - passing BY CONTENT
  - scope terminators (END-IF, etc.)
  - in-line PERFORM
  - SET ... TO TRUE construct
  - CONTINUE statement
  - INITIALIZE statement
  - EVALUATE statement
* COBOL/370 (V1R1) changes (mostly intrinsic functions)
* Brief introduction to LE (Language Environment), including 
  - full discussion of date and time LE services
  - overview of all services
  - sample code for condition handling and dynamic storage allocation
* COBOL for MVS & VM (V1R2) changes (mostly enhanced C interoperability)
  - Null-terminated literals
  - Euro support
  - local-storage section
  - recursive programs
  - RETURNING option on call and procedure header
  - pass arguments BY VALUE
  - introduction to Object Oriented COBOL
* COBOL for OS/390 & VM (V2R1) changes
  - DLL support
  - new intrinsic functions
  - new options for ACCEPT
  - Millenium Language Extensions (optional)
* COBOL for OS/390 & VM (V2R2) changes
  - ADDRESS OF for working-storage
  - comp-5 data
  - 31-digit numbers
  - line sequential files
  - OS/390 UNIX support
  - SQL co-processor support

Includes four hands on exercises.

That should get application programmers up to speed quickly.

More detail on our website: http://www.trainersfriend.com


Regards,


Steve Comstock
Telephone: 303-393-8716
www.trainersfriend.com
email: steve@trainersfriend.com
256-B S. Monaco Parkway
Denver, CO 80224
USA
```

```
If you are just now looking at these differences, are you aware that VS
COBOL II will "go out of service" in 3 months?  This is an (almost) obsolete
compiler.  It doesn't include intrinsic functions or much support for
4-digit years.  The current "strategic" IBM COBOL compiler is "IBM COBOL for
OS/390 & VM".  It has its own migration guide, if you are interested in
that.
```

```
Rexm:

The best place to get an inexpensive compiler or to learn how to write
COBOL code is to buy Thane Hubbell's book, "Teach Yourself COBOL In 24
Hours!"

The book only costs about $20.00 US$ and includes the compiler at no
additional charge.

It is not only a great book, but also incudes 16 and 32 bit versions
of the Fujitsu COBOL compiler.  The ISBN number of Thane's book is:

0-672-31453-3

You can buy the book on-line at:

http://www.chapters.ca
http://www.indigo.ca
http://www.hasting.com
http://www.bookpool.com
http://www.barnesandnoble.com
http://www.amazon.com
```

#### ↳ Re: How does COBOL differ with VB / Delphi?

- **From:** cauldronuk@aol.com (CauldronUK)
- **Date:** 2000-12-19T14:08:01+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol


#### ↳ Re: How does COBOL differ with VB / Delphi?

- **From:** Calvin Crumrine <Calvin_Crumrine@dced.state.ak.us>
- **Date:** 2000-12-19T14:03:45-09:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<3A3FE951.ABBDAA67@dced.state.ak.us>`
- **References:** `<t3tsivlbmle812@corp.supernews.com>`

```
As a COBOL programmer switching to VB I'd say that it depends on the
application. One I just finished had 2 parts, a data entry part and an
extract/report part. The extract/report part was remarkably similar to
COBOL but the data entry part was (and, frustratingly still is) an entirely
different beast.

VB is event driven, but for an extract/report program the only true event
is starting it. (maybe selecting the criteria if it's variable criteria,
but the more variable it is the more the focus changes to the user choosing
the criteria vs. the program generating the report.)

I've never worked with Delphi but I assume it would be similar, i.e. if a
program lends itself to sequential processing then you code it sequentially
and it ends up similar to COBOL. If it takes event-driven processing then
you write it that way and it ends up quite a bit differently.

rexm@magicgroup.net wrote:

> How does COBOL differ with VB / Delphi?
>
…[8 more quoted lines elided]…
> http://www.help.com/
```

<a id="t-1a0d9f375c"></a>
## Thread: cobol lab work — 1 msgs

### re: cobol lab work

- **From:** eoyore <secret@aol.com>
- **Date:** 2000-12-18T23:57:16-08:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<3A3F14DC.9861E087@aol.com>`

```
I will take cobol in the spring and I don't care if I 
ever use it again after that. Cobol is a Computer Information
Systems AAS degree course at the college I'm attending.  Wait until you
have to take an Object Oriented programming Course.  You will wish you
were in cobol.  In the object oriented Language Delphi
and other object oriented languages, you will come across
pointer variables.

Let me tell you about pointer variables Craig.
Say I have a class named TMiddleFinger.
I create a new instance of this class on the form.

procedure;
var
PointAtCraig: TmiddleFinger;
 
begin
PointAtCraig:= TmiddleFinger.Create;
end;

TmiddleFinger is the new object based on the class and PointAtCraig
is the pointer variable.

See how easy that it? Actually Craig I don't think
it stays that easy for long.  That is why you shouldn't
alienate yourself from the newsgroups by displaying a 
negative attitude.  You will need help unless your a 
genius.

good luck
Eoyore & Friends
```

---

## Thread: cobol lab work — 1 msgs

### re: cobol lab work

- **From:** eoyore <secret@aol.com>
- **Date:** 2000-12-19T00:01:03-08:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<3A3F15BF.59EA5E36@aol.com>`

```
I will take cobol in the spring and I don't care if I 
ever use it again after that. Cobol is a Computer Information
Systems AAS degree course at the college I'm attending.  Wait until you
have to take an Object Oriented programming Course.  You will wish you
```

###### ↳ ↳ ↳ Re: cobol lab work

- **From:** rjones1005@aol.com (RJones1005)
- **Date:** 2000-12-23T04:43:27+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<20001222234327.03963.00006059@ng-ct1.aol.com>`
- **References:** `<3A420E9B.D7C52365@brazee.net>`

```
>If I were hiring a CoBOL programmer, it would be a plus if I saw that the
>applicant was familiar with other languages.

It's more than a plus IMHO.  If you ever want to have the attitude that "I am a
professional programmer" then you should think of COBOL as merely a tool. I
other words, I am not a COBOL programmer, I am a programmer who uses COBOL to
craft solutions to problems and tasks. 

I have seen "COBOL programmers", 15 - 20 years programming computers and they
didn't understand squat about variable types, parameter passing, scope, etc.
etc.  God help them if they ever loose their current jobs.  When we took an
overview course on Ada, I was appalled that they simply did not understand this
stuff.

Second, professional programming goes beyond simply learning the syntax of yet
another programming language.  A language does not a decent programmer make. 
And experience is meaningless in this context too.  Those same said "highly
experienced" programmers I talked about didn't understand diddly about
structured programming.  Have you ever heard "maximize cohesion and minimize
coupling?" If not you better find out darn quick (I suggest "Code Complete" by
Steve McConnell).

I was hired 2 years ago into a COBOL shop that was primarily a maintenance
shop.  Honest to God I had not written a line of COBOL code in almost 20 years
when I was hired.  Yet I recently finished rewriting THE program from hell, a
notoriously awful program that no one, not even the ones who have been at this
place 23+ years and understood the accounting system inside and out could deal
with.  Why?  The fact that they'd been using a COBOL 85 compiler for 5 years (7
now) and NO ONE knew any COBOL 85 (and still don't), only the old COBOL 74
standard, is a big clue.  30 years of programming unhindered by progress. 
COBOL is not a dead language, it only looks like it when you meet the
experienced, but utterly stagnent programmers using it.  Forgive me if this
sounds like bragging (well, I am damn proud of my work) but this really makes
the point.

If you are not constantly learning new stuff about the *craft* of programming,
you're dead meat.  And when you define your self in terms of "I'm a <insert a
language here> programmer" you automatically and subconsciously limit yourself.
 Beware.
```

```
1PP 5648-A25 IBM COBOL for OS/390 & VM  2.1.1
```

#### ↳ Re: IGYPS2112-E message after WRITE

- **From:** "William M. Klein" <wmklein@ix.netcom.com>
- **Date:** 2000-12-19T13:43:12-06:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<91odm0$sql$1@slb7.atl.mindspring.net>`
- **References:** `<3a3f8a10$1001$tfs$mr2ice@news>`

```
Someone CORRECTLY indicated that the problem was the period after column 72.
Moving just the period to a new line would fix it - or you could add an
END-SEARCH statement followed by a period.

The reason that the older compiler handled this was that the next line was a
paragraph-header and the OLDER compiler often (not quite always) assumed a
period before paragraph headers.

Without the period (and without an END-SEARCH), the SEARCH statement is a
conditional statement- and is nested in an "AT END" phrase where an
imperative statement is required.
```

##### ↳ ↳ Re: IGYPS2112-E message after WRITE

- **From:** rjones1005@aol.com (RJones1005)
- **Date:** 2000-12-23T04:12:19+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<20001222231219.03963.00006052@ng-ct1.aol.com>`
- **References:** `<91odm0$sql$1@slb7.atl.mindspring.net>`

```
>Someone CORRECTLY indicated that the problem was the period after column
>72.
>Moving just the period to a new line would fix it - or you could add an
>END-SEARCH statement followed by a period.

IMHO don't go mixing scope terminators and periods.  I use scope-terminators
exclusively and use periods only at the end of paragraph names and at the end
of paragraphs (COBOL 85 ANSI STANDARD requirement).  The problem with periods
is that you will inadvertentaly end up terminating everything, and they may not
be what you intend.  And I guarantee you will get all mucked up if you go
mixing these with IFs.

In this case the END-SEARCH is sufficient.  You do not need to terminate the
write w/ END-WRITE, or a period.

To terminate a paragraph I always use CONTINUE.  (period at the end).  It's big
and it stands out. In this  way when I'd editing code I don't mess up and get
the period in the wrong place when cutting/pasting (for example).
```

###### ↳ ↳ ↳ Re: IGYPS2112-E message after WRITE

- **From:** "William M. Klein" <wmklein@ix.netcom.com>
- **Date:** 2000-12-23T13:37:00-06:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<922uqo$o33$1@slb7.atl.mindspring.net>`
- **References:** `<91odm0$sql$1@slb7.atl.mindspring.net> <20001222231219.03963.00006052@ng-ct1.aol.com>`

```
The original program had the period in column 73 JUST BEFORE A
PARAGRAPH-NAME, therefore, having SOME period is required.  You may do (as
you say later) a CONTINUE with a period - but many would view this as
"over-kill".  If you did take that approach, then you would need BOTH an
END-SEARCH and an END-WRITE (as the sample had nested conditionals - which
would ALL be terminated by a period).  Actually, I think that coding both
terminators would be a "good" thing - but using the single period would also
solve the "original" problem.

NOTE: The original "question" was also a case of someone working with '74
Standard code - just now moving to an '85 Standard compiler.  THEREFORE,
there were probably NO expolict scope terminators in the source, so the
"period" solution would be most consistent with the original code.  However,
you would only "know" that it was a '74 compiler - if you knew IBM mainframe
compiler versions/releases.

NOTE2:  I do not (at all) disagree with the "general" view of using ALL
explicit scope terminators with a single period per paragraph.  However,
that may be a "problem" if trying to do "minimal" maintenance on an existing
'74 Standard source program.
```

###### ↳ ↳ ↳ Re: IGYPS2112-E message after WRITE

_(thread depth: 4)_

- **From:** rjones1005@aol.com (RJones1005)
- **Date:** 2000-12-24T04:56:10+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<20001223235610.12555.00001413@ng-fv1.aol.com>`
- **References:** `<922uqo$o33$1@slb7.atl.mindspring.net>`

```
>NOTE2:  I do not (at all) disagree with the "general" view of using ALL
>explicit scope terminators with a single period per paragraph.  However,
>that may be a "problem" if trying to do "minimal" maintenance on an existing
>'74 Standard source program.

I agree. The behaviour of statment termination is different using periods and
scope-terminators.  The best example is compound ifs - we've all seen them -
and we've all seen massive compounded and IF ELSE IF statments all terminated
with a single period at the end.  Using scope terminators there must be one for
each IF. And BTW, that's a good thing.  I've been able to successfully
"maintain" some lousy IF code because replacing periods with END-IFs gave me
better control over what code was inside of what IF.

When I do maintenance, I do not replace existing periods with scope terminators
unless absolutely necessary.  It might be necessary if I were, for example, to
wrap the existing code inside a PERFORM loop.  That existing period would
incorrectly terminate the perform loop.

I do how ever use all scope terminators on all new code.
```

###### ↳ ↳ ↳ Re: IGYPS2112-E message after WRITE

- **From:** Howard Brazee <howard@brazee.net>
- **Date:** 2000-12-27T07:22:11-07:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<3A49FB13.269D2DD3@brazee.net>`

```
> IMHO don't go mixing scope terminators and periods.  I use scope-terminators
> exclusively and use periods only at the end of paragraph names and at the end
…[3 more quoted lines elided]…
> mixing these with IFs.

I've seen you say that a few times.  I have an environment where I have to use

IDMS code.  (I also feel comfortable with full stop periods within paragraphs).
But there is no way I am going to give up my scope terminators.

environment where everybody uses periods.
```

- **From:** "William M. Klein" <wmklein@ix.netcom.com>

- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<92da66$fj2$1@slb7.atl.mindspring.net>`

```
"Howard Brazee" <howard@brazee.net> wrote in message
news:3A49FB13.269D2DD3@brazee.net...
>
> RJones1005 wrote:
>
> > IMHO don't go mixing scope terminators and periods.  I use
scope-terminators
> > exclusively and use periods only at the end of paragraph names and at
the end
> > of paragraphs (COBOL 85 ANSI STANDARD requirement).  The problem with
periods
> > is that you will inadvertentaly end up terminating everything, and they
may not
> > be what you intend.  And I guarantee you will get all mucked up if you
go
> > mixing these with IFs.
>
> I've seen you say that a few times.  I have an environment where I have to
use
> periods because I don't know for sure what my pre-compiler will stick in
for my
> IDMS code.  (I also feel comfortable with full stop periods within
paragraphs).
> But there is no way I am going to give up my scope terminators.
>
> So far, I haven't come across any problems by using scope terminators in
an
> environment where everybody uses periods.
>

If you (and everyone who maintains your programs) knows and understands the
differences between CONTINUE and NEXT SENTENCE, then you really should NEVER
have any problems "mixing" scope-terminators and periods.  The only
problem(s) that I have ever seen or heard of - are from people who think the
two are identical - or don't understand their differences.

In the next Standard, there are EXIT PARAGRAPH and EXIT SECTION statements.
In some ways, I wish that "we" had also added "EXIT SENTENCE" (as synonymous
with Next Sentence) and EXIT STATEMENT (similar - but not always identical
to CONTINUE).  Maybe that would have convinced all COBOL programmers that
they need to understand the difference between a sentence and a statement -
and then the scope-terminator vs period argument could "die" a well deserved
death <G>.
```

###### ↳ ↳ ↳ Re: Periods and Scope-terminators - again (was: IGYPS2112-E message after WRITE

_(thread depth: 6)_

- **From:** "Rick Smith" <ricksmith@aiservices.com>
- **Date:** 2000-12-29T11:57:28-05:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<92ifn7$2kl2$1@news.hitter.net>`
- **References:** `<91odm0$sql$1@slb7.atl.mindspring.net> <20001222231219.03963.00006052@ng-ct1.aol.com> <3A49FB13.269D2DD3@brazee.net> <92da66$fj2$1@slb7.atl.mindspring.net> <92em29$7ua$1@sshuraac-i-1.production.compuserve.com>`

```
The use of NEXT SENTENCE has been made archaic
in the draft COBOL standard (CD 1.10, Appendix E.1, item 3).

"3) NEXT SENTENCE phrase in the IF and SEARCH statements.
This phrase can be confusing, especially when specified in a
delimited-scope statement. It is a common belief among users
that control is transferred to a position after the scope delimiter
rather than to a separator period that follows it somewhere. In
addition, it is a common source of errors, especially for
maintenance programmers who inadvertently insert a period
somewhere before the actual terminating separator period.
The CONTINUE statement and scope delimiters can be used
to accomplish the same functionality and such constructs are
clearer and less prone to error."

NEXT SENTENCE may become obsolete in the following
standard, 2006(?) or later, and may no longer be part of the
COBOL language in any subsequent standard, 2011(?) or later.
------------------
Rick Smith

Russell Styles wrote in message
<92em29$7ua$1@sshuraac-i-1.production.compuserve.com>...

[...]
```

###### ↳ ↳ ↳ Re: Periods and Scope-terminators - again (was: IGYPS2112-E

_(thread depth: 8)_

- **From:** rjones1005@aol.com (RJones1005)
- **Date:** 2000-12-30T15:06:11+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<20001230100611.23172.00006692@ng-fv1.aol.com>`
- **References:** `<B672B640.1E6%jeffbaynard@home.com>`

```
The program I rewrote, about 5000 physical lines in the procedure division
before precompiling had scores of NEXT SENTENCE and 76 GO TOs (yes, I counted
them). It seems to me that NEXT SENTENCE  is simply a variation on GO TO.  But
beyond that NEXT SENTENCE works with periods and CONTINUE works with
scope-terminators.  

Taking one of our famous page long (multi-IF imbedded) IF statements all
terminated by a single period... A NEXT SENTENCE would pass execution to the
next executible statement immediately after that single period.  OTOH, if this
page-long IF were written with scope-terminators and CONTINUEs, a CONTINUE
would pass execution to the next executible statement immediately following the
scope-terminator of the imbedded IF that the CONTINUE is inside of; NOT to the
end of the entire page-long IF.

Finally, and I cannot emphasize this enough, the scope-terminator construct
SIGNIFICANTLY enhances program maintenance.  Adding, changing, and deleting
code with scope-terminators is magnitudes easier than the old sentence
paradigm.
```

###### ↳ ↳ ↳ Re: Periods and Scope-terminators - again (was: IGYPS2112-E

_(thread depth: 9)_

- **From:** "William M. Klein" <wmklein@ix.netcom.com>
- **Date:** 2000-12-30T11:15:40-06:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<92l585$o1h$1@nntp9.atl.mindspring.net>`
- **References:** `<B672B640.1E6%jeffbaynard@home.com> <20001230100611.23172.00006692@ng-fv1.aol.com>`

```
"RJones1005" <rjones1005@aol.com> wrote in message
news:20001230100611.23172.00006692@ng-fv1.aol.com...
 <snip>
> Taking one of our famous page long (multi-IF imbedded) IF statements all
> terminated by a single period... A NEXT SENTENCE would pass execution to
the
> next executible statement immediately after that single period.  OTOH, if
this
> page-long IF were written with scope-terminators and CONTINUEs, a CONTINUE
> would pass execution to the next executible statement immediately
following the
> scope-terminator of the imbedded IF that the CONTINUE is inside of; NOT to
the
> end of the entire page-long IF.
>

Just so you see some of the confusion (for "real-world programmers") what
you say about CONTINUE is *not* exactly correct.  In practice, it is how it
is used (usually) but the following is perfectly valid code and the CONTINUE
does *not*  "pass execution to the next executible statement immediately
following the scope-terminator ..."

If A = B
   continue
   Read ABC
      At End
           continue
           Display "This will be executed"
    End-Read
    Display "This too will be executed when a = b"
Else
    Continue
    Dipslay "and this will be executed when A does not equal B"
End-if
Display "Nothing will pass execution directly here"
  .

All a CONTINUE statement does is act as a "no-op" and control passes
wherever it would go if there were no statement there.  There is actually a
time when code like this is semi-reasonable, e.g.

  Add 1 to A
     On size Error
         Subtract 2 from B
         Continue
      Not on Size error
         Display "This is part of the ADD not the Subtract"
   End-Add

It is possible to code an END-SUBTRACT statement where the CONTINUE is - but
some people and shops do not like using them with "unconditional"
statements.  If you don't have EITHER a CONTINUE or an END-SUBSTRACT, the
NOT ON SIZE ERROR is "matched" with the wrong verb.  (I would personally
PREFER using END-SUBTRACT, but CONTINUE accomplishes the "same thing" in
this case)
```

```
EQUAL TO

EVALUATE TRUE
   WHEN yadda yada

      dothat
    WHEN yadda yadda

logic clean with IF...ELSE IF...ELSE IF... he/she would not have gotten it
clean with EVALUATE TRUE, either..
```

###### ↳ ↳ ↳ Re: IGYPS2112-E message after WRITE

_(thread depth: 4)_

- **From:** rjones1005@aol.com (RJones1005)
- **Date:** 2000-12-30T14:51:18+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<20001230095118.23172.00006691@ng-fv1.aol.com>`
- **References:** `<3A49FB13.269D2DD3@brazee.net>`

```
>> IMHO don't go mixing scope terminators and periods.  I use scope-terminators
>> exclusively and use periods only at the end of paragraph names and at
…[13 more quoted lines elided]…
>IDMS code.  (I also feel comfortable with full stop periods within
paragraphs).
>But there is no way I am going to give up my scope terminators.
>
>So far, I haven't come across any problems by using scope terminators in
>an
>environment where everybody uses periods.


If you have an IF inside a PERFORM loop, and terminate the IF with a period,
and lets say you terminate the PERFORM with an END-PERFORM, The PERFORM and IF
are both terminated at the period. I learned this the hard way.  With
scope-terminators I can, for example, put IFs inside of EVALUATES inside of
PERFORMS and control the termination of each.  

It became clear to me that scope-terminators aren't just a nice feature, but
necessary for the implementation of in-line PERFORMs, et. al.  BTW I'm using
Microfocus COBOL. IMHO scope-terminators gives the programmer excellent control
for building well structured code.  W/out getting into detail,
scope-terminators was a key COBOL 85 construct that allowed me to "code away"
all the GO TOs with strictly structured code (execution always enters at the
top and always exits at the bottom) while preserving the intent of the old
code.
```

```
ALthough other have pointed out the issue of the period in column 73,
technically an END-WRITE would be required as a WHEN clause requires an
imperative statement and WRITE / INVALID KEY is not imperative while WRITE /
```

##### ↳ ↳ Re: IGYPS2112-E message after WRITE

- **From:** "William M. Klein" <wmklein@ix.netcom.com>
- **Date:** 2000-12-25T22:22:46-06:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<9296gr$qtf$1@nntp9.atl.mindspring.net>`
- **References:** `<3a3f8a10$1001$tfs$mr2ice@news> <6vvb4t4f2f6fs4cqv001q7juk04s678mqq@4ax.com>`

```
Not true.

A period terminates ALL pending conditional statements, so you could have
(for example),

  If A = B
     Read XYZ
        At End
           Call "ABC"
                 On Exception
                    Add 1 to LMN
                        On Size Error
                            Display "The following period will terminate
MULTIPLE conditionals"
         .

NOTE: The ANSI'85 Standard (where END-xxx were introduced) was *REQUIRED* to
keep this rule - for compatibility with the '74 Standard.
```

```
>From: "Jeff Baynard" union27@macconnect.com

>We were informed today that our 'parent' corporation is taking away my 
>beloved ROSCOE editor and replacing it with TSO/ISPF.  Any comments on that?
…[3 more quoted lines elided]…
>Jeff

My sympathies for sure.  I'm a ROSCOE junkie myself.  I also have access to
TSO/ISPF and have found it somewhat acceptable but there are editing functions
I do in ROSCOE that I have been unable to do in ISPF.  An example would be to
change a string on specific lines within specific boundries - a snap in ROSCOE
- still can't do it in ISPF (3.4 function or ELIPSE - see below ).  I also
haven't been able to duplicate the FILL function.  I go into TSO to edit files
that are larger than 256 positions.  I can only access FILEAID thru TSO as well
as QMF and TLMS.  They never turned on the ROSCOE interface for these.

We use Librarian and have ELIPSE in TSO to edit directly in the test library
and browse the production library.  However after saying that LIBCCF (change
control for those not familiar with it) is done in ROSCOE as are all compiles
etc.  I have no idea how to do them in TSO and all our TSO bodies (we have the
choice of ROSCOE or TSO/ISPF) must go into ROSCOE for these functions.  I will
say that file allocation and copying are a bit easier in TSO and there some
other nice features as well.

All in all you'll get used to it after a few choice words here and there. After
all - hubby dearest made the switch a few years ago and survived and he's NOT
one for change :).

Eileen
```

##### ↳ ↳ Re: mainframe editors

- **From:** Howard Brazee <howard@brazee.net>
- **Date:** 2000-12-19T23:54:19-07:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<3A40579B.F47661A6@brazee.net>`
- **References:** `<91p32l0j9s@enews4.newsguy.com> <20001220010030.04515.00001520@ng-cn1.aol.com>`

```
YukonMama wrote:

> My sympathies for sure.  I'm a ROSCOE junkie myself.  I also have access to
> TSO/ISPF and have found it somewhat acceptable but there are editing functions
> I do in ROSCOE that I have been unable to do in ISPF.  An example would be to
> change a string on specific lines within specific boundries - a snap in ROSCOE
> - still can't do it in ISPF (3.4 function or ELIPSE - see below ).

I recommend using the exclude function.  You can also use bounds.

For instance, use line commands to exclude all lines except those which you wish to
change.  Then do the command C ABCD EFGH ALL NX   8 72
(change ABCD to EFGH for every occurrence on non-excluded lines in columns 8-72).


> I also haven't been able to duplicate the FILL function.

It has been 20 years since I have used Roscoe - what does this do?
```

##### ↳ ↳ Re: mainframe editors

- **From:** mike__c@my-deja.com
- **Date:** 2000-12-20T10:48:18+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<91q2ph$ms1$1@nnrp1.deja.com>`
- **References:** `<91p32l0j9s@enews4.newsguy.com> <20001220010030.04515.00001520@ng-cn1.aol.com>`

```
In article <20001220010030.04515.00001520@ng-cn1.aol.com>,
  yukonmama@aol.com (YukonMama) wrote:

> I also haven't been able to duplicate the FILL function.

Don't know if this is what you're looking for (taken from a posting by
JeffRice @ http://mvshelp.com/ubb/Forum7/HTML/000264.html - this
posting also includes a REXX edit macro to fill a given column range
with a given string):

C ALL P'=' 'X' 10

will change all the characters in column 10 to 'X'. For more than one
column the syntax would be:

C ALL P'==' 'XY' 10 11



Sent via Deja.com
http://www.deja.com/
```

##### ↳ ↳ Re: mainframe editors

- **From:** croxbo@my-deja.com
- **Date:** 2000-12-20T23:02:43+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<91rdqf$si5$1@nnrp1.deja.com>`
- **References:** `<91p32l0j9s@enews4.newsguy.com> <20001220010030.04515.00001520@ng-cn1.aol.com>`

```
If you want to change something on certain lines and certain columns
using ISPF, you have several ways:

1) you can exclude the lines you want to change with the exclude
primary command or with the x line command
2) you can mark lines between labels by putting labels on the first and
the last line of the block you want to change. Say you use .f for the
first line and .l for the last line.

Suppose you want to change any character on column 50 to 55 into spaces
you can give the command:

1) c p'=' ' ' all x 50 55
2) c p'=' ' ' .f .l all 50 55

both ways will work. If you don't like it, you can undo things with the
undo command. I worked also with Roscoe. I prefer ISPF a lot!


Sent via Deja.com
http://www.deja.com/
```

#### ↳ Re: mainframe editors

- **From:** Herwig Huener & Josella Simone Playton <webmaster@Josella-Simone-Playton.de>
- **Date:** 2000-12-20T12:22:31+01:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol

- **References:** `<91p32l0j9s@enews4.newsguy.com>`

```
2000-12-20 12:01:00 MET

Jeff Baynard wrote:

> ...

> Or any comments about mainframe (OS390) editors in general..

The subject of mainframe editors raises my blood presure.
Because mainframe working environment is one of
the largest cause of reduction of quality and quantity of
work one can do.

As I often say, we work *for* a mainframe environment,
not *with* it.

As for editors, this type of software is the most individual
interface to the user. Type of education, biography,
frequency of use and availability determine which editor
is best.

In most cases, for larger edition work, an editor on
a desktop computer is by far the best choice. Also, of
course, some sort of network for transporting files to
and from the mainframe. However, although I have my
preferences, I do not recommend a specific editor.

Forcing employees to use a editing environment which
they do not like not only reduces quality and speed of
work. It even has consequences for health. The motivated
programmer defies every impediment to his work.
Unnecessary obstacles have dire effect on motivation
and wellness. Also, using an unfamiliar editor may
cause a programmer to look more frequently from
keyboard to screen and back. This may have ill
effects for the eyes, expecially for older users.
(Standard medical textbook tell details, but reading
that is no fun, I warn you.)

So, if there is a company policy "one editor for
everybody" and "what is good for everybody is good
for you", I deduce that there is no specific interest
in quality of work and no interest in health of employees.
Alternatively, there may be considerable ignorance
in management about how to archieve results.

IMHO the best choice is: For small editing jobs on
the mainframe, use any editor which is there. If that
happens to be your favourite editor, you can of course
use that editor for everything. For all others, a
desktop solution is best.

And, whether mainframe editing or desktop-editing:
Speed is important - I dont see any use in keeping
programmers waiting.

Herwig
```

```
2000-12-21 13:22:31 MET

NA wrote:
>
> ...
…[5 more quoted lines elided]…

Yes? How? I am always willing to learn!
> ...

> In the United States of America, where the legal doctrine is one of
> 'employment at will' and one can daily read of 20-year-tenure employees
> being told, on Friday afternoon at 1530hrs, to clean out their desks, the
> sense is much more one of 'you get what you give'.

Quite so. And that is the reason that 20-year-tenure
employees are mostly seen to fall back into a state
management-is-always-right. No creative objection
anymore - even in our country, where it is not easy
to get rid of such an employee. The result is what
I cannot express in English: "Innere Kï¿½ndigung" and
"Dienst nach Vorschrift". Maybe someone can translate?

Actually, it is the law that an employee is required
to do what he is told to do. Building a wall in the
morning and demolishing it in the afternoon. He is
not required to do what is right. So what you expect
from somebody with limited chances for future
employment?

On the contrary, being asked to do something which
is dangerous for one's health may result in a lawsuit
against the company or even against the responsible
manager personally - if a causal relation between
working conditions and illnesses can be proved
(Which may be difficult in many cases).

BTW, back to the editor: We have, in Germany,
something called "Bildschirmarbeitsplatzverordnung",
a strict law requiring minimal standards of
a workplace with computers. For instance, it is
no more legal to give an employee a CRT with
60 Hz refreshing frequency.

This Bildschirmarbeitsplatzverordnung is the national
manifestation of a Law which applies in all of the
European Union. In the latter, it is required that
a computer shall be fast enough not to keep his
users waiting. In the German Bildschirmarbeitsplatzverordnung
this point has been dropped. Forgotten. Just so.
So, in Germany, it is entirely legal to work with
slow computers and waiting all day that the cursor
moves. The employee is safe if he cannot accomplish
much work by that reason.

He is not safe, however, if he is ambitious enough,
from heart disease.

What do you say to that?

Herwig
```

```
NA wrote:
>

"Loyal Opposition" is the term I was looking for. A
difficult concept: Loyal to whom or what? In the
age of "global players" companies merge and split
and give birth to sub-companies. I don't know
"my company". If I knew, that knowledge is obsolete
next week!

The age of loyality is gone.

As for "Loyal opposition": Wasn't it Henry Ford himself who
remarked: "I respect any of my directors who has a different
opinion than me. Also, I fire him."

A few years ago, I saw a publication where the benefits
of "loyal opposition" had been computed but the math was
not completely outlined and I did not follow it closely.
Sorry I cannot name the paper and its author right now.

Herwig
```

```
case. If (y) is done the result will most likely be (z), for reasons (m),
(n) and (o); if, however, (w) is done then, for reasons (p), (q) and (r)
```

```

Herwig Huener & Josella Simone Playton wrote
>Quite so. And that is the reason that 20-year-tenure
>employees are mostly seen to fall back into a state
…[4 more quoted lines elided]…
>"Dienst nach Vorschrift". Maybe someone can translate?

I'm not getting drawn any further on this subject. As Michael has frequently
quoted "It's the Artist, not the paintbrush." He's right.

However, I WILL respond to your request for translation Herwig...(Your
English, BTW, is generally outstanding...)

"Innere Kuendigung" - I've not come across this, but I deduce as follows:

"Innere" - inside, hidden, internal as in "Innere Einstellung" Your
attitude.
"Kuendigung"  - cancellation, layoff, dismissal.

Therefore "a mentality afraid of dismissal"? However, "Kuendigung" can also
mean quitting or giving up so it could be "given up, don't care"? As you can
see, it isn't easy.

"Dienst nach Vorschrift" is very simple.  Literal translation "Service
according to written commandment"


The English equivalent is "Work to Rule". Do exactly what is required, no
more, no less. This is usually employed as a negotiating tactic during
industrial disputes. It has a negative overtone in that nothing more than
what is absolutely necessary will be done and all time consuming processes
and procedures (which might ordinarily be circumvented) will be followed to
the letter.

Hope this helps.

(All my German is self taught from books, with help from friends, while
living in Germany. I have never had a lesson in German and am not a scholar
in these matters. However, I have no difficulty with conversational German.)

Pete.
```

#### ↳ Re: mainframe editors

- **From:** "Peter E. C. Dashwood" <dashwood@enternet.co.nz>
- **Date:** 2000-12-21T02:55:44+13:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<91qf92$o05$1@hermes.enternet.co.nz>`
- **References:** `<91p32l0j9s@enews4.newsguy.com>`

```

Jeff Baynard wrote in message <91p32l0j9s@enews4.newsguy.com>...
>We were informed today that our 'parent' corporation is taking away my
>beloved ROSCOE editor and replacing it with TSO/ISPF.  Any comments on
that?
>Or any comments about mainframe (OS390) editors in general..
>
>Thanks in advance,
>Jeff

I've worked with both and am inclined to agree with Herwig; use a PC editor.

In the "good old days" we wrote ROSCOE Procedures (ROSPROCS) to automate
tasks like compiling etc.

Inevitably, we had the same thing you are encountering (replacement of
ROSCOE with TSO/ISPF).

Actually, ISPF is very good and the advanced editing features in it make it
very powerful. But best of all you can write and run REXX with it!

All the joy of ROSPROCs but with bells on!

Having worked on PCs since they were invented, I've now become used to that
environment and would prefer to use it for program development and
maintenance. In fact, I can't understand why people still use a mainframe to
develop and debug COBOL code.

On a PC you have a dedicated processor all to yourself and get instant
response ALWAYS, not subject to the vagaries of TSO loadings where response
can vary from sub-second to 20 seconds... How many times in a TSO
environment have you had the response suddenly slow down just when you are
in the middle of a tricky piece of logic? You lose the whole thread of what
you're doing while you wait for the system to respond...

Herwig made some very good points in this thread.

I realise that we usually don't get a choice and must take whatever the
installation standard is, but that doesn't mean the subject can't be
discussed...

The bottom line is Programer Productivity (as Herwig observed) and that is
best served by people editing code with whatever tool they feel most
comfortable with.

Anyway, Jeff, nothing to worry about. Within a few weeks you'll be quite
happy with TSO.
(One thing I found helped during the transition, was to sit down with
someone who knew TSO well and get him to walk through the basic functions
like locating and copying datasets, etc.  It took about 20 minutes to learn
the basics and you can get the rest from the extensive online help.)

Pete.
```

#### ↳ Re: mainframe editors

- **From:** Steve Thompson <sthompson2_@neo.rr.com>
- **Date:** 2000-12-20T14:37:02+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<3A40C3D3.AE4E8805@neo.rr.com>`
- **References:** `<91p32l0j9s@enews4.newsguy.com>`

```
Jeff Baynard wrote:
> 
> We were informed today that our 'parent' corporation is taking away my
…[4 more quoted lines elided]…
> Jeff

I've read the rants about editors in this thread to this point. 
One of the posters believes that MVS stands for Man v. System.

All that aside, I would imagine that your bean counters and
MIS/IT Director have gotten tired of CA.  Let me guess why:  CA
has raised prices yet again, and, there is no real development or
support for ROSCOE.

Now, if you can, and very quietly, find out what the reasoning
is, you may be able to reverse this decision.  How you may ask? 
Well, I use to be a WYLBUR developer.  One of our largest
clients/customers decided to go to an ALL TSO based environment
(for editing and the like).  At that point in time they had 250
concurrent WYLBUR users -- WYLBUR was a single address space
supporting 250 users.  Roscoe is very similar, in that x number
of users run in one Roscoe address space.

Here is the rub:  After migrating 50 users from WYLBUR to
TSO/ISPF w/ CLIST/REXX, the company was looking at having to
upgrade a 3090/600J!  They had run out of page space (getting
address space creation failure messages due to page space
shortages).

Why all this?  Because TSO takes up one address space, and then
each TSU (Time Share User) takes up one address space.  As a
result, IBM makes many of the TSO & ISPF modules RENT for loading
into LPA/ELPA.  Each TSU has to allocate the same data sets
(initial logon/proc), and then allocate all of the data sets
needed for the user (ISPF libraries and the like).

End result is, a HUGE impact in CPU, paging, and C-store
requirements.

Assume if you will that WYLBUR and ROSCOE have the same ratio in
moving from them to TSO in the area of resource requirements
(that is, WYLBUR & ROSCOE have the same savings in resources),
and that you are going to have to change ROSCOE "execs" to REXX
or CLIST.  Let us also assume that you can write applications in
ROSCOE just like you can in WYLBUR, so that you don't have to use
CICS (and you can make direct IDMS calls!).

If you have 50 full time users (programmer types) that switch to
TSO/ISPF, you can expect to need to define 2-4 more PAGE data
sets AND add a new CPU AND add C/E-store to the system to hold
down paging.

Plus, you will have to migrate the applications from ROSCOE to
TSO/ISPF or to CICS.

I'd quietly check to see if all this has been taken into
account.  But be prepared for "we are going to make this
migration anyway."

As for the functions and features you are use to in ROSCOE, the
editing of submitted JCL for resubmit is not available.  SDSF
does not allow you to edit JCL.  You will need to play some games
to capture that file from SDSF and then edit it in another
location and resubmit.

Also, TSO/ISPF SUBMIT would have to be modified to get it to
behave as SUB does for ROSCOE.  So you need to get use to having
a standard JCL member that contains a JOB card (and all the
JES2/3 specific stuff) to insert with JCL you want to submit.

After that, you will have to forgive me, I've forgotten almost
everything I knew about Roscoe, because I was doing WYLBUR
development, and working with TSO/ISPF for years now.
```

###### ↳ ↳ ↳ Re: mainframe editors

- **From:** Howard Brazee <howard@brazee.net>
- **Date:** 2000-12-20T10:50:43-07:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<3A40F172.E7A0E0AB@brazee.net>`
- **References:** `<91p32l0j9s@enews4.newsguy.com> <3A40C3D3.AE4E8805@neo.rr.com> <500C33F371E5D36F.A56EF53F0459915A.E558D0DB43572533@lp.airnews.net>`

```
An editor is a tool (as is a computer language).  When you work in an environment
where you are given a tool, the best thing to do is to learn to use that tool well.

If you are given TSO, learn it and look at its strengths (which are many).  There's
always a trade off, but almost always you can adjust and as productive with the new
tool.

I prefer to learn a tool such as TSO using as much as possible, the defaults and
existing macros.  I dislike it when someone changes default actions of keys in
their terminal emulators or TSO.  That means I do funny things when I use their
keyboard.

But with TSO, I do make the following key changes for all of my sessions:
F12 = RETRIEVE   (some sessions may prefer CRETRIEVE)
F2 = START       (if someone presses F2 to split, this  works about the same)
F9 = SWAP NEXT  (It didn't change function much)

The only key I change in the next 12 is F21= SWAP PREV, to go backwards.

Why?  RETRIEVE is useless unless it is attached to a key.
Switching SPLIT to START allows me more sessions.


Some mainframe people have said that the mouse is our enemy.  I use it for one
thing - defining text to be CTL-V or CTL-C moved around.   It can be a nice saver
this way.  Just a few minutes ago, I cut a column of data names, inserted some
blank lines, pasted it twice, and entered a line:
D       DISPLAY '"
="'                                     '"'.

Then I moved the above line over the pasted columns to display the set of fields.
(line commands M and OO & OO).  Very nice and typo resistant.
```

```
> editor outlook on life.

If I am moving or copying lines, I use CUT and PASTE (or sometimes GET and PUT
which we have at our shop).   In this case I was copying columns and moving them
to different columns.

I also use windows cut and paste when I am in SDSF and pull out a file name which
was expanded using symbolics.  Then I go to ISPF and can view the file without
typing it in.  I cut social security numbers to move to my on-lne application.  I
cut a field from my compile listing, and go to my source and do a X ALL;F ALL
ctl-V  (to paste the field name).

The best thing about editors such as SPF is the exclude command.  It saves me
lots of problems.

I know of a one handed typist who who is right handed, but has the mouse in his
left hand while he types the way he always has, with his right hand!

What I don't understand - but is very popular - is the practice of using the
mouse to use the paste command from a menu or button.  Way too slow when you have
Ctl-V available!
```

```
I just use the VSE/ICCF editor.  The compiler doesnt care.  It can
generate line numbers if you tell it to or just leave them out and
number it at the end.

In article <3A40F172.E7A0E0AB@brazee.net>,
  Howard Brazee <howard@brazee.net> wrote:
> An editor is a tool (as is a computer language).  When you work in an
environment
> where you are given a tool, the best thing to do is to learn to use
that tool well.
>
> If you are given TSO, learn it and look at its strengths (which are
many).  There's
> always a trade off, but almost always you can adjust and as
productive with the new
> tool.
>
> I prefer to learn a tool such as TSO using as much as possible, the
defaults and
> existing macros.  I dislike it when someone changes default actions
of keys in
> their terminal emulators or TSO.  That means I do funny things when I
use their
> keyboard.
>
> But with TSO, I do make the following key changes for all of my
sessions:
> F12 = RETRIEVE   (some sessions may prefer CRETRIEVE)
> F2 = START       (if someone presses F2 to split, this  works about
the same)
> F9 = SWAP NEXT  (It didn't change function much)
>
> The only key I change in the next 12 is F21= SWAP PREV, to go
backwards.
>
> Why?  RETRIEVE is useless unless it is attached to a key.
> Switching SPLIT to START allows me more sessions.
>
> Some mainframe people have said that the mouse is our enemy.  I use
it for one
> thing - defining text to be CTL-V or CTL-C moved around.   It can be
a nice saver
> this way.  Just a few minutes ago, I cut a column of data names,
inserted some
> blank lines, pasted it twice, and entered a line:
> D       DISPLAY '"
> ="'                                     '"'.
>
> Then I moved the above line over the pasted columns to display the
set of fields.
> (line commands M and OO & OO).  Very nice and typo resistant.
>
>


Sent via Deja.com
http://www.deja.com/
```

```
takes you right to the manual that explains the message.
```

```
For all your various comments about ISPF, and Rosco, here is one you might
find a boor, but kept me reading the whole subject here.

The original author of Rosco is the same guy who authored MetaCOBOL, and
many other software products. His name: Steve Wright.  He  had degrees in
Math and Electrical Engineering.  He was the programmer of record of our
first Gross to net program, and I learned C-10 (machine language for the
Univac I) documenting some of his utilities.  I never got to try Rosco, but
would have selected it were it my choice over TSO. However, I taught a lot
of newbees how to make TSO do a lot of things before we began to do much
with on-line programming. Seeing a reference to Exclude brought back "fond"
memories to this old coot.

Warren Simmons
```

##### ↳ ↳ Re: mainframe editors

- **From:** allen@slickedit.com
- **Date:** 2000-12-27T19:10:52+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<92derm$ne3$1@nnrp1.deja.com>`

```
Visual SlickEdit is now available for the OS/390(USS).  It has all the
features of the Windows and Unix version of Visual SlickEdit and
includes ISPF emulation, dataset utilities, and SDSF interface.  It runs
as a USS application and uses X-windows to paint screen at your
workstation (Unix or Windows).  If you are interested in a demo we can
do one over WebEx.

After using cards for 2 years (right-on YukonMama), ISPF for 10, and
then XEDIT for 10 I think that you are almost always going to be most
comfortable with what you learned first.  (Except cards, they weren't
hard to give up (-8.)  Many of the Visual SlickEdit developers still use
SlickEdit emulation key bindings instead of CUA.

If I ever go back to programming I will not go back to ISPF after using
a graphical editor with the functions of SlickEdit.  Sorry for the sales
pitch.

Regards and Happy New Year, Allen.


Sent via Deja.com
http://www.deja.com/
```

```
It is to do with 16-bit co-existence.
Had this problem lots of times in Win 95.
Don't know Win ME yet, but this inelegant solution fixed most cases:
FIRST load another 16-bit application.
We set up WPS.EXE (Windows Process Status) to kick off (minimised) in the
Startup group.
(The R&D guys have now written some little 16-bit thing which has the same
effect but invisible to the user.)
```

```
but not at the end.  I guess the program sees that it is just empty

this?  Thanks.
```

- **From:** "William M. Klein" <wmklein@ix.netcom.com>

```
What compiler and operating system are you using?  It *may* be that defining
your file as "RECORD SEQUENTIAL" in your FD (rather than just "defaulting"
to sequential) will solve your problem.

The other question is, how do you know that the spaces aren't being written?
Do you use a "text editori" to review them - or some other means?  It may be
that they are being written - but you "can't see them".

All of this DOES vary depending on compiler and operating system.
```

- **From:** Howard Brazee <howard@brazee.net>

#### ↳ Re: Writing filler

- **From:** "Jerry P" <jerryp@bisusa.com>
- **Date:** 2000-12-22T01:52:31+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<zty06.3252$LN3.119712@newsread2.prod.itd.earthlink.net>`
- **References:** `<3A416DE6.8FB84BD8@prodigy.net>`

```
It is often the case that:

When reading a text file, if a CR is encountered before the record is
filled, the compiler generates code to space-fill the remainder of
defined input record (this is a COBOL standard). In other words, if
the program asks for 100 bytes and the operating system supplies only
80, the program fills the remaining 20 bytes with blanks.

The compiler, for output, takes advantage of the above rule by simply
not writing trailing blanks. This saves space on the output media. At
least that's the theory.

In your case, you'll have to over-ride this default behavior by some
appropriate mechanism unique to your compiler/operating system. It
could be in the code itself (BLOCK CONTAINS 100 CHARACTERS), another
form of the syntax (ORGANIZATION IS FIXED), or some add-on (ASSIGN TO
MYFILE.TXT[U]). Or something similar.








"Michael Bosco" <mbosco51@prodigy.net> wrote in message
news:3A416DE6.8FB84BD8@prodigy.net...
> Hi.  I am extremely new to cobol.  I am trying to WRITE a record to
a
> text file.  The records must be a fixed length, so there is filler
at
> the end of each record (19 spaces).  When I write the record,
everything
> works fine, except the 19 spaces at the end are never written.  If I
put
> those spaces at the beginning or middle of the record, it works
fine,
> but not at the end.  I guess the program sees that it is just empty
> space with nothing after it, so it just cuts it off.  How can I
prevent
> this?  Thanks.
>
```

<a id="t-65ed1fe523"></a>
## Thread: Odd MOVE question — 25 this month / 26 total

### Odd MOVE question

- **From:** markd@bellsouth.net (md2100)
- **Date:** 2000-12-21T14:57:38+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<3a4214db.1001310828@news1.lig.bellsouth.net>`

```
Given this simple FD & working storage:

      FD  the-file.
      01  the-rec.
          05  field-1      pic 9(9).
          05  field-2      pic X(9).
          05  field-3      pic X.

      working-storage section.
          77  fd-field-name   pic x(20).
          77  result              pic (1024).
          
Is there any way to 'indirectly' reference/MOVE an item? In other
words, something like this:

      accept fd-field-name.  
      move <reference>fd-field-name to result.

Example, if the fd-field-name entered is "field-1", the result in
'result' is the _contents_ of field-1 from the-rec?  What I'm trying
to avoid is a huge EVALUATE that explicitly moves each FD field name
to 'field-value' based on the value of 'fd-field-name', ala:

EVALUATE fd-field-name
    when "field-1" move field-1 to result
    when "field-2" move field-2 to result
    when "field-3" move field-3 to result
     ...ad nauseum...
END-EVALUATE

The program I'm writing needs to support multiple files, some with
hundreds of fields, and some that change so it could get ugly quick.
Being able to move by reference could potentially save thousands of
lines of code. BTW, this will be under MF COBOL and any MF-specific
solutions (ie, non-portable) are fine.  I have to believe someone has
jumped this fence before.

TIA
```

#### ↳ Re: Odd MOVE question

- **From:** "Leif Svalgaard" <leif@leif.org>
- **Date:** 2000-12-21T15:21:50+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<iep06.30016$7V2.389336@typhoon.austin.rr.com>`
- **References:** `<3a4214db.1001310828@news1.lig.bellsouth.net>`

```
No, you cannot do it as you described.
One approximation to what you want could be:

01  rec1.
     02   field-val   pic x(9) occurs 1000 times.

77 field-nbr pic 999.
77 result  pic x(1024).

accept field-nbr
move field-val (field-nbr) to result
```

##### ↳ ↳ Re: Odd MOVE question

- **From:** "Michael Mattias" <michael.mattias@gte.net>
- **Date:** 2000-12-21T18:57:54+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<Sos06.1174$bD3.170805@paloalto-snr1.gtei.net>`
- **References:** `<3a4214db.1001310828@news1.lig.bellsouth.net> <iep06.30016$7V2.389336@typhoon.austin.rr.com>`

```
I guess you "could" build a table of field-names and the associated offsets,
datatypes and sizes, ACCEPT the dataname and then do a lookup, go get the
data and MOVE it. And I do mean, YOU can do it (not me).
```

#### ↳ Re: Odd MOVE question

- **From:** lcccpiasabird@my-deja.com
- **Date:** 2000-12-21T19:47:05+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<91tmnn$m42$1@nnrp1.deja.com>`
- **References:** `<3a4214db.1001310828@news1.lig.bellsouth.net>`

```
In article <3a4214db.1001310828@news1.lig.bellsouth.net>,
  markd@bellsouth.net (md2100) wrote:

we have a file with a key and part of the key is the record type.

the file has 9 different record types we just redefine the the rest of
the record 9 times.  Depending on the record type we know where the
data is.

Try a group moves you have a large field in the record layout.  Then
you define several areas of the same size in working storage.  Then you
can move the entire group depending on a condition.  If you made it all
one big table with sections occupying the same space and redefine it
with an occurs you could use a subscript to move it.


Some compilers
> Given this simple FD & working storage:
>
…[36 more quoted lines elided]…
>
```

```
problem.  The only other viable option is to explicitly code/account

I'm looking for is this:

   77  WS-FLD-NAME  pic 9(20)  value "REC-FLD-1".
   77  WS-RESULT      pic x(80).

   MOVE (reference modifier)WS-FLD-NAME to WS-RESULT.
           or
   MOVE FUNCTION XYZ (WS-FLD-NAME) to WS-RESULT.

and WS-RESULT would contain the actual _contents_ of REC-FLD-1 record
field, not the literal "REC-FLD-1". I suspect I'm looking for a magic
solution that may not exist.
```

###### ↳ ↳ ↳ Re: Odd MOVE question

- **From:** "William M. Klein" <wmklein@ix.netcom.com>
- **Date:** 2000-12-21T20:55:29-06:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<91ufqe$t24$1@slb0.atl.mindspring.net>`
- **References:** `<3a4214db.1001310828@news1.lig.bellsouth.net> <91tmnn$m42$1@nnrp1.deja.com> <3a4270b7.1024827393@news1.lig.bellsouth.net>`

```
The bottom-line answer is that field names are not NORMALLY stored in
"object code" - so knowing  (at run-time) a specified field-name does NOT
let you get at the proper location in storage.

There are TIMES when certain compilers do store data-names (usually for
debugging purposes) - but those are usually "internal-only" interfaces and
won't help.

THEORETICALLY, if your compiler provides a compile-time listing that shows
"offsets" in storage of specified data-names, then you could "process" the
compiler listing to get the offset in storage of what you want (based on the
field-name).  This "processing" could be done once (per compile) and create
a data-set to be read by your actual program.  My guess is that this would
be a WHOLE LOT more trouble than individual EVALUATE statements - but it
could be done (but most vendors do NOT guarantee that their compiler
listings don't change between releases - so you might need to "change" your
processing routine - each time you apply maintenance to your compiler).
```

###### ↳ ↳ ↳ Re: Odd MOVE question

- **From:** riplin@kcbbs.gen.nz
- **Date:** 2000-12-22T09:59:45+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<91v8mf$tfm$1@nnrp1.deja.com>`
- **References:** `<3a4214db.1001310828@news1.lig.bellsouth.net> <91tmnn$m42$1@nnrp1.deja.com> <3a4270b7.1024827393@news1.lig.bellsouth.net>`

```
  markd@bellsouth.net (md2100) wrote:

> I appreciate people's responses, but I guess I didn't describe the
> problem well enough.  For starters, modifying an FD is not an option.
…[11 more quoted lines elided]…
> I'm looking for is this:

> I suspect I'm looking for a magic
> solution that may not exist.

The short answer is no you can't do, in Cobol, what you are asking for.

Are you writing a report writer ? (as distinct from a report generator).

Many years ago I started developing what I called a 'synthetic system'
written in Cobol so that I could easily develop a generalised file
maintenance and report writer that would handle a large part of the
basics for a production system.  This has worked well over the years.

The basic synthetic system is based on a restricted set of FDs that
describe a set of files into which actual data files are forced.  This
gives somewhat inefficient use of record space, but disk drives are
cheap.  For each actual file a dictionary gives the relationship between
the fields, by type and index, and the field name.  A screen layout text
file specifies how the fields for a given file are laid out in the
maintenance program and a script file describes the reports required.

When a new system is required the base can be thrown together very
quickly so that master file data entry can proceed while I design the
rest of the system.  All file maint and reporting is quickly implemented
with text dictionary, screen and report scripts.

When I started retroactively applying the report writer to existing
systems I redesigned it slightly using a file module for each file and
designed a large interface containing enough fields of sufficient size
to cater for every possible layout.  The file module then does a MOVE of
each record field into the interface, thus every record looks the same
to the report writer.  Each file also needs a dictionary to say where in
the interface the data can be found:

Interface:

	01	Interface-Record.
 	    03  IR-Key              PIC X(32).
            03  IR-Flag             PIC X OCCURS 40.
            03  IR-Word             PIC X(4) OCCURS 40.
            03  IR-Value            PIC S9(8)V99 OCCURS 50.
            03  IR-Text             PIC X(40)    OCCURS 50.
            03  IR-Date             PIC 9(6)     OCCURS 20.


Each File-Handler:

        READ file ..

        MOVE DaDa-Key       TO IR-Key
        MOVE DaDa-Replaced  TO IR-Flag(1)
	MOVE DaDa-Unit      TO IR-Word(1)
        MOVE DaDa-Name      TO IR-Text(1)
	MOVE DaDa-Address   TO IR-Text(2)
        .... for every field to somewher in interface

Each Dictionary:

*FILE DADA
REPLACED,F,1
UNITCODE,W,1
NAME,T,1
ADDRESS,T,1

Keep the number of types to a minimum becasue an EVALUATE will be
required for this.

Then the dictionary can be used to determine the type and index with a
simple IF .. ELSE or EVALUATE it can be accessed.  The report writer (if
this is what it is) can handles every file via its file handler in a
consistent way.  The field names can be presented as a list to the user
for selection and/or can be used in a script, such as

*REPORT OVERLIMIT
*FILE DADA
*COMPUTE
TOTALBAL=BALANCE0,E,BALANCE3       (E is sum of)
OVERLIMIT=TOTALBAL,-,CREDIT
*SELECT
CREDIT > 0                   (only print if there is a credit limit)
OVERLIMIT > 0                (only print if balance > credit limit)
*SORT
OVERLIMIT,D		      (sort to descending ie worst first)
*LINE 1
NAME
PHONE
TOTALBAL
CREDIT
LASTPAID
LASTPAYMENT
*ENDREPORT

(This is the sort of thing my report writer does)




Sent via Deja.com
http://www.deja.com/
```

###### ↳ ↳ ↳ Re: Odd MOVE question

- **From:** "Michael Mattias" <michael.mattias@gte.net>
- **Date:** 2000-12-22T13:32:47+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<3KI06.548$tk5.51905@dfiatx1-snr1.gtei.net>`
- **References:** `<3a4214db.1001310828@news1.lig.bellsouth.net> <91tmnn$m42$1@nnrp1.deja.com> <3a4270b7.1024827393@news1.lig.bellsouth.net>`

```
md2100 <markd@bellsouth.net> wrote in message
news:3a4270b7.1024827393@news1.lig.bellsouth.net...
>
> I appreciate people's responses, but I guess I didn't describe the
> problem well enough...

> What I would like to be able to do is directly associate an FD's data
> item _name literal_ to the actual data item's _value_ at run time....


You have described your problem (desire?) more than well enough.

The problem is, once the program is compiled, those datanames do not exist
anymore - they've all been translated into offsets and the approriate
machine instructions used to reflect the PICTURE clause available at COMPILE
time for any operations using those datanames.

Unless you take on the "herculean" task of coding those names, you cannot do
what you want to do.

(Unless, of course, you write a program to parse the source code and
generate all the necessary tables and MOVEs. )
```

#### ↳ Re: Odd MOVE question

- **From:** "Jerry P" <jerryp@bisusa.com>
- **Date:** 2000-12-23T00:31:53+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<ZnS06.4490$k8.158377@newsread1.prod.itd.earthlink.net>`
- **References:** `<3a4214db.1001310828@news1.lig.bellsouth.net>`

```
Here's what we do:

In our case, a user selects a field (to appear on an output report or
to be used in a calculation or have its contents moved to another
field, etc.).

We have a table (actually a text file read into the program)

name
...
Addr1         ACxxxxyyyy
Addr2         ACxxxxyyyy
City             ACxxxxyyyy
....

Where "A" implies alphanumeric (other choices are D=date, 0-9=numeric
decimal places, etc.)
"C" denotes which file (C=Customer), xxxx = offset from beginning of
record to 1st byte of field, and
yyyy=length of field. Sort of a poor-man's data-dictionary.

The user selects the field name(s) to use, say on a report.

This text list is searched once per run to determine the
characteristics of each item in the report. These characteristics are
stored in a table: For example ifteen selected fields, fifteen entries
in the table.

The code, then is:

PERFORM VARYING INDX FROM 1 BY 1
    UNTIL INDX > NUM-ELEMENTS
    MOVE TABLE-BEG(INDX) TO MYBEG
    MOVE TABLE-LEN(INDX) TO MYLEN
    EVALUATE TABLE-TYPE(INDX)
       WHEN 'A' PERFORM MOVE-ALPHA
       WHEN 'N' PERFORM MOVE-NUMBER
       WHEN 'D' PERFORM MOVE-DATE
       END-EVALUATE
    END-PERFORM.

...

MOVE-ALPHA.
      MOVE INPUT-REC(MYBEG:MYLEN) TO PRINT-LINE(NEXT-COL:MYLEN).

MOVE-NUMBER
    is trickier. Ours is somewhat simplified since we deal with only
two types of numbers s9(5)V99 or S9(5).



"md2100" <markd@bellsouth.net> wrote in message
news:3a4214db.1001310828@news1.lig.bellsouth.net...
> Given this simple FD & working storage:
>
…[32 more quoted lines elided]…
> solutions (ie, non-portable) are fine.  I have to believe someone
has
> jumped this fence before.
>
> TIA
>
```

##### ↳ ↳ Re: Odd MOVE question

- **From:** "William M. Klein" <wmklein@ix.netcom.com>
- **Date:** 2000-12-23T13:40:27-06:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<922uvc$6v$1@slb6.atl.mindspring.net>`
- **References:** `<3a4214db.1001310828@news1.lig.bellsouth.net> <20001222225415.03963.00006043@ng-ct1.aol.com>`

```
No, Micro Focus (MERANT) is not unique in supporting "pointers."  Almost all
workstation compilers do now - and they will be included in the next
ANSI/ISO Standard.  HOWEVER, they still won't help take a data-name and
dynamically (at run-time) find the values in that data item.  As stated
earlier, most compilers do NOT store data-names in object code - so there is
no way to find the storage location (at run-time) from a data-name.
```

```
and destination names).  There's a pre-processor available that
implements it.
```

##### ↳ ↳ Re: Odd MOVE question

- **From:** thaneH@softwaresimple.com (Thane Hubbell)
- **Date:** 2000-12-28T04:04:39+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<3a4abacf.83884166@news1.attglobal.net>`
- **References:** `<3a4214db.1001310828@news1.lig.bellsouth.net> <3a465e46.3801360@news1.attglobal.net>`

```
Well, I've exchanged some email and here's the deal.  Thew new
VALIDATE certainly WILL handle this.  Here's the code:


FD The-File.
01 The-rec.
   05  Field-1 Pic 9(9)
       Present When Fd-Field-Name = "FIELD-1" Destination result.
   05  Field-2 Pic X(9)
       Present When Fd-Field-Name = "FIELD-2" Destination result.
   05  Field-3 Pic X 
       Present When Fd-Field-Name = "FIELD-3" Destination result.

Accept Fd-Field-Name
Move Function Upper-case (Fd-Field-Name) to Fd-Field-Name
Validate The-Rec.



Now, in the draft standard you can do this - as the Upper-case
function can be used as an identifier...


 FD The-File.
 01 The-rec.
    05  Field-1 Pic 9(9)
        Present When Function Upper-Case (Fd-Field-Name) = "FIELD-1"
Destination result.
    05  Field-2 Pic X(9)
        Present When Function Upper-Case (Fd-Field-Name) = "FIELD-2"
Destination result.
    05  Field-3 Pic X
        Present When Function Upper-Case (Fd-Field-Name) = "FIELD-3"
Destination result.

This is NOT available in the pre-processor of which I spoke - but the
VALIDATE CAN be used now by using this preprocessor - you can find
more infomation on it at:

http://www.spc-systems.com

(You may have to send an email from there - a cursory look didn't
reveal the pre-processor -- but I have it on good authority that it
exists).


On Sun, 24 Dec 2000 20:37:34 GMT, thaneH@softwaresimple.com (Thane
Hubbell) wrote:

>I think the new COBOL "Validate" can do this.  (Combining valid values
>and destination names).  There's a pre-processor available that
…[45 more quoted lines elided]…
>My personal web site: http://www.geocities.com/Eureka/2006/

---
Try a better search engine:  http://www.google.com
My personal web site: http://www.geocities.com/Eureka/2006/
```

###### ↳ ↳ ↳ Re: Odd MOVE question

- **From:** pknudsen@gw.total-web.net (Paul Knudsen)
- **Date:** 2000-12-30T18:46:17+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<3a502ce0.26740870@news.gw.total-web.net>`
- **References:** `<3a4214db.1001310828@news1.lig.bellsouth.net> <3a465e46.3801360@news1.attglobal.net> <3a4abacf.83884166@news1.attglobal.net> <9M_26.2421$s4.1354@news.indigo.ie> <3a4cb81d.54527930@news.gw.total-web.net> <92if0i$i7i$1@slb1.atl.mindspring.net>`

```
OK, it could be site specific.  I've never been able to find a 31 bit
option in our production assembler.

My main point is that there's no longer any reason to do I-O in
assembler.
On Fri, 29 Dec 2000 10:43:59 -0600, "William M. Klein"
<wmklein@ix.netcom.com> wrote:

>COBOL can "happily" CALL DATA(31) programs - assuming the Assembler is
>expecting them.
>
>NOTE: If this statement doesn't mean anything to you - it is an IBM
>mainframe compiler option available since VS COBOL II.
```

###### ↳ ↳ ↳ Re: Odd MOVE question

_(thread depth: 7)_

- **From:** Binyamin Dissen <postingid@dissensoftware.com>
- **Date:** 2000-12-30T22:32:19+02:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<dihs4tstq23572h7d3ivuq1vffkm3rt9pt@4ax.com>`
- **References:** `<3a4214db.1001310828@news1.lig.bellsouth.net> <3a465e46.3801360@news1.attglobal.net> <3a4abacf.83884166@news1.attglobal.net> <9M_26.2421$s4.1354@news.indigo.ie> <3a4cb81d.54527930@news.gw.total-web.net> <92if0i$i7i$1@slb1.atl.mindspring.net> <3a502ce0.26740870@news.gw.total-web.net>`

```
On Sat, 30 Dec 2000 18:46:17 GMT pknudsen@gw.total-web.net (Paul Knudsen)
wrote:

:>OK, it could be site specific.  I've never been able to find a 31 bit
:>option in our production assembler.

As assembler is coded directly, rather than compiled, there is not concept of
a 31 bit option. The code and interfaces have to be written to handle 31 bit.

There are AMODE and RMODE assembler directives, but all they do is set
indicators in the object deck so that the linkage editor can determine, if not
given explicit AMODE & RMODE instruction, what is the least restrictive
environment required. If the directives are not specified they default to
24/24.

:>My main point is that there's no longer any reason to do I-O in
:>assembler.

Certain I/O can not be done in COBOL, such as when the format/record length of
the files is not known.  

For example, without assembler, how would you handle a case where the RECFM is
FB but the LRECL can be one of 80, 122, 155, 193, etc.?

:>On Fri, 29 Dec 2000 10:43:59 -0600, "William M. Klein"
:><wmklein@ix.netcom.com> wrote:

:>>COBOL can "happily" CALL DATA(31) programs - assuming the Assembler is
:>>expecting them.
>
:>>NOTE: If this statement doesn't mean anything to you - it is an IBM
:>>mainframe compiler option available since VS COBOL II.
```

## Thread: Win2000 + COBLIB legacy woes — 4 msgs

_Topics: [`COBOL's future, legacy, and obsolescence`](topics.md#future)_

### Win2000 + COBLIB legacy woes

- **From:** brendanl79@my-deja.com
- **Date:** 2000-12-21T16:45:58+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<91tc45$cj3$1@nnrp1.deja.com>`

```
Hi all,

We've run our legacy accounting software (RealWorld) for 10 years on a
DOS box, then as a DOS window on a Win95 box. Now we're trying to move
it to a Win2K box. We moved the relevant directory to the box,
attempted to run the program, and got the error message:

"Cobol run time library not installed".

This message perplexes me, because everything appears to be set up
properly:

--The batch file that starts the software includes "SET COBDIR = .",
and the COBLIB.DLE is located in the same directory as the batch file.

--We created a Windows PIF for the batch file that sets the proper
working directory.

--I even tried FORCEDOS.

So, for some reason, the library is not loading properly, although it
is most certainly present and pointed to in the proper manner.

Anyone with experience getting legacy DOS-based COBOL stuff to run on
an NT/2K box, please help!

Brendan LeFebvre
brendanl@iname.com


Sent via Deja.com
http://www.deja.com/
```

#### ↳ Re: Win2000 + COBLIB legacy woes

- **From:** "Gael Wilson" <gael.wilson@merant.com>
- **Date:** 2000-12-22T11:37:17
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<91vi4t$c7l$1@hyperion.mfltd.co.uk>`
- **References:** `<91tc45$cj3$1@nnrp1.deja.com>`

```
Brendan,

>
> "Cobol run time library not installed".
>

I'm surprised that FORCEDOS did not work. However, the alternative is to add
the directory containing the COBLIB.DLL (if your app includes it) to the
Os2LibPath system environment variable. Your app will then run as a 16-bit
OS/2 app rather than a DOS app.
```

#### ↳ Re: Win2000 + COBLIB legacy woes

- **From:** "Liz Young" <nospam@sonic.net>
- **Date:** 2000-12-22T20:48:20+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<o6P06.5849$W76.95668@typhoon.sonic.net>`
- **References:** `<91tc45$cj3$1@nnrp1.deja.com>`

```
Try adding the Cob set statements to the %SystemRoot%\System32\autoexec.nt
file (this and config.nt are read when you launch a 16bit process), and you
may have to append your path statement so the OBJ directory comes first.

rem append search path
set path=f:\dir\obj32;f:\public;f:\public\subpub;%path%
set pathext=.com;.exe;.cmd;.bat

rem set cobol environment
set cobdir=f:\dir\obj32;p:\dp\mf40\exedll;p:\dp\mf40\lbr
set cobcpy=p:\dp\dir\src\dds
set coblib=p:\dp\dir\src\dds
set cobsw=-f0+k3+i1-p1-l6
set vcscfg=p:\dp\dir\src\pvcs
set cobanim_2=animate
set seq=f:\dir\obj32

-Liz
LeeWatleeZZZ@hotmail.com
remove the Z's for reply

<brendanl79@my-deja.com> wrote in message
news:91tc45$cj3$1@nnrp1.deja.com...
> Hi all,
>
…[29 more quoted lines elided]…
> http://www.deja.com/
```

## Thread: IBM Mainframers: VSAM Space Allocation Software — 8 msgs

_Topics: [`Mainframe, z/OS, JCL, CICS`](topics.md#mainframe) · [`VSAM, files, sorting`](topics.md#files)_

### IBM Mainframers: VSAM Space Allocation Software

- **From:** "Michael Mattias" <michael.mattias@gte.net>
- **Date:** 2000-12-21T16:54:57+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<BBq06.1019$DE1.125547@dfiatx1-snr1.gtei.net>`

```
December 21, 2000

About twelve months months ago, I asked here if anyone could suggest a 'VSAM
for Dummies'- type tool to enable a calculation of the space allocations
which should be used during an IDCAMS DEFINE of a VSAM dataset. Thanks to
several people who helped me with this project, that software is now
available.

Version 1.1 of "VSAMSpace" is a single 55K Windows 32-bit (NT/9x/2K)
executable. It does not require any support DLLs, does not read or write to
the system registry or do any other annoying stuff. To run it, you click on
it twice in Windows Explorer. To un-install, you delete the file.

When you click the "Doc" pushbutton, it extracts the doc file to a text file
in the same directory where the executable is and launches NOTEPAD to view
it. (All the math details are in the documentation).

Operation of the software is so simple even a mainframer can handle it.

And, the best thing about this software - at least insofar as I can tell
about this crowd - is that the price is right: free.

If you'd like a copy of this software, just send an e-mail request to
michael.mattias@gte.net with a return e-mail address. I can attach the file
to the email as an EXE or as a ZIP file (about 25K) if you need to get past
a firewall or just feel better about it that way; so let me know if you you
want the software attached as "EXE" or "ZIP."

Regards,
Michael Mattias
Racine WI
michael.mattias@gte.net

PS:I will NOT send the software in response to postings here, nor do I edit
out so-called "spam-traps" from e-mail addresses. If I cannot click 'reply'
or on an address in the text of the mail, it won't happen.
```

```
I imagine that this is due to the amount of support DLLs that would 
have to ship with a COBOL executable.
VB is usually a safe bet to use for Windows based distributions as
the VBRUNxx.DLL is usually installed (at least in most instances that 
I have seen.).  Delphi is another RAD Tool that creates small footprint
applications for distribution.
Maybe someday, we will see a COBOL implementation that does not 
require all the excess baggage of the current distribution requirements.
```

```
No, it's due to the fact that I use PowerBASIC a lot. However, the number of
support DLL's required with PB applications (ZERO) is one of the reasons I
chose PB for Windows-based programming. The approximate 1.4Mb run-time, the
requirement to register all the ActiveX DLL's, and the need for VB to have
its DLL's (which of course, are not pure DLLs) in a directory (folder) where
it wants it and nowhere else were big reasons I avoided Microsoft Visual
BASIC like the plague.
```

#### ↳ Re: link error

- **From:** "Paulo Vieira" <pvieira@emporsoft.pt>
- **Date:** 2000-12-22T10:43:04
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<91vb87$otg$1@venus.telepac.pt>`
- **References:** `<20001221140109.03957.00005553@ng-ct1.aol.com>`

```
Most of the time I get this error, is because I have a window running the
program and am trying to compile it on another. The OS locks the executable
whenever it is loaded, thefore preventing the compiler from deleting it. The
solution, of course, is to terminate the runing unit before compiling.
Sometimes it isn't enough; for instance, if runing the program caused a
serious error on KERNEL32.DLL, the runtime system is unable to unload the
program from memory and the only solution is to reboot.

Season's greetings
Paulo Vieira, Emporsoft
```

## Thread: clearing the screen with Fujitsu — 2 msgs
