### clearing the screen with Fujitsu

- **From:** "Minora" <Minora@bigfoot.com>
- **Date:** 2000-12-21T22:19:18+02:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<3a4265e3.0@news1.mweb.co.za>`

```
Hi
Here is another newbie question. How do I clear the display (Fujitsu v3).
I am running win98SE.

After downloading and reading their manual's I am still stumped. In Micro
Focus personal Cobol I use this code "DISPLAY SPACES UPON CRT" and the
display is cleared. This code is also executed in Fujitsu but it just opens
another display window called "screen" and clears it. (the other windows is
the console that displays my menu).

Here is what I tried:
1) write a "perform n times" routine to display say 80 space on the console
it works, but the menu is displayed at the bottom of the console window.
2) Placed the following code in the special-names paragraph "console is
crt". Now only one windows is opened "screen". But this creates a new
problem now each new line is displayed on the previous line. So after the
menu is displayed only the last line show on the "screen" window and the
cursor for the accept statement is flashing at left of this last line. It
looks like this:
"0  5) EXITT A REPORT OF TRANSACTIONS TO DATE" (The cursor is flashing in
the 0 at the beginning of the line. Please see my code below.)
What am I missing as this code works perfectly in MF?

Here is my code:

 DATA DIVISION.
 FILE SECTION.
 WORKING-STORAGE SECTION.
 01 MENU-OP.
     05 CHOICE                   PIC 9   VALUE 0.
 PROCEDURE DIVISION.
     PERFORM MAIN-MENU UNTIL CHOICE = 5
     STOP RUN.
*
 MAIN-MENU SECTION.
     DISPLAY SPACES UPON CRT
     DISPLAY '          **--    MAIN MENU    --**'
     DISPLAY SPACE.
     DISPLAY '   PLEASE MAKE A CHOICE (VALID RANGE 1 - 4)'
     DISPLAY '   ----------------------------------------'
     DISPLAY SPACE
     DISPLAY '   1.) ENTER INCOME'
     DISPLAY '   2.) ENTER A TRANSACTION'
     DISPLAY '   3.) DISPLAY SUMMARY REPORT'
     DISPLAY '   4.) PRINT A REPORT OF TRANSACTIONS TO DATE'
     DISPLAY '   5.) EXIT'
     DISPLAY SPACE
     ACCEPT CHOICE

Thanks
Minora
```

#### ↳ Re: clearing the screen with Fujitsu

- **From:** "donald tees" <donald@willmack.com>
- **Date:** 2000-12-21T17:36:57-05:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<91u0h2$ka3$1@news.igs.net>`
- **References:** `<3a4265e3.0@news1.mweb.co.za>`

```
There are TWO display screens in Fujitsu, which can be a bit confusing.
I use one as an operators console, and the other as a "screen". Common
display statements go on one, and Screen section stuff goes on the other.
I think you are specifying the wrong one.  Try DISPLAY SPACE AT
LINE 1 COLUMN 1, and I think you will get the correct screen to blank. You
night also check the word CONSOLE as opposed to CRT.  There are ways
to set which of the two are used in the SPECIAL NAMES section. (I am using
GUI, and only use the console/screen for debugging).  Back when using
screens, I always used a SCREEN SECTION, which will also work.

Minora wrote in message <3a4265e3.0@news1.mweb.co.za>...
>Hi
>Here is another newbie question. How do I clear the display (Fujitsu v3).
…[51 more quoted lines elided]…
>
```

On Fri, 22 Dec 2000 02:44:19, deek40@aol.com (Deek40) wrote:

> I typed in the code out of Teach Yourself Cobol in 24 hours chapter #4 Screen
> I\O .  When i run the program it runs great, how would i modify the code so it
> stores what you type into the data entry feilds?
> 

<snip program>

After the "accept data-entry-screen" the fields in working storage 
(screen-items) will contain the data entered.

You will have to define a file (a select statement and an FD) with 
fields in the data record that will be used to store the data. You 
have to open the file as ouput, move the working storage data fields 
to the FD's record fields, write the record to the file and then close
the file.
```

## Thread: help: adding to an indexed file problem — 4 msgs

_Topics: [`VSAM, files, sorting`](topics.md#files) · [`Help requests and how-to`](topics.md#help)_

### help: adding to an indexed file problem

- **From:** goble@gtech (David. E. Goble)
- **Date:** 2000-12-22T09:52:13+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** alt.cobol,comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<3a4218c1.379813@news.adelaide.on.net>`

```
Hi all;

Iam using Microfocus personnal Cobol.

I have created a program to create an indexed file from a sequential
file. It has one record.
   
       FILE-CONTROL.
           SELECT f200-members-file
               ASSIGN TO DISK "data/starters/members.dat"
               ORGANIZATION IS LINE SEQUENTIAL
               ACCESS IS SEQUENTIAL
               FILE STATUS IS w120-file-status.
           SELECT f100-members-file
               ASSIGN TO DISK "data/members.dat"
               ORGANIZATION IS INDEXED
               ACCESS IS RANDOM
               RECORD KEY IS f110-memb-licNo
               ALTERNATE RECORD KEY IS f120-memb-name
               FILE STATUS IS w120-file-status.
       DATA DIVISION.
      ***************
       FILE SECTION.
      *-------------
       FD  f100-members-file
           LABEL RECORDS ARE STANDARD
           RECORD CONTAINS 196 CHARACTERS
           DATA RECORD IS f100-members-rec.

key pic x(07)
name 
	first pic x(14)
	surname pic x(14)

So the indexed file has

temparyChristopher              Surname

I wrote another program to add to the index file. It asks the user for
a first name and surname, then...

    OPEN I-O f100-members-file.
...
           READ f100-members-file
               KEY IS f120-memb-name
               INVALID KEY
                   PERFORM 2100-GET-MORE-DETAILTS
                   PERFORM 2200-WRITE-MEMBER
                   PERFORM 2300-ANYMORE-MEMBERS
               NOT INVALID KEY
                   STRING err1 f110-memb-licNo w120-file-status
                           DELIMITED BY SIZE
                       INTO w990-display-message
                   END-STRING
                   PERFORM 2900-ERROR
           END-READ.

But when I enter the name "Christopher Surname" and trace the program,
it assumes that  the new key is "         " (ie spaces) and rightly or
wrongly assumes that the new record is not invalid!

This behaviour is that of the "with duplicates". I want behaviour of
without duplicates.

Is there a way to use an alternate key without duplicates???
--Regards       David. E. Goble
             goble [AT] kin.net.au
          http://www.kin.net.au/goble
Po Box 648 Kingscote, Kangaroo Island, SA 5223
```

#### ↳ Re: help: adding to an indexed file problem

- **From:** "Peter E. C. Dashwood" <dashwood@enternet.co.nz>
- **Date:** 2000-12-28T01:50:05+13:00
- **Newsgroups:** alt.cobol,comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<92cpvh$ksh$1@hermes.enternet.co.nz>`
- **References:** `<3a4218c1.379813@news.adelaide.on.net>`

```
In  a previous response to David's message I wrote:

======================   Start quote from previous response ================

"The answer is also simple, David.

There has to be a logic error. (Or maybe a definition changed between the
version you are running and the version which created the file...)

The fact that the primary key has spaces in it has no bearing on it. You
have correctly defined the Alternate key to be the "Key of Reference".

This apparently exists on the file, but the system is sure that it
doesn't...

Check that the single record on the test file has the correct information in
the Alternate key field. It is not one byte out, or something similar. You
will get an INVALID KEY on READ if the record is not found. It won't be
found if the key on the file doesn't match the key in the program."

==================  End Quote from previous response ================

(I wrote this before receiving the file...spooky isn't it <G>)

Examination of the file with a Hex editor reveals that the defined alternate
key is 13 bytes and the program has defined 14.

Problem solved. An easy error which most of us have made at some time. Be
warned!

Pete.
```

##### ↳ ↳ Re: help: adding to an indexed file problem

```
David,

Allow me to refresh your memory... (I resent the implication that I
fabricated this...)

On the 25th I posted to this NewsGroup, in response to your request for
help.
(We agree on that.)

In that post I suggested (among other things) that you check the key on the
file against the key in the program.

Here's the quote:
================    start quote from 25 December  ===================
"The fact that the primary key has spaces in it has no bearing on it. You
have correctly defined the Alternate key to be the "Key of Reference".

This apparently exists on the file, but the system is sure that it
doesn't...

Check that the single record on the test file has the correct information in
the Alternate key field. It is not one byte out, or something similar. You
will get an INVALID KEY on READ if the record is not found. It won't be
found if the key on the file doesn't match the key in the program."

==============   End Quote from 25th December ===================

The next thing that happened (and you seem to have overlooked it...) was
that you sent Barry Steinholtz a copy of the source code and the file, and
also copied me.

That was on the 27th December. TWO DAYS AFTER the post containing the
prediction above.

I checked the file, found that it was indeed ONE BYTE OUT as I had
predicted, and mailed you privately a complete summary of the problem with a
screenshot from the Hex editor, showing the exact field in error, on the
28th. To jog your memory, here is the message:

========= Quote from private mail to David A. Goble on 28th
December:==========

"David,

The solution to your problem, along with some tips which might be helpful,
are attached.

Good luck with your COBOL.

Pete Dashwood."

======End Quote from private mail to David A. Goble on 28th
December:==========
Attached was the screenshot described above.

My post to the NewsGroup on the 28th was to advise anyone else to avoid the
same problem. The reference to it being "spooky" was because the key was act
ually ONE BYTE out, as I had predicted 3 Days BEFORE! (It could've been ANY
number of bytes out; it was the fact that it was ONE that I described as
"spooky".)

So there was NO tampering with dates on Linux boxes or anything else.
(Anyway, my ISP would be responsible for that, not me). It was just years of
experience predicting a possible source of error that could result in the
problem you described. And actually getting it right on the button.

Pete.

## Thread: Mainframe to WEB — 7 msgs

_Topics: [`Mainframe, z/OS, JCL, CICS`](topics.md#mainframe) · [`Web, XML, modern integration`](topics.md#web)_

### Mainframe to WEB

- **From:** "Brad Prothero" <brad.prothero@clarica.com>
- **Date:** 2000-12-22T11:51:52-06:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<MxM06.2$t6.1204@news.corpcomm.net>`

```
We have an IBM mainframe that our production code is residing. We want to
port a small subset to the PC to allow Web access to some of the
functionality. The problem that we are running into is how should we deal
with the data in EBCDIC form on the PC. We will be using Fujitsu version 5
compiler on the PC. They have a alphabet clause that can identify EBCDIC but
I have not gotten that to work correctly. I have not tried to use this on a
file but it says that it will work.

The problem that I have is in our working storage, we have 88 levels that
have "'5A' thru '59'". To be able to use this on the PC, we will need to
change this. Has anybody run into this problem before? Is there another
solution other than changing every line where this happens?

We are discussing how to architect this: pass data via MQSeries and do
calculations on the server or pass a request via MQSeries, do the
calculations on the Mainframe, then pass back the results and format on the
server.

Any help would be appreciated.
Brad Prothero
Clarica Life Insurance
Fargo, ND
```

#### ↳ Re: Mainframe to WEB

- **From:** barfly_bob@my-deja.com

Bob

deal
> with the data in EBCDIC form on the PC. We will be using Fujitsu
version 5
> compiler on the PC. They have a alphabet clause that can identify
EBCDIC but
> I have not gotten that to work correctly. I have not tried to use this
on a
> file but it says that it will work.
>
> The problem that I have is in our working storage, we have 88 levels
that
> have "'5A' thru '59'". To be able to use this on the PC, we will need
to
> change this. Has anybody run into this problem before? Is there
another
> solution other than changing every line where this happens?
>
> We are discussing how to architect this: pass data via MQSeries and do
> calculations on the server or pass a request via MQSeries, do the
> calculations on the Mainframe, then pass back the results and format
on the
> server.

#### ↳ Re: Mainframe to WEB

- **From:** Support@ScreenIO.com (Kevin J. Hansen)
- **Date:** 2000-12-22T18:48:53+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<3a43a138.83820207@news>`
- **References:** `<MxM06.2$t6.1204@news.corpcomm.net>`

```
On Fri, 22 Dec 2000 11:51:52 -0600, "Brad Prothero"
<brad.prothero@clarica.com> wrote:

>We have an IBM mainframe that our production code is residing. We want to
>port a small subset to the PC to allow Web access to some of the
…[9 more quoted lines elided]…
>solution other than changing every line where this happens?
===============
Hi, Brad,

We handled this in our old ScreenIO product on-the-fly by inspecting a
field that we knew always contained "Y" or "N" to determine whether
the rest of the screen data was ASCII or EBCDIC and then just doing a
conversion of the blocks of data.

The situation in that case was that programmers on the PC could set a
compiler option that worked in EBCDIC ratiher than ASCII, which was
nice for running against mainframe data files.  CA-Realia provided
this facility (we had several customers that used it, which is why we
provided the capability in ScreenIO), and Merant may also - I just
don't recall.

It sounds as though Fujitsu's equivalent isn't working for you, but
that would indeed be the easiest approach.  If that doesn't work I
suppose you could investigate a different compiler.

Other than your 88-level items, it is not a difficult issue, but when
I hit that remark I knew you'd need to handle this at the compiler
level - it's not something you can do yourself.

Kevin

Norcom - COBOL Programming Tools
GUI ScreenIO - A Windows UI for COBOL
http://www.screenio.com
```

<a id="t-fb55d2ed29"></a>
## Thread: Merant (Microfocus), Unix, "Scan Directory" (x"91") — 3 this month / 4 total

_Topics: [`Compilers and vendors`](topics.md#compilers)_

### Merant (Microfocus), Unix, "Scan Directory" (x"91")

- **From:** karthur@primal.com
- **Date:** 2000-12-23T04:05:30+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<9218a8$e42$1@nnrp1.deja.com>`

```
Hi...

Microfocus cobol compilers used to provide an x"91" call that would
return directory information back to the calling program.  It was
subfunction 69 of the x"91" call-by-number routine.  Returns what
a "dir" command does, i.e. program names, types, sizes, date/time, etc.

On current unix versions of Merant cobol products, they no longer
support most x"91" functions.  That's okay.  They offer call-by-name
routines that return the "current" directory, and whether or not a file
EXISTS, but there doesn't seem to be an equivalent to the above.

Any suggestions?  Some call-by-name routine I'm missing?  Some easy
interface to the unix shell (ls command)?

What I'm trying to do is port a program to unix that does the
equivalent of a DOS "dir" command with wildcards, (e.g. "dir RU*.*").
Some equivalent "ls" functionality is fine.  Program needs to look for
a varying number of files with a particular prefix.

Thanks for your help!

Kevin Arthur


Sent via Deja.com
http://www.deja.com/
```

#### ↳ Re: Merant (Microfocus), Unix, "Scan Directory" (x"91")

- **From:** "William Wood" <beavis27@earthlink.net>
- **Date:** 2000-12-23T20:48:03+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<7c816.10958$G4.448115@newsread2.prod.itd.earthlink.net>`
- **References:** `<9218a8$e42$1@nnrp1.deja.com>`

```
We have some code that does this and it does use the 'ls' command to do it.
We format what we are looking for in a WS variable and do a system call
sending the results of the list to a file that we can then read.  For
example:

01  WS-UNIX-CMD.
    05  FILLER                    PIC XXX VALUE "ls".
    05  WS-LS-ARGS        PIC X(20).
    05  FILLER                    PIC X(28) VALUE z" > /tmp/lsfile 2>
/dev/null".

You move your list arguments into WS-LS-ARGS and make a system call

CALL "SYSTEM" USING WS-UNIX-CMD.

Then open the /tmp/lsfile file and read in the results of the list.  It's
ugly but it works.
```

##### ↳ ↳ Re: Merant (Microfocus), Unix, "Scan Directory" (x"91")

- **From:** karthur@primal.com
- **Date:** 2000-12-29T00:18:00+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<92gl7j$7u2$1@nnrp1.deja.com>`
- **References:** `<9218a8$e42$1@nnrp1.deja.com> <7c816.10958$G4.448115@newsread2.prod.itd.earthlink.net>`

```
In article <7c816.10958$G4.448115@newsread2.prod.itd.earthlink.net>,
"William Wood" <beavis27@earthlink.net> wrote:

> We have some code that does this and it does use the 'ls' command to
do it.
> We format what we are looking for in a WS variable and do a system
call
> sending the results of the list to a file that we can then read.  For
> example:
... .... .....

Thank you!  As you might imagine, I was hoping for a more elegant
solution, but hey, like you said - it gets the job done!

Craig:

The best place to get an inexpensive compiler or to learn how to write
COBOL code is to buy Thane Hubbell's book, "Teach Yourself COBOL In 24
Hours!"

The book only costs about $20.00 US$ and includes the compiler at no
additional charge.

It is not only a great book, but also incudes 16 and 32 bit versions
of the Fujitsu COBOL compiler.  The ISBN number of Thane's book is:

0-672-31453-3

You can buy the book on-line at:

http://www.chapters.ca
http://www.indigo.ca
http://www.hasting.com
http://www.bookpool.com
http://www.barnesandnoble.com
http://www.amazon.com




Bob Wolfe, flexus
When replying by e-mail, make sure that you correct the e-mail address.

The COBOL FAQ has moved.  To view the most recent version, please check out the
web version at:

  http://www.cobolreport.com/faqs/cobolfaq.htm

If you have comments, corrects, deletions, or additions, please send private
email to:

    wmklein <at> ix.netcom.com

The following is Appendix B.5 - Changes to create Version 3.01

 o Recorded new location of the FAQ
 o Updated some old (bad) web links
 o Added some new COBOL books (particularly those written or contributed to - by
frequent comp.lang.cobol submitters).
 o Added information about LegacyJ (PERCobol) and changed the company name from
"Synkronix" to "LegacyJ".
 o Updated information for changes in product and company names and addresses
where available
 o Updated the URLs for downloading the draft of the next COBOL Standard and
CobCy
 o Started the Samples/Example Section
 o Tried to get rid of most specific references to Windows/NT, Windows/95,
Windows/98, and Windows/2000.
 o Added links to Xinotech
 o Added information on Norcom and GUI ScreenIO
 o Added (back) information on Wang
 o Added (back) information on the Tiny-COBOL ('74 Standard) project

## Thread: Net Express 3.1 - Customize — 1 this month / 6 total

##### ↳ ↳ Re: Net Express 3.1 - Customize

- **From:** auto73594@hushmail.com (Aleph3)
- **Date:** 2000-12-25T12:03:39+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<t4edqv7p2na0@news.supernews.com>`
- **References:** `<8sjgin$7pv$1@news.inet.tele.dk> <39ed52ba.1532593@hyperion>`

```
In article <39ed52ba.1532593@hyperion>, Mike.Wilkin@merant.com (Mike Wilkin) wrote:
>On Wed, 18 Oct 2000 08:39:15 +0200, "Fernando Kvistgaard" <fek@lr.dk>
>wrote:
…[22 more quoted lines elided]…
>UK

Long time has passed since the promised date.
If you are not afraid to tweak the registry, the solution is very simple:

REGEDIT4

[HKEY_USERS\.DEFAULT\Software\Micro Focus\NetExpress\3.1\IDE\Ide]
"Recent File List"=dword:00000005
"Recent App List"=dword:00000006


The surest method is to run "regedit" from the Run menu
open the above mentioned place
right click on the right pane
select new DWORD
rename  into Recent App List
and modify into the value you wish.

Otherwise, for Win98 users, copy the above code into a text document
you must have a blank line at the end.
give the text .reg extension
dblclick it
I am not sure about other version of WINDOWS registry location, but if you are 
familiar with registry manipulation, you can adapt the reg file accordingly.

Luck

Ilan
```

Hi All;

Is there a better way to do this;

run thru all possible combinations of a set of 6 numbers, in the most
efficent way.

My program seems to work when I step thru it with Microfocus personal
Cobol, but when I try to run to cursor or run it, my microfocus stops
responding.

Iam running microfocus on a 486dx266 with 20MBs?

The code below should 
	run thru all possible combinations,
	read the indexed file,
		if the combination is NOT there,
		then write the combination to the new file.

       IDENTIFICATION DIVISION.
      *************************
       PROGRAM-ID. salotton.
      * make lotto index file
       AUTHOR. David. E. Goble.
       INSTALLATION. Gtech_Computing.
       DATE-WRITTEN. 01/01/2001.
       DATE-COMPILED.
       SECURITY. Gtech_Computing, free to distribute.
       ENVIRONMENT DIVISION.
      **********************
       CONFIGURATION SECTION.
      *----------------------
       SOURCE-COMPUTER. 486DX2-66.
       OBJECT-COMPUTER. 386SX-33.
       INPUT-OUTPUT SECTION.
      *---------------------

           SELECT f200-lotto-file
               ASSIGN TO DISK "data/nosout.seq"
               ORGANIZATION IS LINE SEQUENTIAL
               ACCESS IS SEQUENTIAL
               FILE STATUS IS w120-file-status.
           SELECT f100-lotto-file
               ASSIGN TO DISK "data/salotton.ind"
               ORGANIZATION IS INDEXED
               ACCESS IS RANDOM
               RECORD KEY IS f130-numbers
               ALTERNATE RECORD KEY IS f140-no-of-times-drawn
               FILE STATUS IS w120-file-status.

           RECORD CONTAINS 20 CHARACTERS

               10 f231-lowest                  Pic 9(02).

               10 f233-3                       Pic 9(02).
               10 f234-4                       Pic 9(02).
               10 f235-5                       Pic 9(02).
               10 f236-highest                 Pic 9(02).
               10 f237-sup1                    Pic 9(02).
               10 f238-sup2                    Pic 9(02).

           05 f330-numbers.
               10 f331-lowest                  Pic 9(02).
               10 f332-2                       Pic 9(02).
               10 f333-3                       Pic 9(02).
               10 f334-4                       Pic 9(02).
               10 f335-5                       Pic 9(02).
               10 f336-highest                 Pic 9(02).
               10 f337-sup1                    Pic 9(02).
               10 f338-sup2                    Pic 9(02).
           05 f340-no-of-times-drawn           Pic 9(04).
       WORKING-STORAGE SECTION.
      *------------------------
       01 w100-program-switches.
           05 w110-end-of-file                 Pic x.
               88 w111-eof                     value 'y'.
           05 w120-file-status                 Pic x(02).
           05 w320-temp                        Pic 9(02).
       01 w400-temp-array.
           05 w420-no OCCURS 6 TIMES
                         INDEXED BY w420-index Pic 9(02).
       PROCEDURE DIVISION.
      ********************
       0000-MAIN-MODULE.
      *=================
           SORT f300-sort-file
               ON ASCENDING KEY
                   f331-lowest
                   f332-2
                   f333-3
                   f334-4
                   f335-5
                   f336-highest
               INPUT PROCEDURE 1000-BEFORE-SORT
               GIVING f200-lotto-file.
           STOP RUN.
       1000-BEFORE-SORT.
      *=================
           OPEN INPUT f100-lotto-file.
           MOVE "n" TO w110-end-of-file.
           PERFORM VARYING w420-no(6) FROM 45 BY -6
                   UNTIL w420-no(6)<=1
               PERFORM VARYING w420-no(5) FROM 44 BY -5
                       UNTIL w420-no(5)<=1
                   PERFORM VARYING w420-no(4) FROM 43 BY -4
                           UNTIL w420-no(4)<=1
                       PERFORM VARYING w420-no(3)
                               FROM 42 BY -3
                                   UNTIL w420-no(3)<=1
                           PERFORM VARYING w420-no(2)
                                   FROM 41 BY -2
                                       UNTIL w420-no(2)<=1
                               PERFORM VARYING w420-no(1)
                                   FROM 40 BY -1
                                       UNTIL w420-no(1)<=1
                                   PERFORM 1100-SORT-NUMBERS
                                   READ f100-lotto-file
                                       INVALID KEY
                                           RELEASE f300-sort-rec
                                   END-READ
                               END-PERFORM
                           END-PERFORM
                       END-PERFORM
                  END-PERFORM
               END-PERFORM
           END-PERFORM.
           CLOSE f100-lotto-file.
       1100-SORT-NUMBERS.
      *==================
           SORT w420-no ASCENDING.
           MOVE w420-no(1) TO f331-lowest
           MOVE w420-no(2) TO f332-2
           MOVE w420-no(3) TO f333-3
           MOVE w420-no(4) TO f334-4
           MOVE w420-no(5) TO f335-5
           MOVE w420-no(6) TO f336-highest.

#### ↳ Re: help: program works when I step thru but not while run to cursor

- **From:** dxmixxer@netdirect.net (Douglas Miller)
- **Date:** 2000-12-26T18:49:53+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** alt.cobol,comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<3a48ea56$0$1503$7ea90a65@news.netdirect.net>`
- **References:** `<3a487f61.23076342@news.adelaide.on.net>`

```
In article <3a487f61.23076342@news.adelaide.on.net>, goble@gtech wrote:
>Hi All;
>
…[7 more quoted lines elided]…
>responding.

I'm not surprised: the number of combinations of n things taken r at a time is 
given by C(n, r) = n! / ((n - r)! * r!). C(45, 6) = 8,145,060. That's a lot of 
combinations to evaluate. And due to some bugs in the program, you're 
generating a few more than that, while failing to generate others that should 
be.

The innermost loop of your nested PERFORMs is being executed some nine million 
times -- and that innermost loop is performing a SORT, *and* reading from a 
file. Soooooo.... you've written a program that's performing nine million 
SORTs, eight million WRITEs, and nine million READs; is it any wonder that it 
appears to stop responding? I'm sure it's still running, but it's gonna take 
some time to finish. 

How much time? Well, let's try some rough estimates. Due to the nature of the 
program, most of the reads will be for records that are not present in the 
file, so you won't get much benefit from disk caching. Figure the 17 million 
logical I/Os to result in half as many (8.5 million) physical I/Os. And 
they'll all be *random* I/Os, too, very few sequential track-to-track disk 
seeks here. Assuming a 10ms seek time and 6ms latency, you're looking at about 
38 hours to do all that physical I/O.

And then there are the nine million SORTs, too. If each one takes only 10 
milliseconds, that adds another 90,000 seconds, or 25 hours.

Add in the PERFORMs, and the logical I/Os, and just off the top of my head, 
I'd guess you're looking at a minimum of three solid days for this program to 
complete.

There is a *much* simpler algorithm for doing this (it should be much faster 
too) without the SORTs or the READs. As I suspect this is a homework problem, 
though, I won't describe the algorithm, but rather give you some hints toward 
discovering it.

1. My assertion that an algorithm exists, in which the sort is unnecessary, is 
itself a huge hint toward discovering it. Think about how you could rewrite 
your PERFORM statements so that the numbers are guaranteed to be always in 
ascending sequence.

2. My assertion that an algorithm exists, in which reading an indexed file is 
unnecessary, likewise is itself a huge hint toward discovering it. The logical 
consequence of this assertion is that an algorithm exists which will generate 
each combination exactly once, removing the need to check each generated 
combination to see if has been generated before. Your program unnecessarily 
evaluates both (45, 44, 39, 42, 41, 35) and (45, 44, 35, 42, 41, 39), for 
example. An algorithm which generates only one of these permutations is 
superior to one which generates both, and then eliminates the duplicate.

3. I referred to some bugs your program contains. An understanding of these 
bug may help guide you to the discovery of a better algorithm: Although the 
purpose of the program is clearly to generate lottery numbers, it produces 
some permutations which could not possibly be lottery numbers, for example 
(39, 39, 39, 39, 39, 39) or (45, 44, 39, 40, 39, 40). The structure of your 
PERFORM statements shows that you have attempted to avoid this situation, but 
a closer look will show clearly that this code misses the mark. Specifically, 
the six loops will generate these sets of numbers:
45, 39, 33, 27, 21, 15, 9, 3
44, 39, 34, 29, 24, 19, 14, 9, 5
43, 39, 35, 31, 27, 23, 19, 15, 11, 7, 3
42, 39, 36, 33, 30, 27, 24, 21, 18, 15, 12, 9, 6, 3
41, 39, 37, 35, 33, 31, 29, 27, 25, 23, 21, 19, 17, 15, 13, 11, 9, 7, 5, 3, 1
40, 39, 38, 37, 36, 35, 34, 33, 32, ...
There is considerable overlap between these sets. Look for a better method of 
avoiding overlap.

4. Another bug resulting from the incorrect structuring of the PERFORM 
statements is the program's failure to generate certain correct combinations. 
For example, since 40 and 38 each appear *only* in the sixth series, the 
program cannot generate any combination containing both 40 and 38. Likewise, 
since 42, 40, and 36 are contained only in two sequences, the fourth and 
sixth, no combination containing all three will ever be generated. Look for an 
algorithm that guarantees that every possible combination will be generated.


>
>Iam running microfocus on a 486dx266 with 20MBs?
…[154 more quoted lines elided]…
>Po Box 648 Kingscote, Kangaroo Island, SA 5223
```

I know creating all possible combinations does not need a sort or a
file. The File is a results archieve file of some three years of lotto
draws.

My idea is to run thru all possible combination sets, rejecting those
sets that have already been drawn. However this will still leave a lot
of sets to pick from. As you pointed out, there are C(n, r) = n! / ((n
- r)! * r!). C(45, 6) = 8,145,060 sets. Removing the sets that have
already been drawn 52 games a year for 3 years = 156. This still

ideas. Then again, I think I have figured it out...

for(z=1;z<POSSIBLES+1;++z)
 for(y=z+1;y<POSSIBLES+1;++y)
  for(x=y+1;x<POSSIBLES+1;++x)
   for(w=x+1;w<POSSIBLES+1;++w)
    for(v=w+1;v<POSSIBLES+1;++v)
     for(u=v+1;u<POSSIBLES+1;++u)
	printf("%d %d %d %d %d %d\n",z,y,x,w,v,u);

Sorry for the C code, but it is was easier and quicker to write and
debug C code than Cobol. Esp; on an old workhorse like this 486...:>

## Thread: How to View a Cobol File in Windows — 5 msgs

_Topics: [`Help requests and how-to`](topics.md#help)_

### How to View a Cobol File in Windows

- **From:** Carlos Lages <clages@attglobal.net>
- **Date:** 2000-12-26T17:46:29-02:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<3A48F595.AE37C689@attglobal.net>`

```
Hi, People
I Would like  to generate  a TXT (Could Be A Report ) file  using
Fujtisu  COBOL and/or MicroFocus after that  View this TXT File  and/or
Print  or Save IT.

Does anybody Knows how to do that , Or which Software Can I Use ?

 By the way   POWERForm (Fujitsu) Dont do that.
Cristal Reports Do that but Not using a Complex  Report, And I have to
Design
all the forms again and Create several Formulas .

The Main Ideia is Use all the Ready report Program changing the
Destination to a File instead Printer.

Thanks in Advance

Carlos Lages
From Rio de Janeiro
```

#### ↳ Re: How to View a Cobol File in Windows

- **From:** "William M. Klein" <wmklein@ix.netcom.com>
- **Date:** 2000-12-26T14:34:49-06:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<92avd8$77$1@nntp9.atl.mindspring.net>`
- **References:** `<3A48F595.AE37C689@attglobal.net>`

```
Specify that the ORGANIZATION of the output file (which can have a .txt
extension) is LINE SEQUENTIAL (not RECORD SEQUENTIAL - or just SEQUENTIAL).
This should create a "file" that any old Windows text program will let you
read.

There are several different ways to specify "line sequential" output files
in both Fujitsu and Micro Focus.  Therefore, check your documentation for
which method works best for you. (Let us know if you have trouble finding
them.  We would need to know which compiler, which release, and where you
have already looked in your documentation.)
```

#### ↳ Re: How to View a Cobol File in Windows

- **From:** "donald tees" <donald@willmack.com>
- **Date:** 2000-12-26T18:08:09-05:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<92bcm5$ose$1@news.igs.net>`
- **References:** `<3A48F595.AE37C689@attglobal.net>`

```
Formprint by Flexus will do exactly what you want.

<a id="t-c8c767427e"></a>
## Thread: Keyboard-Problem with MF 4.0 and Win95 — 3 this month / 5 total

### Keyboard-Problem with MF 4.0 and Win95

- **From:** Frank Pohlmann <Frank.Pohlmann@baeurer.de>
- **Date:** 2000-12-28T12:05:20+01:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<3A4B1E70.44F0E0C6@baeurer.de>`

```
I have a problem with the keyboard on Win95/Win98 and MF WB 4.0.32.
I use "decimal point is comma". The regular Comma works fine, but the
Comma in the Num-block provides a point instead of a comma. Not just in
numeric fields, in PIC X fields too.

#### ↳ Re: Keyboard-Problem with MF 4.0 and Win95

- **From:** SBrueggemann@gmx.net (Sven Brueggemann)
- **Date:** 2000-12-30T00:10:48+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<3a4d2232.1148559395@news.btx.dtag.de>`
- **References:** `<3A4B1E70.44F0E0C6@baeurer.de>`

```
Frank Pohlmann <Frank.Pohlmann@baeurer.de> schrieb:

Hello Frank,

>I have a problem with the keyboard on Win95/Win98 and MF WB 4.0.32.
>I use "decimal point is comma". The regular Comma works fine, but the
>Comma in the Num-block provides a point instead of a comma.

With WB 4.x there were several keyboard problems, especially with
Win98. MF fixed (or better: worked around) them one by one with the
following NetExpress versions. In NetExpress 3.1 there is only one
left: exactly the one you have described.

You can read the details in Microsofts Knowledgebase, and since it is
a Windows bug, you shouldn't expect a fix by Merant. You shouldn't
expect a fix by Microsoft either, since they don't think it is that
important as it really is.

If you use your apps for internal purposes there are several tools
available that provide the keyboard mapping means you need to get your
comma working. If you have to support customers, good look to you. You
can either talk them into an other operating system or make them
install one of these mapping tools. There simply is no satisfiying
solution.

Best regards

Sven
```

```

============
Hi, Terry,

API calls that do this kind of stuff.  We didn't pursue it at the time

Kevin
Norcom - COBOL Programming Tools
GUI ScreenIO - A Windows UI for COBOL
http://www.screenio.com
```

#### ↳ Re: Get file size in Realia?

- **From:** "Jerry P" <jerryp@bisusa.com>
- **Date:** 2000-12-28T22:56:58+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<_yP26.35348$3B5.1392512@newsread2.prod.itd.earthlink.net>`
- **References:** `<3A4B8316.8BC6623F@arkansas.net>`

```
We did that once before and, while the code is no longer available,
here's how we did it.

1. Run the Realia stand-alone utility that displays the ISAM file
header. Print the screen.

2. Use a hex editor to prowl around in the first record of the ISAM
file. Find the bytes that contain the values from the printout in
which you are interested (i.e., record length). Note the displacement
of the bytes of interest from the beginning of the record.

3. Define the ISAM file as [B] with a 2K record. Open as input, read
the first record. Close the file. This gets you the ISAM header
record.

Use the discovered displacements - such as for the bytes containing
the record size - in your production program.


"Terry Grider" <tgrider@arkansas.net> wrote in message

##### ↳ ↳ Re: Get file size in Realia?

- **From:** "Oscar T. Grouch" <dustbin@home.com>
- **Date:** 2000-12-30T05:08:35+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<n5e36.46274$59.13209352@news3.rdc1.on.home.com>`
- **References:** `<3A4B8316.8BC6623F@arkansas.net> <3A4D3892.FE85086E@bellsouth.net>`

```
You might be able to get a byte count using DOS_LSEEK twice, once with
SEEK-FROM-START set to TRUE and again with you set SEEK-FROM-END to TRUE and
set SEEK-OFFSET to 0. I'd have to test it to be sure but I don't have Realia
installed, just an old manual. You probably have to use DOS_FILE_OPEN to get
the necessary file handle.

The Win32 API will return this information in the nFileSizeLow field ot the
WIN32_FIND_DATA structure when you use FindFirstFile() or FindNextFile(). If
the file is larger than 4GB then you need to use both nFileSizeLow and
nFileSizeHigh. I ain't never called a Win32 API from Realia though...

#### ↳ Re: NetExpress Character Application default color

- **From:** "Judson McClendon" <judmc@bellsouth.net>

- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol

"David Begley" <dbegley@houston.rr.com> wrote:
> Is there anyway to set the default colors (background & foreground) for a
> character application in NetExpress?
…[3 more quoted lines elided]…
> is difficult to read.

Actually, I believe the colors are brown on black, a default color
combination that could only have been selected by someone with the
ergonomic sense of a potato.  I'm sure they were inspired by the
vast number of text editors, word processors and terminal emulators
that uses that default. ;-)  No doubt, MF has failed to remedy the
gaff because so many users have come to love that illegible combo.

To correct the situation you need to do two things:

    1. Using ADISCF change the default colors to white on black.
       (Don't despair, if you're particularly clever, you should
        be able to figure out how to do it in a week or less.)

    2. In your AUTOEXEC.BAT file set the environment variable:

        set cobsw=+s5  (plus whatever other switches you may be using)

You see, the environment variable must be present so the executable
will listen to what you have already told it in ADISCTRL.  Whoever
built this nonsense into the system was determined.  What provokes
me is not that this is overly onerous, just that it is unbelievably
stupid, and should have been corrected before the first customer saw
the product.
```

#### ↳ Re: NetExpress Character Application default color

- **From:** "Russell Styles" <RWSTYLES01@CS.COM>
- **Date:** 2000-12-29T17:52:43-05:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<92j4ma$20e$1@sshuraaa-i-1.production.compuserve.com>`
- **References:** `<YzN26.39021$wX2.680333@typhoon.austin.rr.com>`

```

"David Begley" <dbegley@houston.rr.com> wrote in message
news:YzN26.39021$wX2.680333@typhoon.austin.rr.com...
> Is there anyway to set the default colors (background &
foreground) for a
> character application in NetExpress?
>
> When the old application ran under DOS, it defaulted to white
on black.
> When compiled under NetExpress 3.0, the default is red on black
and the text
> is difficult to read.
>
>
>
>
You do it the same way it worked in 16 bit runtime.

    To set system (default) attribute:

77 SET-ATTR                     PIC X COMP-X VALUE 7.
77 THE-ATTR                     PIC X.
77 ATTR-ON-OFF              PIC X COMP-X VALUE 16.
77 ATTR-ON                        PIC X COMP-X VALUE ZERO.
77 ATTR-OFF                    PIC X COMP-X VALUE 1.

CALL X"A7" USING SET-ATTR THE-ATTR.            *> SET THE ATTR
CALL X"A7" USING ATTR-ON-OFF ATTR-ON.      *> INSURE THAT IT IS
BEING USED.

    Above assumes attribute is being defined as a hex value.
Make THE-ATTR comp-x
if you prefer decimal values.

    Above assumes int/gnt.  Probably works with EXE/DLL, but I
can not swear so.

    Above information is in NETX 3.1 help file.  Should be in
3.0.
```

##### ↳ ↳ Re: NetExpress Character Application default color

- **From:** "Russell Styles" <RWSTYLES01@CS.COM>
- **Date:** 2000-12-30T00:39:18-05:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<92jt04$c9$1@sshuraac-i-1.production.compuserve.com>`
- **References:** `<YzN26.39021$wX2.680333@typhoon.austin.rr.com> <92j4ma$20e$1@sshuraaa-i-1.production.compuserve.com>`

```
    The suggeston below also assumes (I think!) that you are
using ADIS, ie

    I have no idea if this works with "plain" displays.

## Thread: How to print a printfile in Windows — 2 msgs

_Topics: [`Help requests and how-to`](topics.md#help)_

### How to print a printfile in Windows

- **From:** "Fernando Kvistgaard" <fek@lr.dk>
- **Date:** 2000-12-29T13:09:41+01:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<da%26.58$dR2.2691@news.get2net.dk>`

```
I'm working with NetExpress 3.1 and Flexus Cobol ForPrint.

When I make print document I kan send it direct to the printer or to a file
if the printer is defined to print to a PRN-file.

I'm thinking to make listbox where I read all my PRN-files and from my Cobol
program to print them out  or delete them. My problem now is how to print
the files. I think this kan be done with a sort of ActiveX which I could
call from Cobol with the file name as a parameter, or may be this could be
done with an API call to winspool.drv?

Is there somebody who could help with this.

Thanks

Fernando
```

#### ↳ Re: How to print a printfile in Windows

- **From:** thaneH@softwaresimple.com (Thane Hubbell)
- **Date:** 2000-12-29T12:31:08+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<3a4c82cd.35214533@news1.attglobal.net>`
- **References:** `<da%26.58$dR2.2691@news.get2net.dk>`

```
You can use a form print call to find the "names" of the printers -
then using that name use a CBL_COPY_FILE call from NetExpress to
"copy" the file to that printer.  One important thing to remember is
that you must have saved the print file as it was sent to the SAME
printer driver that you will be printing it on.  Printer specific
information is in the saved file.

On Fri, 29 Dec 2000 13:09:41 +0100, "Fernando Kvistgaard" <fek@lr.dk>
wrote:

>I'm working with NetExpress 3.1 and Flexus Cobol ForPrint.
>
…[15 more quoted lines elided]…
>

---
Try a better search engine:  http://www.google.com
My personal web site: http://www.geocities.com/Eureka/2006/

## Thread: Fujitsu COBOL 4.0 using ODBC — 4 msgs

_Topics: [`Compilers and vendors`](topics.md#compilers) · [`Databases and SQL`](topics.md#databases)_

### Fujitsu COBOL 4.0 using ODBC

- **From:** tcladner@aol.com (TCLadner)
- **Date:** 2000-12-29T15:56:52+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<20001229105652.05840.00000325@ng-cu1.aol.com>`

```
I'm trying to make the switch from Micro Focus DOS COBOL to Fujitsu COBOL 4.0. 
I ran the sample10 ODBC program and it seems to work okay.  The sample reads an
ODBC data source that points to an ACCESS97 database that contains one table. 
The ODBC administrator allows the user to point to that specific *.MDB file (in
the example it's stock.mdb).  I need to read from an Advantage Database Server
(product of Extended Systems) table (ADT extension).  The problem is that the
Advantage supplied ODBC driver allows the user to point to a directory
containing all the tables.  I would like to see an example showing how Fujitsu
COBOL identifies and reads from a specific table in the directory.

Any help would be appreciated.

Thanks,

Tommy Ladner
```

#### ↳ Re: Fujitsu COBOL 4.0 using ODBC

- **From:** "Brad Prothero" <brad.prothero@clarica.com>
- **Date:** 2000-12-29T13:23:34-06:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<Qx536.27$t6.3780@news.corpcomm.net>`
- **References:** `<20001229105652.05840.00000325@ng-cu1.aol.com>`

```
We had dBase tables in one of our apps and all we did was set up the driver
to the correct directory, then treat the different files as tables.

In the sample, there is one table named stock (I do not have sample 10, I am
going off sample 12). Since the Access ODBC driver points to the file,
anywhere in the program it references "STOCK", it is referring to the table
"STOCK" in the file STOCK.MDB and not just the file. So all you have to do
is put the filename that you want to access in where "STOCK" is in the SQL
statements and then adjust the field names to correspond to your field
names.

I am sorry that I do not have any code but I can help with specifics if you
cannot get this working.
```

#### ↳ Re: Fujitsu COBOL 4.0 using ODBC

- **From:** "Peter E. C. Dashwood" <dashwood@enternet.co.nz>
- **Date:** 2000-12-30T12:10:27+13:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<92j83u$vjj$1@hermes.enternet.co.nz>`
- **References:** `<20001229105652.05840.00000325@ng-cu1.aol.com>`

```
Tommy,

There are 2 ways you can access Databases using Fujitsu.

You can use the DataBase control provided with PowerCOBOL or you can use
embedded SQL from within COBOL97 or PowerCOBOL.

If you are using the DataBase control you must specify the data source and
it behaves very much like Visual Basic using MicroSoft's DAO (Data Access
Objects).

If you are using embedded SQL you can specify the table you want through
SQL.
(This is not Fujitsu dependant, it works across any RDB platform)

After successfully connecting to the database (you can do this with an SQL
CONNECT or you can use the RTE (Run Time Environment) file (Cobol85.cbr)),
you should specify the required table using SQL. There are 2 ways to  do
this:

1. Qualify the column name by prefixing the table name to it. Like this:

     table1.column1

2. Specify the table in the SQL "FROM" statement. (I would recommend this as
it makes less "clutter" when your SQL gets complex).

     SELECT  column1, column2, column3
           INTO   :column1, :column2, :column3
        FROM  table1
     WHERE  column2 = "hello"

(Note you must use an SQL DECLARE for the host variables before you can
reference them in an INTO. They are prefixed with a colon, when referenced
within SQL, but just as a normal COBOL dataname outside the SQL (no colon).
So, after the above statement you would find the contents of column1 on
table1, for the row where column2  = "hello", in the dataname "column1".
(Similarly for column2 and column3) You can then reference "column1" as a
COBOL dataname and manipulate it.

You can "join" tables by assigning a correlation variable to replace the
table name. It's like a "shorthand" qualifier.

              FROM table1 x, table2 y

"x" and "y" can now be used to reference the appropriate tables....

              WHERE x.col1 = y.col1

would match the "col1" fields on table1 and table2.

You can see from the above there are a number of options for  specifying
tables.

If you need more, mail me privately and I'll send a complete tutorial.

Pete.

TCLadner wrote in message <20001229105652.05840.00000325@ng-cu1.aol.com>...

```

<a id="t-9dee916dbb"></a>
## Thread: mainframe editors continued — 1 msgs

_Topics: [`Mainframe, z/OS, JCL, CICS`](topics.md#mainframe)_

### mainframe editors continued

- **From:** Herwig Huener & Josella Simone Playton <webmaster@Josella-Simone-Playton.de>
- **Date:** 2000-12-31T11:45:32+01:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<3A4F0E4C.406D5356@Josella-Simone-Playton.de>`

```
2000-12-31 11:44:55 MET

Once upon a time there was a piano-player. He was employed at a large
company where he played the piano most skillfully. It was a special,
probrietary piano, with many special keys in special places for many
special functions. Because of this skill he had, he was paid a fine
salary.

One day the company decided that all employed piano-players had to
change to another instrument, a violin. A violin, they said, is much
cheaper because it is essentially only a box of wood, and it should be
more easy to play a violin because there are only four strings attached
to it. So, in the context of global competition, it would be cheaper,
they said, to hire cheaper violin-players. The existing staff of
piano-players just had to aquire the new skills, they said, as we all
have to learn continuously.

The piano-player now learned to play the violin. Although he had been a
brilliant piano-player in his days, as a violin-player, he was only
mediocre. In fact, listening to him was rather horrible, far
exceeding, for instance, the secret joys of listening to someone
playing the bagpipe.

In principle, he could have changed to playing an open-source-piano
which
he would have mastered easily - the idea of aranging the keys in
ascending order had crossed his own mind in his old piano-days - but the
company said that he would not be allowed to do so. The
open-source-piano, they said, has not been manufactured by Microsoft,
and its architecture was too simple to impress customers and competitors
alike. No - a violin is the instrument of choice, and what is good for
everybody is good also for the old piano-player.

Because of his mediocre violin-playing, the piano-player was sacked. As
a violin-player, you will never amount to very much, he was told, and
also, he was told, in a booming economy, he would easily find a new
job, such as ice-cream selling or re-tuning old pianos in such
companies which did not make the transition from the age of the piano
to the age of the violin.

What is the morale of this story?

-- Never build up skills related to probrietary tools only.

-- If you use open-source-tools, never tell your boss: He will be
   more impressed if you get results with clumsy probrietary tools.

-- Bagpipe-playing is still worse than everything else combined.

(c) Herwig Huener
```

---

## Thread: Survey : : Are you having computer dreams at night? — 1 msgs

### Survey : : Are you having computer dreams at night?

- **From:** rr@dreamgate.com_remove_to_e (rr)

Are you having computer dreams?

Includes dreams of computers, programming, peripherals, Internet
venues, and anything digital.

Questionnaire Online:
http://www.dreamgate.com/dream/computers/computerdreams.htm




----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Also, you can :
� e-mail them to me, Richard Wilkerson, at rcwilk@dreamgate.com

� drop them off anonymously at   http://www.dreamgate.com/dream/temple

------------------------------------
DETAILS: 

Are you dreaming of problems with your hard disk, getting connected,
the wrong programs coming up, not being able to find the file you
want? Does your computer turn you on, and have you found yourself
mating with a digital partner or cyborg  sex? Has god spoken to you
through your computer in a dream? Has the computer in a dream assisted
you in becoming lucid? 

Just as during the last turn of the century, we shifted from horse and
carriage dreams to cars, trucks and jets, now too we are entering a
new cyber-symbolic era of networking and global interface. What dream
content will remain, what will change? 

This is a joint study by Electric Dreams and DreamGate:
 http://www.dreamgate.com/electric-dreams
